The Scientific Method of Falling Apart

by ememalia

Summary

Dr Agatha Harkness, while one of the most respected researchers in neuroscience, had earned her reputation as tough, demanding and exacting. Those who couldn’t handle her methods didn’t last long, and those who did—well, those were the ones who would thrive in the world of research.

What will happen when her mysterious new PhD student Rio Vidal discovers a breakthrough which undermines Agatha's previous research? And what will transpire between the two when this brings them together to unravel the science behind this groundbreaking discovery?

- or -

what results from a procrastinating neurosci student having agathario brainrot and not knowing what else to do w it

chapter 1

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Agatha walked briskly through the lab building, her heels clicking sharply against the floor. She was late, and she liked it that way. The PhD students she was about to meet, the three who’d been assigned to her this year, would be sitting in the lab common room, fingers fidgeting, heart rates spiking as they waited for her. Good. She wanted them on edge. It was part of the process - the first lesson in survival. Let them stew in nerves for a while. Let them worry. It was an excellent way to see who could handle the heat, who could stand up to the pressure.

Agatha had earned her reputation long ago. They called her The Wicked Witch of Neuro. Only behind her back, of course. She didn’t mind. It was true enough. She was tough, demanding, exacting. Those who couldn’t handle her methods didn’t last long, and those who did? Well, those were the ones who would thrive in the world of research. A world where people didn’t coddle you, didn’t pamper you, and certainly didn’t forgive incompetence. And besides, whatever people wanted to say about her behind her back, they also knew her reputation in academia. The 230 publications she had to her name, the 52 of those which were as primary author. She was good. Very good. And the students she supervised? They always, always received research grants for their next projects in the month after they received their PhD. Well, that is, if they survived through 3 years under Agatha first.

She passed a few research fellows and MSc students as she walked. They all met her eye, then immediately glanced away and hurried past. She didn’t care. She relished it. The students she trained would have to learn to command respect, just as she had. Confidence, unwavering and unapologetic. That’s how you got ahead.

Her outfit was nothing unusual, yet it always made a statement. A crisp white shirt, tucked neatly into high-waisted purple trousers. Her black hair was pulled tightly into a bun at the back of her head, practical yet elegant. But it was the long blue lab coat, billowing behind her as she walked, that made her presence feel almost theatrical. She moved like she belonged in the space, like the lab was hers to command. Her stage. She liked that.

She reached the entrance to the common area and paused for a moment, taking in the sight of the students through the glass door. Agatha had three students this year: Billy, Jennifer, and Alice. She made it a point to familiarize herself with their names and faces from the student list ahead of time, committing each detail to memory. It was a small but satisfying tactic. When she entered the room and called them by name without them uttering a word, it always caught them off guard. The sudden recognition, the feeling of being seen and scrutinised before they’d even spoken, it put her in control from the start. It was a subtle but effective way to assert her dominance and remind them that they were already under her watchful eye.

The three of them were sitting on the worn sofas, their backs ramrod straight, eyes wide with nervous energy. They were right where she wanted them. It was almost too easy. She could feel their collective unease from here. Good. They were scared. They should be.

But then, something caught her attention. There was a fourth student, someone she hadn’t expected. A girl, black-haired, sitting casually to one side of the room. Her legs were crossed, her posture completely relaxed, and she was twirling a pencil between her fingers with an air of boredom, or perhaps quiet amusement. Her lack of anxiety, her easy confidence, intrigued Agatha. She checked the student list in her mind, three students. Billy, Alice, Jennifer. This girl wasn’t supposed to be here. Interesting.

The girl wore black tailored trousers and a white shirt, the sleeves rolled up around her elbows, unbuttoned just a bit too much for someone on their first day, revealing a hint of collarbone and a casualness that didn’t quite belong in this setting. Her dark hair fell softly around her face, framing it with an effortless, almost careless grace. Her makeup was simple but striking. Dark eyes, smoky and sharp, the kind of look that made her seem detached from the conventional expectations of professionalism. There was something about her, a subtle defiance, perhaps, that made Agatha take a second look. She wasn’t trying to impress in the way Agatha would have expected, and that, oddly enough, was what made her so interesting. Agatha made a mental note to figure out what the deal was with this mysterious addition to her cohort.

For now, though, it was time to make her entrance.

Agatha opened the door, the soft click of the handle louder than it had any right to be in the stillness. All four students immediately snapped their heads toward her, eyes wide, like deer caught in headlights.

"Good morning," Agatha said coolly, scanning the room, her gaze deliberate as it flicked over each student, pausing just slightly longer on the black-haired girl. She could already feel the tension thickening. She was good at this. So good at reading people, at assessing them before they even spoke a word.

“I am Dr. Harkness,” she said, her voice cold and measured. She let the words hang in the air for a beat, watching as each student absorbed the weight of her name. Billy looked at her with an almost manic intensity, probably trying to read her. Alice, on the other hand, had the deer-in-headlights look she expected from most first-years. Jennifer seemed poised, but her rigid posture betrayed the anxiety that she was trying to conceal. And then there was the girl in the corner.

Agatha's eyes slid over her. Relaxed, almost too much so, and still with that knowing expression, twirling her pencil between her fingers with an air of confidence. Agatha narrowed her eyes for a fraction of a second before continuing.

“Welcome to the neuroscience PhD programme,” Agatha continued, her voice as harsh as ever. She could see Alice’s shoulders tense, the poor thing probably regretting her decision to come here already. Billy was leaning forward a bit too eagerly, trying to hide the nervous sweat beading on his forehead. Jennifer was trying to maintain control, her hands folded in her lap, but her eyes darted between the others and Agatha, as if waiting for the proverbial shoe to drop.

The black-haired girl, however, didn’t seem to be as rattled. There was something about her, some subtle energy that made Agatha stop and take note. But this wasn’t the time to engage. She would get to her later. For now, the message had to be made clear to all of them.

“I will be your supervisor for the next three years,” Agatha said slowly, giving the words weight, ensuring they registered. She allowed her eyes to move from one student to the next.

“Now, I’m sure you’re familiar with my reputation,” Agatha continued, her voice not changing in the slightest. “But if not, let me make it crystal clear to you. I do not tolerate incompetence.” She took a few deliberate steps toward the group, watching as they reacted. Billy trying to maintain eye contact, but with an almost desperate edge to his stare. Alice was looking at her from beneath her lashes, face pale but attentive. Jennifer was more composed but seemed to shrink under Agatha's steady gaze.

“I am fair,” Agatha said, her tone sharpening slightly, “but my standards are high. I won’t coddle you, I won’t hold your hand and I won’t allow for repeated mistakes. Understand?”

The room was so still now, Agatha could almost hear their hearts pounding in sync. She let the silence stretch on, savouring their discomfort.

"This may sound harsh," she continued, her voice a little colder, as she leaned slightly against the back of a chair, surveying the students before her. “Think what you will, but the world of research is cutthroat. Millions of researchers competing for the same funding, the same grants, the same awards." Her eyes flicked to each of them in turn. "You think that being here means you’re special? No. It means you’ve been given a chance. But chances are fleeting. They disappear when you fail.”

The words hung in the air, heavy with meaning. Agatha could feel the collective breath being held, could see the way Jennifer's knuckles whitened as she gripped the edge of the sofa. Billy’s chest was rising and falling faster now, while Alice remained still, almost too still. Agatha’s eyes finally flicked back to the girl, she was still twirling that pencil. There was something there. A glimmer of an expression. Respect? Admiration? Something like that. It was subtle, perhaps she thought Agatha wouldn’t notice. Her gaze locked on the girl for a moment, a flicker of something passing between them. The girl didn’t flinch. Fascinating.

“The first thing you’ll learn here is that this lab is not a place for weaklings,” Agatha said, her voice firm and unwavering. "You want to make it to the top? Then you’ll need to work harder, think sharper, and fight for every inch. This is not a game."

She paused, her eyes catching the girl’s once more. The pencil twirled faster, and Agatha couldn’t help but feel a little curious. This one would either be an asset or a liability, and she wasn’t sure which yet.

Agatha savoured the moment, a quiet thrill humming beneath her cool exterior. She loved the theatre of it all. The heavy silences, the charged glances, the palpable tension she could almost taste. This first impression was a carefully constructed ritual, a performance she had perfected over the years. It was her stage, and each nervous shift, every hesitant glance from her students, was proof of her control. Her students were on edge. Right where she wanted them.

Well, all except the black-haired girl. She sat there, calm and composed. She wore an infuriating smirk which had been plastered on her face throughout Agatha’s speech. Agatha should be annoyed, but rather than unsettle her, the girl’s defiance was a thrill. A challenge wrapped in quiet rebellion. It excited her, this rare flash of resistance. She would break her soon enough.

"I expect excellence. Anything less, and you’ll find yourself out of your depth." She straightened, her mouth curving into a smirk as she clasped her hands together. “Right, so, you will be either in the lab or analysing data for most of your time until you start to write up your research. Your schedule is up to you. You’re grown-ups, you can manage your own time.’

Agatha’s lips twisted into a sarcastic smile as she let her gaze settle on the black-haired girl, still so infuriatingly relaxed. "But, of course," she began, her tone laced with dry amusement and her hands curling into a dramatic flourish, "when I was doing my PhD, I was spending all my time in the lab. I stayed well past sunset most days, and I assure you, I had little time for... other pursuits.” Her eyes swept over the group, watching as their shoulders tensed further.

Agatha’s gaze flicked back to the girl, who hadn’t moved an inch, still looking at her with that infuriating smirk. She raised an eyebrow. “But, I suppose,” she continued smoothly, her voice rich with sarcasm, “if you’d rather be doing something else, that’s fine.” Agatha paused to snicker loudly, as if she was amused by what she was about to say “I’m sure the world of research will be... very forgiving for that kind of behaviour.” She let the words linger, letting their weight settle over them all.

“The only scheduled time you need to spend here” Agatha continued, her voice steady and cold, “is two sessions per week, about 2 hours each, with me, assisting with my current research, it—”

But then, Jennifer’s hand shot up. Agatha suppressed an annoyed sigh, her gaze hardening as she looked at her. She hated being interrupted. “Yes, Jennifer?” she said coolly, watching the shock ripple through them all as they registered that she already knew their names. She allowed herself a small, smirk. Her tactic had worked beautifully.

“Oh, um, I actually prefer to go by Jen,” Jennifer stammered, clearly thrown by Agatha’s familiarity.

“What was your question, Jennifer?” Agatha replied, her voice icily unyielding. She could see Jennifer falter, her mouth opening and closing as she scrambled to regain her confidence.

“Oh, I just wanted to say…” Jennifer took a shaky breath. “I’ve read your research proposal for your current project…on depression in early life as a risk factor for developing Alzheimer’s. It’s just groundbreaking. Really, it’s incredible.”

Agatha’s mouth twitched as a sharp irritation settled in. There was always one—the inevitable suck-up, the overeager devotee who thought a few compliments would put them in her good graces. They never seemed to understand just how little flattery impressed her.

She took a deliberate step towards them, letting her gaze sweep over the other students. “See what Jennifer did just then?” she said, her voice dripping with sarcasm. “She interrupted me, with no apparent question, just to... suck up. Do not do that.” She levelled her gaze at each of them in turn, pausing on Jennifer, who had gone beet red. “If you have an actual, intellectual question about my research, please, be my guest. But reading the abstract of my paper does not get you any points here. It’s, like, the first thing that comes up if you search my name on the university website.”

Agatha’s gaze swept over the students, landing on the black-haired girl. She noted the subtle lift of her eyebrow, the faint smirk tugging at the corner of her mouth. She looked almost impressed. There was a glint of admiration in her eyes, as if she recognised Agatha’s performance for what it was and, against her better judgment, appreciated it. Good, Agatha thought with a flicker of satisfaction, one that she quickly smothered, If the girl wanted a show, she’d come to the right place. This one might prove to be more intriguing than she’d anticipated.

Agatha flicked her gaze back to Jennifer, who now looked like she wanted the ground to swallow her right then and there. “I do not care that you think my research is groundbreaking,” she said, a hint of amusement tugging at her lips. “I know it’s groundbreaking. Everything I do is groundbreaking.”

With flourish of her long lab coat, she began to strut out the door, calling ‘Come. Follow me.’ Agatha listened with pure delight as they scrambled up behind her, not wanting to fall behind and risk Agatha’s wrath.

As they walked briskly down the corridor, Agatha spoke, her tone cool and unwavering. "As I was saying before I was interrupted” she cast a pointed look at Jennifer, who shrank back slightly, “You will have two sessions per week dedicated to my research. These will either be lectures from me - the lecture hall is upstairs; I’ll see you there for the first one tomorrow - or hands-on research assistance in the lab."

They rounded a corner, and Agatha held the door open as the group started down a flight of stairs. “I’m taking you to the lab now,” she continued, her voice echoing through the stairwell. “It’s where you should be spending most of your time. The lab operates under standard protocols. If, for some reason, you are unsure of these protocols, do not ask me. I’m not here to spoon-feed you information you should already know. Find the handbook and study up if you’ve somehow forgotten your basic lab skills.”

They reached a long hallway lined with doors, and Agatha gestured to a few rooms as they passed. “This is a study space,” she said. “You can use it for data analysis if you need somewhere other than the lab to work. These next rooms contain microscopes, you can bring your slides and study them here if you wish. We have an electron microscope in the main lab, but if you just need a light microscope, these should work fine.”

She led them down a different corridor, pointing out a series of rooms. “Down here, we have neuroimaging machines: two MRIs, two CT scanners, and three EEGs. However-” she added with a wave of her hand, “our lab is home to the largest brain bank for neurodegenerative diseases in all of Europe. So, it’s your choice if you want to use neuroimaging, but personally, I’d recommend post-mortem samples if you don’t want to waste the resource which has just..” she added a flourish of her hand “fallen into your laps.”

She abruptly stopped in her tracks, causing the students behind her to stumble and nearly collide as she turned to face them. Agatha crossed her arms, her gaze sharp. "Can anyone tell me the advantages and disadvantages of post-mortem studies over using clinical evidence?"

A tense silence fell over the group as Billy, Alice, and Jennifer exchanged panicked glances. Agatha’s expression hardened; she was unimpressed. This was bog-standard evaluation. They teach this to 17 year olds in A-level Psychology for god’s sake!

But then, the black-haired girl stepped forward, her voice steady and confident as her smirk grew. “Post-mortem brain donations allow for a more detailed study of brain tissue without the ethical limitations of studying a living patient. You can isolate deeper structures within the brain, and you can use stains to test for chemical markers that can’t be detected through neuroimaging.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow, impressed despite herself, though she opened her mouth to remind the girl that she’d also asked about the disadvantages. But before she could speak, the girl continued.

“—but, the brain is dead,” the girl added, as if reading Agatha’s mind. “Meaning you can’t study activity in real time or see how specific tasks activate different brain areas, which you could with EEGs or fMRIs.”

Agatha felt a small surge of approval. She was about to speak, but then the girl went on, seemingly unfazed by the attention and deep in thought. Agatha could practically see the cogs whirring in her mind “Though, I guess for neurodegeneration research, dementia in particular, it’s neuroanatomy and neurochemistry that matter most. Finding a neurobiological basis for these disorders would likely be genetic, neuroanatomical, or neurochemical. Imaging techniques like MRIs or CTs wouldnt be as effective for that.”

For the first time, Agatha allowed a faint smile to cross her lips. “Precisely,” she said, her voice low but approving. “Well done.”

The girl, rather than showing relief or shrinking back like the others, simply widened her smirk. An expression so confident, so unapologetically bold, that it was almost as if she hadn’t expected nor cared about the praise. The girl’s audacity, her calm self-assurance, sparked something in Agatha, a rare flash of genuine respect. There was intelligence here, yes, but also a boldness, a quiet confidence that she hadn’t encountered in years. This one might be something special, Agatha thought, her intrigue deepening. She’d set out to put her new cohort on edge, to see who would falter, who could withstand the pressure. And already, it was clear, this girl wasn’t just holding her ground, she was thriving under it

Agatha nodded to the black-haired girl, acknowledging her sharp answer, before turning and continuing her strut down the corridor. “At our lab's brain bank,” she began, her voice taking on a matter-of-fact tone, “we collect about six donations a week, give or take. These are individuals with neurodegenerative diseases, mostly Alzheimer’s or Parkinson’s, who choose to donate their brains to research after they die.”

She reached the door to the lab, pushing it open with a flourish. “This,” she said, sweeping her arm to the left, “is the lab.” The space stretched out before them, a vast expanse with rows of workstations, equipment, and research areas that seemed to go on forever. The students stared, wide-eyed with awe. Even the black-haired girl couldn’t entirely suppress a small, appreciative smile at the sight.

Agatha continued, clearly relishing their reaction. “On the right,” she said, gesturing again, “is what we call ‘the room of doom.’” She activated an automatic sliding door, revealing a room filled with freezers on one side and shelves stacked with what appeared to be white buckets.

“Stupid name, really,” Agatha admitted with a scoff. “But it’s where we store all the brain donations.” She shrugged. “When the donations come in, we split the hemispheres. One is fixed in formalin,’ Agatha gestured to the white buckets lining one wall, “this makes it easier to study the neuroanatomy. The other hemisphere is dissected fresh and then frozen.” She gestured to the line of freezers.

Agatha paused for a moment, “Now, I don’t really expect anyone to know this, but—” she eyed them, her gaze particularly sharp on the black-haired girl, “—take a guess. When would you use frozen samples instead of fixed ones? The frozen ones are much more inconvenient. They melt within minutes of coming out of the freezer and start to decompose. So really, they’re just a pain to work with. But why might we still use them?”

She watched as the students exchanged uncertain glances. Her eyes locked on the black-haired girl. Agatha raised an eyebrow, sensing the girl was onto something but hadn’t quite pieced it together yet. She could see the realisation dawning as the girl thought through the possibilities, and Agatha gave her a small nod, silently urging her to speak up.

“Genetic testing,” the girl said after a few seconds.

Agatha’s expression shifted to one of surprise and admiration. She nodded, the smallest smile tugging at her lips. “Yes, very good.”

The black-haired girl began to explain further. “The formalin used to fix the brain limits the DNA you can extract from the cells—”

Before she could continue, Jennifer, unable to resist the urge to jump in, cut her off. “Freezing the brain preserves the genetic material! So, you can use it for genetic testing!” she said, with an overly eager tone, as if she’d just solved the problem herself.

Agatha froze for a moment, shocked at the interruption, and then let out a sharp laugh. She had seen it happen before, one of those students who liked to steal someone else’s thunder, without even understanding the question in the first place. Jennifer had had no idea when Agatha first asked. She just heard the start of the other girl’s answer and ran with it.

The black-haired girl shot Jennifer an incredulous look, her gaze turning into a glare of utter disdain. Agatha gave her a subtle, almost approving glance, amused by the girl's reaction. The girl, for her part, simply smirked, looking between Jennifer and Agatha, almost as if to silently say, Can you believe that just happened?

Agatha smirked back, choosing not to dignify Jennifer’s interruption with a response. She made eye contact with the black-haired girl, her voice dripping with approval as she said, “Excellent. I’m impressed.”

The girl nodded, flashing one last glare at Jennifer as Agatha moved on, her tone shifting to one of business. “Now, take a look around. Choose your workstation, lay out anything you might need for tomorrow. We’re done here for today. I expect to see you in the lab early tomorrow. My lecture starts at 11, but if you want to get a head start on your projects, it would benefit you to get here as early as possible. I want to see your project titles and a rough abstract in the next two weeks. The sooner you get started, the better.”

As the other students wandered off to their chosen workstations, settling in and arranging their materials with a mix of excitement and uncertainty, the black-haired girl lingered behind. She leaned casually against the doorframe of the lab entrance, her smirk still firmly in place, watching Agatha with a sort of bemused defiance.

Agatha raised an eyebrow, her gaze narrowing slightly. "You," she said, pointing a finger directly at the girl, her voice firm.

"Me," she replied, her smirk only widening, her low tone almost mocking.

Agatha tilted her head slightly, her curiosity piqued but irritation bubbling under the surface. “You weren’t on my student list. Who are you?”

"I’m Rio," the girl said with a casual lift of her chin, before performing a playful, exaggerated curtsey, lifting an imaginary skirt with mock elegance.

Agatha scoffed, unfazed by the theatrics. "So what, you don’t have a last name?" she said, emphasizing each syllable as she repeated, "Rio?"

Rio stood up straight from her exaggerated bow and, without missing a beat, replied, "Rio Vidal. And I was transferred from a different PhD supervisor yesterday."

Agatha’s eyebrow arched skeptically. "Transferred, huh? So, what? You changed your mind about your topic last minute? You were in a different specialty and suddenly decided you wanted to dive into neurodegeneration? You should know that I don’t tolerate indecisiveness. It’s a sign of weakness. I want my students to be driven and to know exactly what they want."

Rio’s laughter filled the room, a smooth, confident sound that seemed to irk Agatha. "Trust me when I say there is no one more driven than me, don’t you worry your pretty little head," Rio said with an almost teasing edge.

Agatha’s jaw tightened, feeling a flash of anger surge through her. The girl’s confidence was impressive but she was overstepping her boundaries by a mile. "How dare you—" Agatha began, her voice laced with venom.

"Sorry, Dr. Harkness," Rio interrupted smoothly, her voice dripping with feigned seriousness, though her smirk only deepened. "But genuinely, I’ve wanted to go into neurodegeneration research since I was taking my A-levels. I’m driven. I was under a different neurodegeneration researcher for my project, but my course director, Professor Calderu, swapped me to you. She said my talent would be wasted under any other supervisor."

She shrugged as though it was all no big deal, but Agatha’s eyes narrowed.

Another scoff slipped past Agatha’s lips before she could stop it. "Wow, a little cocky, aren’t we?" she said, crossing her arms over her chest, her eyes studying Rio with growing amusement.

Rio tilted her head slightly, an eyebrow cocked in quiet challenge, but she only shrugged yet again. This air of nonchalance was beginning to really annoy Agatha. "Those were Professor Calderu's exact words. I don’t know what else to tell you."

Agatha couldn’t help but admit, begrudgingly, that the name Professor Lilia Calderu meant something. Lilia had been the neuroscience program director for the BSc, MSc, and PhD programs for the university for over forty years. Agatha had worked alongside Lilia for the better part of two decades, and the woman was a genius. If she believed this girl was truly special... well, Agatha had to at least consider the possibility.

This was starting to get interesting.

chapter 2

Chapter Notes

hi everyone !! decided to post this chapter super soon after the first, I dont think I'll be this quick with future chapters, but I wrote these 2 at the same time and just couldn't wait to post it. hope u enjoyyy :)

See the end of the chapter for more notes

The morning was quiet as Agatha made her way through the chill, her breath visible in the crisp autumn air. She arrived at the lab just as dawn’s golden hues began to reflect off the city, pulling her purple scarf a little closer around her neck, the soft wool a welcome barrier against the cold. Her outfit mirrored yesterday's - high waisted purple trousers and white shirt - but she’d added a white knit sweater over her shirt for extra warmth.

She made her way toward the coffee cart by the entrance, savouring the quiet that came with an early start, when the bustling campus was still asleep.

Agatha slowed, surprised. Rio Vidal was already here, leaning against the cart with a lazy confidence, her hair catching the breeze, hands in her pockets. Agatha’s brow arched.

She had told her students to come in early, but this early? The sun had barely risen. Rio’s presence stirred something beyond mere curiosity; the girl had a talent for the unexpected.

“Dr. Harkness!” Rio called, her smirk lifting as if they were already sharing some private joke.

Her outfit was striking: dark green wide-legged trousers paired with a loose black button-up, rolled up to the elbows, a sleek and effortlessly stylish choice. Agatha noted it suited her exceptionally well, though she couldn't help noticing the shiver in Rio's shoulders. "Morning, Rio. Where’s your coat?” Agatha asked, her voice as brisk as the air. “You’re freezing.” She turned to the barista. “Cappuccino, please.”

Rio scowled. “I left it at home. The tube’s always so hot that I didn’t realise until I got out here.”

Agatha hesitated. She wasn’t one to show any affection, and this one in particular needed a firm hand. But something about Rio’s shivering form softened her resolve. Rio noticed the look and raised an eyebrow, her smirk growing, as if daring Agatha to break character. With a huff, Agatha unwound her scarf and handed it to her.

“As soon as we’re inside, I want that back,” she said, rolling her eyes.

Rio's smirk transformed into an exaggerated look of surprise, her eyes glinting and her hand rising to her chest to clutch imaginary pearls. “Dr. Harkness! Well I’ll be. That seemed almost like… kindness?” She teased as she wrapped the scarf around herself, her shoulders visibly relaxing into its warmth. Agatha scoffed, fixing her with a sharp glare.

“Never. I just don’t want you getting frostbite and losing all your fingers. How would you help me with my research then?”

Rio laughed - a genuine, light laugh that broke through the cold, catching Agatha off guard as the girl flexed her hands. “Oh, of course, my mistake. I’ll be sure to keep them frostbite-free just for you.”

When their drinks arrived, they fell into step together, heading inside as the breeze carried the scent of coffee and fallen leaves around them. They walked in comfortable silence for a few moments, sipping their coffee as the early morning light cast long shadows across the lab building’s polished floors. Then Rio broke the quiet with a surprisingly earnest tone.

“Dr. Harkness, I have a question about your research.”

Agatha glanced at her, eyebrow raised. “Ask away.”

Rio paused, looking as if she were about to dive into some deep, thoughtful inquiry, but then her lips curled into a smirk. “I just wanted to tell you how absolutely groundbreaking I found it,” she said, imitating Jennifer’s overly eager tone from yesterday.

Agatha scoffed, shaking her head. “Don’t even,” she warned, though she couldn’t suppress her smile. Rio’s laughter was bright and unguarded, echoing softly in the hallway as they walked.

After a moment, Rio cleared her throat, her tone shifting to something more thoughtful. “Alright, alright, I did have an actual question.” She looked at Agatha with a seriousness that made her curiosity feel all the more genuine. “If, as you hypothesise, depression is an early-life risk factor for Alzheimer’s… would that risk change if the depression was treated? Using CBT, say, or some other form of therapy?”

Agatha blinked, slightly taken aback by the insightfulness of Rio’s question.

Rio continued, her gaze unwavering. “What I mean is, do you think the risk factor lies in the actual experience of depression? Or is it more about having depression in the first place, like there’s some genetic factor involved?”

Agatha took a slow sip of her coffee, collecting her thoughts. “That’s an excellent question, actually. It’s something I’m still figuring out,” she said, a glint of respect in her eyes as she looked at Rio. “There’s evidence suggesting it’s both. The genetic component was what I had originally thought, that maybe something in the gene for depression was linked to the gene for Alzheimer’s. But then we did a study that showed that how severe someone’s depression is, is actually correlated to how severe the Alzheimer’s would be. That suggests it’s more complicated than just… if you have one, you have the other.”

Rio nodded thoughtfully, processing the answer. “So that means if a person’s depression is treated and managed, it could potentially lower their risk?”

“It’s possible,” Agatha replied, warming to the discussion. “The theory is that interventions, like CBT or drug treatments, might mitigate some of the damage that increases Alzheimer’s risk. But that’s what we’re hoping to confirm through this research.”

Rio nodded, her expression thoughtful. “I didn’t expect the connection to be so direct,” she admitted, glancing at Agatha. “That you could potentially prevent Alzheimer’s by addressing mental health decades earlier.”

Agatha felt a flicker of pride. Rio might have her sarcastic edge, but it was clear she had an agile mind, one that didn’t shy away from complexity. “This is the frontier, Rio. It’s all uncharted territory.”

“Uncharted territory,” Rio repeated softly, a smile playing on her lips. She glanced at Agatha.

Agatha’s breath hitched, the sincerity in Rio’s eyes catching her off guard. For a moment, they just looked at each other, caught in a moment of understanding that felt like it stretched beyond research and data. Finally, Agatha broke the gaze, clearing her throat.

“Let’s see if you’re still this intrigued once you’re actually elbow-deep in data with the rest of us,” she replied, aiming for nonchalance.

"Hold on. So you’re telling me there’s actually serious work in research? And here I was thinking you just liked bossing us around," Rio teased, her smirk widening as she glanced at Agatha from beneath her dark lashes.

Agatha chuckled, though she felt a strange warmth creeping into her cheeks. "Trust me, I do. And you, Rio, are a prime candidate for it.”

"Glad to be of service," Rio shot back with a salute, her grin wide. They reached the lab, and for a moment, Agatha lingered by the door, caught in Rio’s gaze longer than she intended.

“Alright,” she said, stepping aside and motioning for Rio to enter first. “Now, hand over my scarf.”

Rio sighed dramatically, unwrapping it and handing it back, her fingers brushing Agatha's as she did. “As you wish,” she murmured, her tone teasing, but her eyes held something deeper.

Agatha took the scarf, feeling the warmth where Rio had held it. As Rio made her way over to one of the lab benches Agatha called from behind her "Now, time to start brainstorming. Your PhD topic is one of the most important decisions of your career. I’m excited to see what you come up with."

Rio gave a small, resolute nod, her usual smirk replaced by a quiet determination. Without further comment, she pulled her chair closer to the bench where a stack of microscope slides and autopsy reports from the patients who had given the donations sat. Agatha’s brow furrowed. She was certain those hadn’t been there when she’d left the students at their stations the night before.

Had Rio already gotten out the cases to look at? Had she been already digging into the material before her first official day of research? Agatha’s mind raced in a mix of curiosity and disbelief. Most students would wait for the formal start of their research, would take time to review the lab’s resources and perhaps ask for guidance before diving in. But Rio? No, she didn’t seem the type to follow any prescribed order.

She stayed by the doorway, observing as Rio pulled her chair close and immediately began examining each microscope slide in turn, flipping through the thick binder of autopsy reports with a quiet determination. There was no hint of the usual smirk or sarcasm; instead, Rio’s face held an intense, thoughtful focus. Agatha stood there a moment longer, something about the quiet resolve in Rio’s expression making her linger before she finally turned and headed to her own desk on the other side of the lab.

She settled into her chair, trying to direct her attention to the work waiting for her. But every few seconds, she found herself glancing up, catching little glimpses of Rio in her calm, meticulous process.

Rio began examining each microscope slide in turn. Agatha lingered a moment, watching as Rio opened a thick binder of autopsy reports, her eyes darting between the pages and slides, making notes in quick, slanted handwriting. Agatha knew she should get back to her own work, but something about Rio’s focused expression kept drawing her attention. Gone was the playful smirk, the unguarded sarcasm, here was a different side of Rio. Calm, intensely focused, and utterly immersed.

Every few seconds, Agatha glanced over, unable to fully ignore her student’s unusual concentration. Rio’s fingers deftly adjusted each slide under the microscope, her brows slightly furrowed in thought as she read through the patients' histories. She looked up once, catching Agatha watching her. For a brief second, Rio’s mouth curled into a faint smirk before she turned back to the reports, as if absorbing Agatha's silent attention.

After some time, Rio spoke, her voice quiet yet assured. “Alzheimer’s affects only the lower regions of the hippocampus, right? CA2, CA3, and CA4?”

Agatha was slightly surprised by the question, they had been silent for almost an hour. “Yes, primarily. A study I did a few years ago showed that those regions show the earliest signs of neurodegeneration. The rest are somewhat spared.”

Rio nodded, seemingly filing away the information, her eyes still on the report in her hand. “Got it,” she murmured, almost to herself.

As the hours passed, Agatha continued her own work, occasionally stealing glances across the lab. She noted the careful precision in Rio’s movements, the way her lips pressed together in a subtle frown as she scribbled down observations. She’d seen plenty of students go through this stage nervous, uncertain. But Rio’s poise intrigued her. There was something uniquely captivating about her when she was fully absorbed, different from the sarcastic girl she’d met on her first day.

By mid-morning, as sunlight began to filter through the lab’s high windows, the door swung open and the rest of the students trickled in. Billy, Jen, and Alice entered, each one greeting Agatha with a mix of apprehension and respect before settling into their own stations. They exchanged a few curious glances toward Rio, who was too engrossed in her work to notice. Agatha, however, did notice.

The clock ticked away in the background, leaving Agatha with a few more minutes before her lecture began. The lab had settled into a hum of concentration, with Rio hardly lifting her head from the slides and reports spread before her. The other students were scattered across their workstations, but Agatha could feel their eyes on Rio as they exchanged glances, their curiosity piqued by the girl who had already been there when they arrived.

Billy was the one to break the silence. Agatha could barely hear his voice across the lab, but she caught the words clearly enough. "How long have you been here, Rio?"

Without looking up, Rio’s voice floated across the room. "Since 7.30."

The others looked stunned. Alice, her voice rising slightly in disbelief, added, "Wow, that early? Well, we messaged you to ask if you wanted to carpool…we all came together."

Only then did Rio lift her gaze, glancing at Alice with a raised eyebrow and a smirk that said it all. "I didn’t reply for a reason," she said, her voice cool. "I have no interest in showing up at 10 a.m. I’m here to actually do work."

Agatha had to admit, she was impressed. There was no hesitation in Rio’s tone, no need to justify herself. She simply stated it as a fact, as though it were the most natural thing in the world to show up early and just get to work.

The others, however, seemed less than impressed. Jen rolled her eyes and huffed. "What, You think you’re so much better than us, huh? Is that it?"

Alice shot Jen a quick glare, putting a hand on her arm. "Jen, lay off her," she said quietly, trying to smooth over the tension. Billy chimed in next. "Yeah, that’s probably not what she meant, right, Rio?"

Agatha couldn’t help but glance over. She had only met Rio yesterday, but she had an inkling of how the girl was about to respond. Just as Rio opened her mouth, a glint of mischief in her eyes, Agatha stepped in.

"Lecture time, everyone. Let’s head upstairs. Now."

Her tone left no room for argument, and with that, the conversation fizzled out. Agatha watched as Rio glanced over, giving her a look that was half surprise, half amusement. But there was no time for further words. The students, still a little on edge from the exchange, began to gather their things and move toward the stairs.

Agatha waited a moment, letting the room settle before following them. She couldn’t shake the thought of Rio, her calm demeanour now matching the cool confidence she had displayed earlier. There was something about her that made Agatha’s attention linger, but she quickly pushed the thought aside. It was time for work.

— — —

As they entered the lecture hall, Rio was struck by its unremarkable size. It was small, barely seating 30 people, but it felt intimate, the kind of room where every word would echo, and every gaze would be felt. The other students filed in, taking their seats with an air of nervous anticipation. Rio, however, felt strangely detached from the tension in the room. She chose a seat toward the back, leaning into the chair with an ease that almost seemed to mock the others, who sat with their backs as straight as possible, no doubt trying to impress Dr. Harkness. Try-hards , Rio thought with a small smirk, folding her arms and letting her eyes wander.

Dr. Harkness had moved to the front of the room, already setting up her laptop and preparing to give her presentation. Other unfamiliar faces trickled in - academics, other researchers, no doubt curious about the research being presented, or perhaps just about Dr. Harkness herself.

“Good morning everyone.” Dr Harkness started, her voice firm. Rio’s gaze lingered on her, her focus shifting in a way that felt almost instinctive. She admired how Dr. Harkness commanded the room. It wasn’t just her words, or even her research; it was the way she moved, the way she held herself. As the lights dimmed and the first slide appeared, Dr. Harkness turned to the audience, already projecting a kind of power and authority.

"Today, I’ll be presenting my work on the potential link between early-life depression and the risk of Alzheimer’s," Dr. Harkness began, her voice steady and commanding. "As we know, depression affects a significant portion of the population, but the question of how depression may influence the onset of Alzheimer’s has been a topic of considerable debate in the scientific community."

"So, I have been studying this theory for years. My research has found evidence for a correlation between early-life depression and an increased risk of developing Alzheimer’s later in life. However, the exact neural correlates have remained relatively unknown. Until now."

With that, Dr. Harkness clicked again changing to a slide which displayed brain scans with highlighted areas of the hippocampus (the area of the brain responsible for memory). The audience leaned in as she continued, her voice never wavering. "What we’ve discovered is that depression, particularly when it occurs in early adulthood, seems to accelerate atrophy in the hippocampus-”

Rio’s attention shifted away from the slides, the lecture fading into the background as her focus shifted back to the woman at the front of the room. She couldn’t help but admire the way Dr. Harkness performed in front of the room, her hand gestures exaggerated just enough to emphasise each point she made, her voice pitch-perfect with the right amount of emphasis on every key word. It was almost like an art. Each move, each glance, every deliberate pause building tension and focus. Rio found herself captivated, not just by the research, but by the woman giving the lecture.

Rio’s mind wandered back to earlier, to that moment in the cold outside the lab, when she had taken off her scarf and handed it to Rio. It had been such a small gesture, but something about it had shattered the icy facade that Dr Harkness seemed to keep so carefully in place. That moment, when she had almost softened, had been the first time Rio saw her as more than just a rigid academic. There was something behind those sharp eyes, something that Rio hadn’t expected, and it sent a shiver down her spine.

Her gaze remained fixed on Dr. Harkness as the lecture continued, but Rio wasn’t really listening anymore. She was too caught up in the Dr Harkness moved, the way her lips parted just slightly as she spoke, the faint rise and fall of her chest with each inhale. She wasn’t sure why, but she couldn’t tear her eyes away. There was a magnetic pull that the woman exerted without even realising it, something that made Rio’s pulse quicken in the most unexpected way.

As Dr Harkness continued, Rio’s mind drifted again, recalling the way Agatha had held herself that morning. Assertive, controlled, unyielding in her usual manner, but with that crack, however small, of something more. What is it about you, Dr Harkness? Rio thought, a faint curiosity tugging at her.

A small smile played at the corner of Rio's lips as she leaned back in her chair, trying to steady her racing thoughts. It wasn’t just the research. It was the woman herself, the mystery she presented, the way she seemed to be always in control, but - at least for a moment - had let it slip this morning. That small break in her otherwise flawless, harsh exterior was enough to make Rio curious of what else lay under her harsh facade

She didn’t realise at first that Agatha had noticed her staring, but when their eyes met, it was impossible to miss the brief pause in Agatha's presentation. Agatha's gaze flicked to her, sharp and calculating, but there was a subtle smirk playing at the corner of her lips. Rio felt the tension in the air shift, the moment thick with a challenge, but she didn’t look away.

"Miss Vidal," Dr. Harkness's voice broke through the quiet, smooth and teasing. "I just instructed you all to turn your attention to the graphs on the slide. Do you have a problem with doing so?"

It was playful, but there was an edge to it, the kind of edge Rio had come to expect from Agatha. The room seemed to hold its breath, and for a split second, Rio wondered if she should just look down at her lap, act like she’d been paying attention. But then again, where was the fun in that?

"No problem at all, Dr. Harkness," Rio said, her voice light and smooth, matching the playful tone Agatha had set, an innocent smile crawling across her face. "Just thought the way you present was.. fascinating ."

Her words hung in the air for a moment, and Rio could feel the other students shifting slightly. But Agatha didn’t flinch. Instead, she gave a small, satisfied nod and returned her attention to the slide.

"Well, I expect you all to find the research just as fascinating. Now, as I was saying—"

Rio leaned back in her seat as Dr Harkness continued, a faint smile playing at her lips, though her thoughts were already elsewhere. Dr Harkness had definitely noticed her. And for a split second, Rio wondered just how much of that was intentional.

chapter 3

but yeah this chapter is a lil shorter so I was able to get it done pretty quickly yay
anyways I hope u guys enjoy, as I said thank you SO much for all the comments u guys are the sweetest <3

See the end of the chapter for more notes

It was only a few days into the term, and Agatha had already settled into her routine: balancing her own research with overseeing her new batch of PhD students.

They were an uneven group, Billy was bubbly and kind, Alice was focused and efficient, and Jen… Well, she was an obvious suck-up. Agatha could already see that Jen didn’t have the depth of knowledge she pretended to. She was a classic “fake it till you make it” type, but that wouldn’t work here. Agatha had no tolerance for shallow displays of competence; Jen would need to truly learn this if she wanted to succeed in Agatha’s lab.

And then there was Rio Vidal.

Rio had an energy Agatha hadn’t seen in a student in years. She was bold, with a sharp tongue and a confidence that danced perilously close to arrogance. Agatha had been watching her work, noting the way Rio sifted through research papers with an intense, almost defiant focus, as if daring the material to disappoint her. And every so often, Rio would glance up, and they’d make eye contact across the lab. Rio never looked away, her gaze unwavering, as if daring Agatha to react, always accompanied by that smirk that seemed to say I know exactly what you’re thinking, causing Agatha to scoff inwardly in annoyance.

Yet, as much as Rio’s attitude got under her skin, Agatha found herself watching her closely. There was an energy to Rio’s intellect, a quickness that suggested she was actually as bright as she believed herself to be. Agatha noticed the way Rio would pore over research papers, scanning pages with a brisk intensity, occasionally muttering to herself when something didn’t match her expectations.

The past few days had been quiet in the lab. The students, for the most part, had gotten on with their work, each absorbed in their own areas of study. Agatha, though she didn’t expect much from them this early in the semester, had checked in periodically. She knew they’d still be in the stage of narrowing down their PhD topics, sorting through vast amounts of information, and trying to figure out where their own interests intersected with the broader field. She didn’t expect any of them to have a solid project idea ready for at least another week, maybe more.

Billy had been working steadily through his readings, asking an occasional question when he hit a snag with the literature. He seemed like the type who would thrive with a clear set of instructions and a structured plan, though Agatha would have to watch him to see if he could come up with something original. Alice was quiet, efficient, never needing much guidance, but Agatha suspected she was playing it safe, keeping her ideas close to her chest. She’d need a little more time before the real substance of her project emerged.

Then there was Jen. Agatha had caught her once or twice pretending to be deep in thought, but her questions were always superficial—how to organise a literature review, when the next lab meeting was, what kind of formatting they should use for a grant proposal. Nothing that gave Agatha any confidence in her actual research capabilities. Jen seemed to think if she kept asking questions, she could fool Agatha into thinking she was on the right track. Agatha wasn’t fooled. The real work hadn’t begun yet for Jen, but it would have to eventually.

For the most part, the students had left her to her own research. Agatha was grateful for the silence, the uninterrupted hours she could spend digging into her own projects. She had retired to her office and was deep into a paper about the intersection of aging and trauma when Rio approached her desk. Agatha didn’t look up at first, content to let the tension build a little longer

“Need something, Miss Vidal?” she asked, head still pointed down at the paper she was reading , her voice cool, though her curiosity was piqued.

Rio folded her arms, regarding Agatha with a calculating expression. “I have some questions,” she said. “About my project.” Her tone was measured but still held that hint of audacity. Agatha waited, finally glancing up at her, curious but careful not to show it.

Agatha raised an eyebrow, gesturing to the chair in front of her desk, ‘Be my guest.’ She said dryly, although she was eager to hear what Rio had been thinking.

Rio cleared her throat, taking a seat as she continued. “I’ve been going through your past publications, specifically your work on the hippocampus,” she began, holding Agatha’s gaze. “And I’ve been thinking, you found hippocampus degeneration in both epilepsy and Alzheimer’s. But in your study they seemed to target different areas. Alzheimer’s mostly the lower regions of the hippocampus: CA2, CA3, and CA4. Whereas epilepsy causes degeneration all over.’

Agatha tilted her head slightly, her tone clipped. “Yes, I do in fact know what my own research concluded, Miss Vidal. What is your point?”

Rio leaned forward, her voice steady and laced with a subtle satisfaction. “Well, Dr Harkness.” she said, pausing just long enough for her smirk to deepen, “I was looking through some microscope slides from the brain bank, and there are cases where patients with Alzheimer’s showed degeneration all over their hippocampus, not just the lower areas. And there was only one thing those patients had in common: seizures.”

Agatha felt a flicker of disbelief and irritation ripple through her. So that’s what Rio had been after, combing through the slides with such scrutiny. She had found something that directly challenged the neat boundaries Agatha’s research had set. She couldn’t help but feel a sting of offense, and yet… a glimmer of respect, too. There was a sharpness to Rio’s gaze, an assuredness that Agatha couldn’t ignore. She wasn’t just here to follow in anyone’s footsteps; she was carving out her own line of questioning, regardless of whose toes she might step on along the way.

Agatha sat back slightly, her irritation tempered by interest. It was a significant observation, and one that very few students would have thought to pursue. “Interesting,” she allowed, watching Rio’s reaction closely. “So you think there could be a link between Alzheimer’s and Epilepsy? You could be onto something, but that’s an enormous topic for a first research project.”

Rio’s eyes lit up, her voice steady and assured, but with a glint of boldness “That was what I came to ask you about… What would you say about tackling it together? A co-authored study?”

Agatha’s brow lifted in surprise. Bold move, she thought, sizing Rio up. She leaned forward in her chair. “It’s intriguing certainly. I’m listening. But do you even know where we’d start with something like that?”

Rio leaned forward as well, almost mirroring Agatha’s movements. “I want to study the relationship between the progression of both diseases. The possibility that one could exacerbate or even trigger the other. I believe we could find a connection in the subregions of the hippocampus. It could reveal why some epilepsy patients show degeneration in patterns similar to those with Alzheimer’s

Agatha held her gaze, resisting the urge to smile. Rio was annoyingly self-assured, but she had a point. This wasn’t idle speculation; it was a genuinely intriguing line of inquiry. But she’d be damned if she’d let Rio see her approval. “You think you can make the link?”

Rio’s expression sharpened, and she leaned forward. “Yes. I do.”

Agatha regarded her for a long moment, the silence thick with unspoken thoughts. Finally, she gave a faint, almost reluctant nod. “Well, if my own research is going to be turned upside down, I suppose I might as well be part of the process,” she said, her tone dry but edged with interest. “I’ll help you tackle this, Vidal. But understand it won’t be easy. I don’t do things halfway.”

A glint of triumph lit Rio’s eyes and she leaned a little closer, a knowing smile playing at her lips, as if she’d been waiting for Agatha to take the bait. “I wouldn’t expect anything less from you Dr Harkness.”

The casual boldness in her tone sent a slight jolt through Agatha, and she shifted in her chair, steeling herself against the tinge of intrigue that had begun to feel far too personal. She narrowed her eyes, keeping her voice cool. “Good. Because if you’re serious about this, you’ll need to match my rigour, my discipline. We’re talking about research that could turn more than a few heads. You think you’re ready for that?”

Rio’s gaze lingered on her, unflinching. “Absolutely. I’m ready.”

A silence stretched between them, charged and far too intense. Agatha cleared her throat, breaking eye contact, and nodded curtly. “Then we start immediately. Be prepared to re-examine every assumption you’ve ever made, every study you’ve ever read. You’ll need to convince me, and the field, that you’re onto something here.”

Rio’s smirk only widened, and she held Agatha’s gaze for a beat longer than was necessary. “Oh, I will.”

The look was uncomfortably lingering, and Agatha felt her skin prickle with an awareness she refused to acknowledge. She broke the moment with a brisk, dismissive flick of her hand, forcing her tone into something closer to brusque indifference. “Good. Now get back to work, and be ready to update me first thing tomorrow. No excuses.”

Rio raised an eyebrow, amusement glimmering in her eyes. “Understood, see you tomorrow.” She turned on her heel, casting a final, unreadable glance over her shoulder as she strode out of the room.

As Agatha watched her go, she exhaled slowly, feeling the pulse of something unsettling lingering in the air. A sharp, electric awareness that she couldn’t quite shake.

It was more than Rio’s intellect that had caught her attention; there was a quiet intensity in the way Rio held herself, a confidence that pulled at Agatha’s composure in ways she was unwilling to admit. The way her dark hair fell just slightly out of place, as if to emphasise the casual defiance in her demeanour. Her eyes, sharp and calculating, never once breaking away when they’d locked onto Agatha’s; instead, they held steady, as though challenging Agatha to react, daring her to say or do something. Her smile, that smirk, that was always there, like a quiet, knowing invitation to something more. The way her lips curved with the slightest hint of mischief, her eyes never fully revealing what was behind them. It was a look that unsettled Agatha more than she cared to admit.

She forced herself to look back at her own research, tightening her jaw. This was just another project, another student, another question to answer. She wouldn’t allow herself to get distracted. Yet, despite her best efforts, the faint thrill of Rio’s words, her defiant spark, left a trace that lingered far longer than she wanted to admit.

chapter 4

Chapter Notes

posting this chapter a lil earlier than I thought bc my wifi is gonna be down tmr :/ so, I wont be able to post, buttt it means that I decided to edit + post this one today instead!

hope u enjoyyyy :))

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Agatha arrived at the lab earlier than usual, the soft hum of the fluorescent lights barely audible in the sterile, near-empty space. Her heels clicked sharply against the linoleum floor as she walked past the rows of equipment, her mind already flicking through a mental checklist of things to address. But then she froze.

At the far end of the lab, next to the microscope, was Rio. The sight caught her off guard. Rio was seated in her usual spinny chair, looking unusually relaxed, one leg up on the chair as she tucked her knee to her chest, leaning her arm over the knee.

Agatha’s eyes narrowed, scanning the scene without moving any closer. Rio’s tan trousers and loose white T-shirt were more casual than Agatha was used to seeing, though the black sweater vest, loose around her shoulders, was a familiar touch of the sharp confidence Agatha had come to both admire and detest. Her hair sprawled around her shoulders and the edges shone slightly brown as they were illuminated in the soft morning glow.

But there was something about the way Rio held herself. Poised, intent, at ease in the space. It was hard to ignore. Agatha forced herself to look away. Focus. No time for distractions.

Agatha made her way towards Rio, she was close now, almost at Rio’s side, but the younger woman hadn’t noticed her yet, still absorbed in the microscope slide in her hands as she brought the piece of glass to her mouth.

Agatha watched, bemused, as Rio exhaled softly over the surface, fogging it briefly before reaching up with a sleeve to wipe it down.

Her movements were oddly graceful, as if she had all the time in the world, yet there was a sense of purpose behind every flick of her wrist. Rio held the slide up to the light, the soft glow illuminating the sharpness of her features. She ran a slender finger down its length, inspecting it with furrowed brows before squinting slightly, trying to see something just out of reach.

Agatha’s gaze lingered a moment too long. The way Rio’s fingers traced the glass with such care and precision, all of it was disarmingly captivating for some reason. The angle of Rio’s neck, the tilt of her head as she squinted at the slide, the almost meditative quality of her movements... Agatha snapped her focus back to the task at hand.

She leaned in, closer still, until her mouth was just next to Rio’s ear.

"What are we looking at?" Agatha chimed.

The sound of Rio's soft inhale was the only response at first, then, when Rio turned her head with a flash of surprise in her eyes, Agatha added, "You know, just a pro tip, when you’re looking at a microscope slide, using a microscope usually helps."

The smirk that crept onto Rio’s lips was instant, as if the sarcastic quip had already been expected. "Very funny," Rio muttered. "But I’m not looking at the cells. I’m looking at where the slide cuts off."

Agatha raised an eyebrow, intrigued despite herself. She leaned closer, squinting at the slide now visible in the light. The swirling structure was unmistakable, it was the hippocampus. Her favourite part of the brain. That delicate, spiralling shape, so tiny yet responsible for such a monumental task: the coordination of memory. Not just personal memories but meanings of words, facts, motor skills, every mundane detail of daily life depends on this small region.

Agatha watched as Rio’s finger traced the edge of the slide, pointing at the far right. "See here? The slide cuts off before the end of CA1 at the very edge. I can’t see the whole hippocampus."

Agatha's eyes followed the path Rio's finger traced for a moment, mesmerised. It took her a moment to process what Rio had actually said. Clearing her throat in attempt to regain any kind of clarity in her mind. Focus, Agatha. This was important work, not time for distractions.

"That’s a good catch," Agatha admitted, her voice steady, though she could feel the rush of warmth creeping under her collar.

Rio glanced up at her, catching her expression and offering a faint but knowing smirk. "I wonder if it would be possible to cut new slides."

The suggestion caught Agatha off guard. It was rare for PhD students to need new slides, especially not with all the prepared samples in the lab. Most researchers just worked with what they had. Agatha opened her mouth, ready to tell Rio the logistical nightmare that would entail: tracking down case numbers for the right donated brains, checking availability, all the usual hoops.

Before Agatha could open her mouth to suggest it, Rio said, "I’ve got all the case numbers for the patients we need."

Agatha froze. She’s already ahead of me. The thought irritated her, but she refused to let it show. She was the one in charge here. Her stomach twisted with a mix of irritation and reluctant admiration. She was losing her edge.

But there was still more to discuss. They’d also need to check whether there was enough hippocampus tissue left in those donated brains, right? It was a critical detail.

Rio, with that same knowing look, added, "And I checked the ‘room of doom’ this morning. All the fixed samples have enough hippocampus tissue for us to take, except one. But that one has a frozen hippocampus that I figured we could embed and use instead."

Agatha felt a pang of frustration. She barely had the chance to speak, and Rio had anticipated every concern, already solving problems Agatha hadn’t even voiced yet. The girl’s efficiency was infuriating. But there was no denying it: Rio Vidal was proving herself a formidable force in the lab.

For a brief moment, Agatha stood there, stunned into silence. Then, almost against her will, she let out a sharp laugh, the edge of it coloured with respect.

She crossed her arms, trying to regain some semblance of authority. "Well, I suppose you’ve thought of everything, haven’t you?"

Rio’s smirk widened, her eyes glinting as they met Agatha's, not a trace of hesitation in them. "I try," she said smoothly, then added, "It’s not often I get the chance to surprise the Wicked Witch after all."

Agatha raised an eyebrow, leaning in just slightly, her tone playful but edged. "Careful. Not everyone who surprises me lives to tell the tale.”

Rio didn’t miss a beat, her smile deepening, almost daring her. She snickered, unfazed. "So I’ve heard. But I don’t scare that easily." She leaned back in her chair, her posture almost as much of a challenge as her words, arms folded in a mirror of Agatha’s stance. "Besides, I think you’re secretly enjoying the challenge."

Agatha scoffed, though she couldn’t shake the thrill curling low in her stomach. Rio’s words were almost too direct, too bold, yet there was an undercurrent, a glimmer in her eye that Agatha couldn’t ignore. "Don’t flatter yourself," she replied, levelling a cool gaze at her. But her tone softened despite herself.

"Oh, I don’t have to.” Rio shot back with a grin, her voice dropping just enough that it sent an unwelcome warmth creeping up Agatha’s neck. “You seem to do that plenty for me,"

Agatha caught her breath but held her ground, leaning forward just enough to tower over Rio where she sat in her chair. "You’re not here to play games, Rio. This is serious work," she said, the formality in her tone undercut slightly by the glimmer in her eyes.

Rio tilted her head to the side, her gaze unwavering "I know. But who says serious work can’t have a little… intrigue?"

The words hung in the air between them, taut and unyielding. Agatha opened her mouth, about to retort, but the words faltered as Rio’s lips curled into that subtle, almost conspiratorial smile that seemed reserved just for her. Agatha was at a loss for words. An unusual, rare state that only seemed to happen around Rio. For a brief, tense moment, they simply looked at each other, an unspoken challenge hanging between them.

"Fine," Agatha said at last, straightening up and nodding toward the microscope. "If you’re so determined to impress, you can start by actually looking at that slide under the microscope instead of just waving it around, then make notes of exactly what we need from the new slides so we get them right this time. I expect no detail to be spared,"

Rio chuckled, leaning forward to adjust the microscope with an exaggerated flourish. "Your wish is my command, Dr Harkness." she murmured.

Agatha shook her head, managing to turn away just as she felt her own mouth begin to tug into a smile. But as she began the walk to her office, the lingering warmth of Rio’s gaze stayed with her, seeping beneath her skin, leaving her thoughts tangled in a way that, perhaps, she couldn’t afford to unravel.

Agatha strode back to her office, each step brisk, purposeful, as if she could walk off the thoughts that Rio had stirred up. Settling at her desk, she took a deep breath and opened her notebook, flipping to her most recent research notes. But as she tried to focus on her work, she found herself staring through the pages rather than at them.

Her mind wandered back to yesterday. Agatha’s grip tightened around her pen, her eyes narrowing as she recalled that moment. The nerve Rio had to so confidently point out a flaw in her work, one Agatha herself had overlooked. It had been only days into Rio’s PhD, and she’d somehow spotted an inconsistency that had slipped right past Agatha’s meticulous attention to detail. Agatha was no stranger to constructive criticism, especially from colleagues of her standing, but from a first-year PhD student?

The audacity was infuriating.

But it wasn’t just the audacity. It was the infuriating fact that Rio had been right. Agatha could still remember the slight smugness in Rio’s gaze when she’d brought it up, a smirk as though she already knew she’d caught something significant. Agatha’s pride smarted at the memory, and she found herself tapping the pen harder against her desk.

And now, this morning, Rio had done it again, catching an error in the lab’s slides that, admittedly, Agatha hadn’t noticed. It was supposed to be a routine, ordinary task, yet Rio had observed, within minutes, that the hippocampus slide was incomplete. CA1 severed at the edge. The precise attentiveness, the way Rio’s eyes had narrowed, picking apart the oversight… Agatha’s jaw clenched, a slight heat of irritation flaring beneath her collar.

She’s good. Too good. Agatha mused, tapping her pen absently against the page.

The image of Rio inspecting that slide surfaced in her mind again, unwelcome but vivid. Her breath hitched as she remembered the way Rio’s fingers had delicately traced the glass, her profile highlighted in the soft light from the window. The messy strands of hair loosely tucked behind her ears. She looked.. Graceful. Beautiful even.

Agatha blinked, briefly taken aback as she realised her thoughts had drifted further than she intended. Where did that even come from? No, she told herself firmly. This is unprofessional. She’s your student. You’re here to guide her, not…

Clenching her jaw. Agatha shut her notebook with more force than necessary, as if that act alone could dispel the image from her mind. She forced herself to redirect her focus to the day’s work, her mind set on research tasks that required all of her concentration. She would not indulge these thoughts any longer. Whatever fascination Rio inspired was something she needed to leave buried beneath the layers of professionalism. This wasn’t the time, and Rio Vidal was most certainly not the person, for such distractions.

Keep your distance, she reminded herself, her eyes hardening with resolve as she reopened her notebook.

Chapter End Notes
