chapter 5

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Agatha settled into her office. She flung her bag onto the leather chair beside her desk and sighed. The early light cast soft shadows across her office, and a rare quiet settled over the department. She’d arrived before anyone else today, hoping the silence would grant her some semblance of clarity.

She let out a slow, measured breath and dropped onto her desk chair. Normally, the sight of her meticulously organised office, a refuge of books, data sheets, and the sharp scent of lab chemicals, was enough to calm her mind. Today, however, not even the stark, clinical silence could anchor her.

Her jaw clenched as she flipped open her laptop, pulling up a file she’d barely managed to read the night before. She needed to focus on her paper, the one she'd been chipping away at for months. It was foundational, the kind of study that could shift paradigms in neuroscience. If she could just focus long enough to get it done.

But her mind refused to cooperate, drawing her back to the look in Rio’s eyes yesterday. That glint of amusement. The slow, deliberate way her fingers moved over the microscope slides, like she was handling something precious, something alive. Agatha’s cheeks flamed, and she forced herself to look at the sterile rows of data on her screen, hoping the familiar coldness would seep into her thoughts.

She took a breath, then another, forcing herself to focus on the paper draft in front of her. The influence of early-life depression on risk of developing Alzheimer’s Disease stared back at her in bold font, but instead of data points and neural pathways, her mind drifted to Rio’s exasperating smirk, the way her fingers had moved gracefully over the microscope slides yesterday.

What on earth are you doing to me, Vidal? She thought to herself, leaning back in her chair with a frustrated sigh. She couldn’t understand how someone so young, so newly transferred, managed to occupy her thoughts like this. But It wasn’t just Rio’s confidence that set her off. It was her unshakable, almost mocking ease around Agatha, her willingness to challenge and even provoke. Most students would cower under Agatha’s notorious gaze. Rio, however, acted as if she and Agatha were in some twisted intellectual dance. Worse, it felt like Agatha was starting to play along.

Agatha clenched her jaw, hating how her thoughts spiralled each time she considered that smirk or remembered how close Rio had leaned over the lab bench. The previous morning had been particularly exasperating. Agatha had caught herself watching the way Rio’s fingers had trailed along the edge of the glass slide, lingering over her movements rather than actually listening to what Rio was pointing out. Every attempt to focus had dissolved into distraction

‘Snap out of it, Harkness.’ she hissed into her empty office, shaking her head. This wasn’t her. Dr Agatha Harkness did not get distracted by PhD students. Especially not by cocky transfers who thought they could waltz into her lab and act like they belonged there. She didn’t allow distractions. She was controlled, professional, methodical. Traits she’d perfected over years in academia. She’d be damned if she let this girl break down every wall she had put up since the start of her career.

So, she’d tried to keep her distance, keeping Rio occupied with assignments that required minimal supervision. She had notes to make on the requests for new slides, something tedious and time-consuming that wouldn’t require Agatha to linger nearby.

She couldn’t bring herself to set foot in the lab. She told herself it was to focus on her own paper and give Rio the chance to get those notes done. But in reality, she knew she was avoiding Rio. Avoiding the way Rio looked at her, the way her questions cut past pretence and got right to the core. Avoiding that hint of something she couldn’t explain, something that went beyond the typical annoyance she felt with students.

As the hours passed, Agatha stayed resolutely behind her office door, buried in drafts and emails. She convinced herself it was for the best, that keeping her distance would help her refocus, help her reclaim control over her thoughts.

But each time she tried to focus on the work in front of her, her eyes glazed over and her mind circled back to Rio. She pictured her again. Her casual stance, her sharp eyes that seemed to read Agatha’s every move, her irritatingly calm confidence. Agatha gritted her teeth, the pen in her hand hovering idly over the paper as she found herself, once again, stuck in this loop.

This is insane, Agatha thought, her teeth clenched. She’d been in this field far too long to be rattled by a student, no matter how infuriating. Yet, deep down, she sensed there was more to this feeling than mere irritation. There was a tension she didn’t want to acknowledge, something electric about their exchanges that she just couldn’t shake.

Time dragged on, the hours slipping by with glacial slowness. Eventually, the sun dipped lower, shadows stretching across her office. She’d spent the entire day in here, hiding from her own lab, just to avoid the distraction Rio seemed to be creating.

Agatha wasn’t stupid. She knew she couldn’t keep this up forever. Shutting herself away wasn’t a permanent solution to this growing problem. But for now, this distance was the only thing she could think of. A temporary barrier, just enough to clear her mind, to keep from succumbing to whatever strange pull Rio Vidal had over her.

She took a slow, steadying breath, forcing herself to concentrate. This is not like you. You’re better than this, she told herself.

By evening, the usual hum of productivity in the building had faded, the muffled sounds of students and faculty dwindling as they filed out. Agatha knew this was her chance to go down to the lab unnoticed. She needed to check on the work before the night ended, to review what Rio had managed to finish in her absence.

She glanced at the clock. 19:58. By now, she figured Rio must have left for the day. It was long after sundown, she would have gone home hours ago. Agatha could slip in, glance over the notes, and regain her footing without risking another unpredictable encounter.

With a sigh that felt closer to resignation than relief, Agatha pushed back her chair and made her way down the sterile hallway, her heels echoing in the emptiness.

The lights were dim, casting long shadows against the walls as she entered the lab. To her surprise, a figure was hunched over the lab bench, completely absorbed in a notebook, scribbling quick, precise notes. Rio.

Agatha froze, instinctively stepping back into the shadows, watching as Rio absentmindedly tucked a strand of hair behind her ear, her gaze fixed intently on the data. She moved with a surprising ease, focused, unaware of Agatha’s presence.

For a moment, Agatha thought of leaving before Rio could notice her, but something held her in place. She took a breath, squared her shoulders, and cleared her throat - a soft sound, but one that broke the quiet and drew Rio’s attention

Rio looked up, and a glimmer of surprise crossed her face, quickly replaced by her usual smirk. She glanced down at her watch, “Dr Harkness. Burning the midnight oil, are we?”

Agatha straightened, masking her surprise with a practiced coolness. “I could say the same about you,” she replied, her tone carefully neutral. “I assumed you’d have left by now.”

Rio shrugged, glancing back down at the notebook. “I’m almost done with the notes for the new slides, so I thought I might as well just finish them tonight. I didn’t expect you to be checking in though. I was beginning to think you’d left me to the wolves.” Her gaze drifted up, eyes narrowing slightly in that way that made Agatha feel as though she were the one under the microscope. “Avoiding the lab today, Dr Harkness?”

The challenge in her voice sent a thrill through Agatha, despite herself. Get it together, she scolded inwardly, her expression neutral.

Agatha bristled, pushing down the strange sensation that accompanied Rio’s casual challenge. “I have other work to attend to, Vidal. I can’t spend all my time micromanaging my students.”

Rio hummed in response. A small sound which, combined with that infuriating smirk, seemed to say she had read through Agatha’s bluff. “Of course.” her eyes held a glint of something curious, bordering on amused. “Well, you can relax. Everything’s on track. I’ve been making notes the old slides: where they cut off, and what we need to include for the new ones, as you requested.”

Agatha stepped closer to the bench, pulling out the spinny chair next to Rio and sitting down. She leaned back as she glanced at the stack of notes and the orderly trays of slides lined up beside them. Everything was meticulous, even more so than she’d expected. It was clear Rio had put considerable time into this work, going beyond what Agatha had assigned.

“You’ve done well,” Agatha said, her voice quiet but genuine, catching herself off-guard as the words slipped out. She rarely offered praise, and yet here it was, undeniable.

“High praise from The Wicked Witch herself,” Rio said, her voice dropping, edged with something unspoken. “Careful, you might make me think I’m your favorite.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow, attempting to keep her expression steady, though her pulse quickened at the teasing. She scoffed “I don’t have favourites, Rio,” she replied, a hint of steel in her voice. “But you’re… competent.”

Rio chuckled, letting her gaze linger on Agatha’s face for a beat too long. “ Competent ,” she repeated, savouring the word, her tone dripping with sarcasm. “Why do I feel like that’s the closest I’ll ever get to a compliment from you?”

Agatha shifted, feeling the intensity of Rio’s gaze like a physical pull. She looked out the window, anywhere but at Rio, taking in the streetlamp outside which shone into the lab, illuminating the otherwise dark room. “My opinion isn’t what matters here,” she said, keeping her tone crisp. “Your work does.”

“Oh, I don’t know.” Rio’s eyes flicked over Agatha’s face, tracing the lines of her mouth, the faint shadow of her jawline. “I think your opinion matters more than you’d like to admit.”

Agatha forced herself to meet Rio’s gaze, determined not to let the younger woman rattle her. “You wont get far with trying to read me, Rio. I don’t care for attempts at flattery”

“Good thing I’m not trying to flatter you, then. Or to read you.” Rio murmured, her voice barely above a whisper. “Though if I was trying, I’d say that I think you have more opinions about me than you let on.”

Agatha’s throat tightened, but she forced herself to keep her expression steady. “Is that so?” she replied with a curious tilt of her head, keeping her voice as steady as she could, though she could feel her pulse quickening.

“Very much so.” Rio’s gaze drifted down Agatha’s body for the briefest second, then back up, her eyes daring. “And I think you know it, too.”

Agatha’s jaw clenched, though her pulse quickened under Rio’s steady stare. She let out another scoff, “As I said, what I think of you is irrelevant.”

“Is it?” Rio’s lips curved, but her eyes held a different intensity. “Because if I didn’t know better, Dr Harkness, I’d say you have a habit of watching me that goes beyond… academic interest.”

Agatha’s composure slipped for a fraction of a second, just long enough for Rio to notice. She narrowed her eyes, determined not to give Rio any ground. “You’re imagining things, Vidal. I just expect my students to meet a certain standard. Nothing more.”

Rio chuckled softly, leaning forwards on her chair, her elbows resting on her knees. She was close enough that Agatha could catch the faint, warm scent of her perfume. “Right. And it’s just professional expectations that kept you away from the lab all day, then?”

Agatha felt her cheeks warm, a rare lapse that only seemed to fuel Rio’s amusement. Before she could respond, Rio tilted her head as she leaned back in her chair again, voice soft and challenging. “I think you enjoy the challenge. I think maybe… you like that I’m not afraid to push back.”

She should have shut this down, turned on her heel and left Rio with a clipped reminder about boundaries. But she couldn’t seem to move, couldn’t seem to break away from the way Rio’s gaze held her in place, daring her to admit something she wasn’t ready to confront.

Instead, she levelled her voice, masking the slight tremor beneath it. “Careful, Rio. You’re toeing a dangerous line.”

Rio’s smirk softened, but her eyes gleamed with unmistakable intent. “Oh I think I’m exactly where I want to be.” She held Agatha’s gaze, unflinching. “The question, Dr Harkness, is… are you?”

Agatha’s breath caught, but she kept her face impassive, swallowing hard. She placed a hand down firmly on the lab bench between them and stood up. Her tone ice-cool as she replied, “Enjoy your evening, Vidal.” And with that, she turned on her heel and left, the sound of Rio’s soft chuckle following her down the hallway, lingering in her mind long after she’d left the lab behind.

chapter 6

Chapter Notes

u guys I seriously have no self control when it comes to this fic so HERE HAVE ANOTHER CHAPTER MY LOVELIES I HOPE U ENJOYY!!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

It had been a few days since that conversation, and Agatha had tried her very best to ignore it. She’d thrown herself into work, been extra attentive to Billy, Alice and Jen’s questions. Stacked her schedule with extra meetings, taken on every request from the department. Anything to keep her mind from straying back to those maddening words.

"I’d say you have a habit of watching me that goes beyond academic interest."

How dare Rio be that bold? And what the hell did she even mean by it? Agatha was infuriated. She felt like Rio had seen right through her, piercing her defences in a way that left her strangely exposed. Agatha still didn’t understand the mess of feelings Rio seemed to provoke, but somehow, Rio seemed to understand exactly what was going on, and that was intolerable. This girl was always one step ahead, and it only added fuel to Agatha’s smouldering irritation.

The lab was silent now, the students out for lunch, and Agatha was grateful to take advantage of the quiet. She focused on sorting the latest brain donation her lab had received, welcoming the methodical process. This kind of work was simple and direct, almost mindless after Agatha had spent so many years managing this lab. She could lose herself in the work, letting each meticulous cut and measure carry her away from tangled thoughts.

She held the brain in her gloved hands, admiring the smooth, cold surface. She weighed it, logged the data, and carefully laid out her tools. Then, with a practiced hand, she made a clean cut down the centre, separating the hemispheres. She dropped one into the bucket of preservative - formalin - watching as it settled under the surface. The other half she laid on the tray before her, dividing it into sections. Each slice was delicate, precise. She labeled each piece in a plastic bag with its case number and the name of the brain area, then packed them carefully into a bag of dry ice to be stored in the freezer.

She was engrossed that she missed the faint sound of footsteps behind her, a light click she would’ve noticed under any other circumstances.

“Must be nice, working with someone who can’t talk back,” came Rio’s voice, breaking the silence.

Agatha tensed, fingers tightening on the tray for just a second. She didn’t turn around, taking a deliberate breath instead. Of course Rio would show up. Because God forbid she had one moment of peace and quiet to gather her thoughts. No. This girl never missed an opportunity to dig her claws into her.

"I wish could say the same about certain students," Agatha replied coldly, pressing the lid of the dry ice box shut with an audible snap and turning to look at Rio, whose expression was calm, bemused, and annoyingly at ease.

“Maybe thats fair,” Rio said with a small laugh, stepping closer as the smirk landed back on her face. “But you don’t seem to mind students with a little backbone.”

Agatha crossed her arms, fixing Rio with a glare. “It’s only tolerable in moderation,” she retorted, raising her eyebrow. “Excessive backtalk usually indicates a lack of respect.”

“Or,” Rio countered, with that maddening glint in her eyes, “it might mean someone respects you enough to be honest.” She leaned back against the counter, crossing her own arms in a mirror of Agatha’s stance. “But I get it. Not everyone is used to being looked in the eye.”

Agatha felt a prick of irritation, and something else, less familiar. She held Rio’s gaze, unwilling to let this girl get the upper hand yet again. “You assume I’d want honesty from someone who barely knows her own place.”

Rio tilted her head, clearly enjoying this. “I’d say I know exactly where my place is,” she said softly. “Maybe it’s you who’s unsure.”

Agatha’s stomach tightened. She felt her patience fraying, the typical shields that guarded her composure slipping. “I suggest you choose your words more carefully,” she said, her voice low.

But Rio only held her gaze, unflinching. “I just think it’s interesting, that’s all,” she said, tilting her head ever so slightly.

Agatha let out a scoff. “If you spent half as much time on your research as you do in this futile attempt to read me.. or whatever it is you’re trying to do here, you would have serious potential.”

Rio raised an eyebrow. “I am very serious about my work. I thought you might’ve realised that by now, but maybe you’re just too busy watching me to see it.”

The nerve on this girl. Agatha felt heat flare in her cheeks, and she looked away, grabbing for her clipboard. “Let me make something very clear,” she said, her voice low. “I don’t watch you. I evaluate your work, just as I do for any other student. You’re not special.”

Rio’s smile softened, almost a whisper of amusement, but her eyes were sharper than ever. “I didn’t say I was special,” she replied. “But whatever it is you’re doing, watching me… it goes both ways, you know?”

Agatha felt a shiver run down her spine, as if Rio’s words had peeled back something she hadn’t wanted to face. She forced herself to meet Rio’s gaze, steady and unwavering. “Why don’t you pay closer attention to your own work, rather than reading into my actions Vidal.”

Rio chuckled softly, and to Agatha’s annoyance, it wasn’t mocking or defiant; it was as if she’d heard something she’d been waiting for. “Believe me, I’m paying attention,” she said, her voice barely above a murmur. “But not just to the work.”

A silence fell over them, thick and unyielding. Agatha couldn’t form a response, her mind snagged on Rio’s words, the steady weight of her gaze. She wanted to dismiss her, to put Rio back in her place with a snide remark or cutting reprimand, but the words didn’t come.

Finally, after God knows how long, Agatha pulled her thoughts together enough to snap “Is there something you need, Rio?” her tone sharper than intended. “Or are you here just to bother me?”

Rio’s gaze fell to the tray in front of Agatha. “Is this a new brain donation?”

Agatha gave a curt nod, letting her gaze drift momentarily to the formalin-soaked bucket. “Yes. A woman with advanced Alzheimer’s,” she replied, her voice steady. She thought for a second, an idea springing to her mind “We should actually cut some new slides from this one for our project.”

Rio’s eyes met Agatha’s with an uncharacteristically hopeful look. Her voice betraying a hint of excitement. “This is the kind of work I’ve always wanted to be part of.” she said, her voice brimming with sincerity. “I’ve finished with all the notes for the new slides… Do you think I could help with the dissection?”

Agatha paused, weighing her answer carefully. She rarely let students assist with this stage of the process. But something in Rio’s expression was resolute, hungry. Against her usual reservations, she found herself nodding. “All right. Start by opening that bucket,” she said, gesturing to the container of formalin.

Rio moved forward, snapping on a pair of gloves before gripping the lid of the bucket and twisting it off with a smooth, practiced motion. Agatha’s eyes drifted, despite herself, to the way the muscles in Rio’s forearm tensed under where she had rolled the sleeves of her lab coat up. The steady efficiency with which she handled the materials was unexpected, almost impressive.

She forced her gaze back to the tray, refocusing on the task at hand.

They worked side by side in silence, at first with Rio taking the bits of brain Agatha sliced and placing them carefully in the corresponding bags. Agatha watched her out of the corner of her eye, noting the way Rio’s fingers moved deftly over the bags, marking each one with the case number and brain region.

After a few minutes, Agatha risked another glance over as Rio scribbled a case number on one of the bags, looking utterly focused, almost gleeful. Her face lit with genuine interest buzzing just below her steady concentration. There was a bright energy about her that was hard to ignore.

Against her own instincts, Agatha felt herself asking. “Would you like to make the next cut?”

Rio’s head snapped up, her face registering shock, her usual smirk replaced by a delighted grin. “Really?”

“Yes,” Agatha said, her tone softened slightly. “Go ahead.”

Rio’s surprise melted into a small, eager smile as she took the scalpel. With a focused precision, she guided the blade down the tissue, making clean, careful cuts. Agatha watched her hands move, admiring the careful way Rio handled the instrument. Steady, exact.

Then her gaze drifted upward, almost unconsciously, to Rio’s face. Her expression was one of pure, unfiltered passion, her eyes sparkling with concentration and fascination. There was something genuine there, a spark that softened Rio’s features, making her look younger, more vulnerable.

When Rio finally set down the scalpel, her gaze lifted to meet Agatha’s. Agatha nodded approvingly, forcing herself to pull back to her usual professional tone. “Well done,” she said, feeling an unexpected warmth in her words. “You’ve got a good hand for this.

Rio’s smile was small but undeniably proud, and Agatha found herself momentarily lost in the warmth of it, so far from their usual back and forth teasing. A rare moment of sincerity and understanding that passed between them.

chapter 7

Chapter Notes

u guys this is 100% my fav chapter ive written so far im so excited for yall to read it !!

lmk what u thinkk in the comments <3

See the end of the chapter for more notes

After boxing up the fresh brain samples for the freezer and returning the bucket to the shelves, Agatha sent Rio off to fill in some admin forms for the new donation.

She returned to her office, ready to dive back into her own work.

A few solid, productive hours passed, the kind of focus that only pure, uninterrupted quiet could bring. Agatha managed to make significant headway on her paper, her thoughts running sharp and clear, until her phone began buzzing insistently.

The caller ID made her stomach drop: Mother.

If people thought Agatha was cold, ruthless, and unyielding, well, Evanora Harkness was a masterclass in those qualities, sharpened into a weapon. Agatha’s personal policy was to avoid her as much as possible, but that didn’t stop Evanora from reaching out every few months. The routine was always the same: a few clipped questions about Agatha’s life, a bit of forced interest, followed by an all-too-familiar descent into disappointment and disdain.

“You’re wasting your life, Agatha. Chasing science, in that godless place,” her mother had said this time, her voice brittle with frustration. “You’re nearing forty five. No husband, no children. Not a single person who’ll give a damn about you in the end. And all because you thought you were too good for the life I gave you. Too good to stay here, too good to be a proper wife. Do you even know what people back home say about you?”

It was exhausting.

Agatha’s responses had been mechanical, worn down over years of the same conversation. But despite herself, the words crept under her skin, burrowing into those quiet, vulnerable places she preferred to pretend didn’t exist.

The worst part was the moment of hesitation, the flicker of doubt that she could never quite shake. What if, on some level, her mother could be right? What if all her accomplishments meant nothing in the end?

By the time she hung up, her jaw was clenched, and her hands shook just slightly. She reached into her bag, fishing out a pack of cigarettes she’d stashed at the very bottom, a leftover habit she’d mostly kicked years ago, but in moments like this, she didn’t even bother to fight the pull. Could you really blame her?

She shoved the pack into her coat pocket and slipped on her coat. She made her way through the lab, moving purposefully through the building toward the side door that opened to an alley.

Agatha stepped out into the darkness, the sharp chill of the evening air greeting her immediately. She reached into her coat pocket, pulling out the pack of cigarettes she’d shoved in there earlier, her fingers brushing the edges of the crumpled foil. She was about to take one out when a voice came from behind her.

“Wouldn’t have pegged you as a smoker, Dr Harkness.”

Agatha’s heart skipped a beat, and she froze for just a moment before turning around. There, standing just a few feet behind her, was Rio, her face illuminated by a nearby streetlamp. She was leaning casually against the wall, a cigarette dangling between her fingers, smoke curling up around her face in the cold air.

Agatha raised an eyebrow, her lips curling into a subtle, disbelieving smile. “Why not?” she asked, her voice almost cool, despite the slight flicker of irritation that stirred within her.

Rio’s smirk widened, her gaze flicking down to the pack in Agatha’s hand, then back up to meet her eyes. “Well, you’re a world-famous medical researcher,” she said, her tone teasing. “I would’ve thought you’d have more respect for your body than that.”

Agatha scoffed, shaking her head “I could say the same to you,” she retorted, gesturing at the cigarette Rio was holding.

Rio’s grin didn’t falter. “Fair point,” she said with a casual shrug, the smoke lazily drifting around her as she took another drag.

The two stood in silence for a moment, the air between them heavy and thick, their breath misting in the cold. The world around them seemed to hold its breath for just a second, as if time itself was suspended.

Agatha finally broke the silence with a hollow laugh. “I’m not a smoker. Not anymore at least,” she admitted, the words almost slipping out before she could stop them. “But when my mother decides to call… I need something to take the edge off.”

Rio’s eyes softened, though her smirk remained as she nodded her head in response. She didn’t say anything, just watched Agatha as she pulled out a cigarette from the pack and placed it between her lips. She rummaged in her bag, muttering under her breath.

“Fuck,” she hissed, frustration creeping into her voice. She must’ve forgotten her lighter at home. Typical , she thought bitterly. The one day I need it, and I forget my fucking lighter.

Absorbed in her annoyance, Agatha didn’t notice Rio moving closer, her footsteps soft on the cold ground. She only looked up as Rio was stood right in front of her. Their gazes locked, a smirk playing on Rio’s lips as she pulled a lighter from her pocket, flicking it open with a smooth, practiced motion.

Agatha’s breath caught in her throat, her pulse quickening as Rio stepped even closer, almost too close. Rio’s eyes never left hers as she brought the flame to Agatha’s mouth, the red sparks dancing in Agatha’s peripheral vision as the flame flickered. Agatha’s breath hitched in her chest, the air between them suddenly feeling unbearably charged, every second stretching on for what felt like an eternity.

Finally, Agatha inhaled the smoke, the sharp, bitter taste starting to fill her lungs as Rio pulled the lighter away. She didn’t know what had possessed her to let Rio get so close, but she couldn’t seem to bring herself to care in the moment. All she could focus on was the weight of Rio’s gaze, the way she felt impossibly present in that shared space, as if every small movement between them held meaning.

Agatha let out the breath, the mist of smoke rising in the cold air, her chest tight and full in a way she couldn’t explain. The moment lingered, hanging between them, just as taut as the tension in the lab that seemed to follow them both everywhere. Rio remained close, still watching her, and for a heartbeat, neither of them moved.

"Thanks," Agatha muttered, her voice quieter than before. She quickly pulled the cigarette away from her lips, looking anywhere but at Rio.

Rio watched her for a moment as she stepped to the side, the quiet stretching on longer than it should have. Finally, she asked, her tone softer than usual, “Are you okay?”

Agatha flicked her gaze back to Rio, not expecting the question. It wasn’t like her to ask, especially in such a gentle manner. “Do you… want to talk about your mother?” Rio added, her voice just a touch hesitant.

Agatha took a long drag from the cigarette, exhaling slowly, her chest tightening. She shook her head, forcing a tight smile that didn’t quite reach her eyes. “No, it’s fine. I’m fine. She’s just the usual crazy religious insane woman. Hates me for not having children. Hates me for not liking men. Hates me for choosing a career over becoming a mindless housewife, for leaving home and moving to London.” She paused to scoff bitterly, her lips curling into a wry smile, fingers tightening around the cigarette. “Anyway, I’m over it by now. She does this every few months. Same old rant. It’s just…” she paused, taking another long drag “Exhausting.”

Agatha didn’t realize she’d said so much until the words were already out. She immediately regretted it, her usual control slipping, leaving her feeling exposed in front of Rio. She quickly tried to backtrack, her voice turning more guarded. “I’m sorry, I shouldn’t be talking about this with you. It’s unprofessional.”

Rio didn’t say anything at first, but her eyes softened, her gaze a little more understanding than before. After a moment, she took another drag from her own cigarette, then flicked the ash away, her expression thoughtful. “You know,” she said casually, but with a touch of something more serious beneath the words, “You’re allowed to have moments where it gets to you. Doesn’t matter how much you’ve moved on. Sometimes it just hurts, right?”

Agatha was quiet for a moment, not quite meeting Rio’s gaze, but she could feel the weight of the words hanging in the air. She let the smoke curl from her lips, watching it drift up and disappear into the cold sky.

After a few seconds, Rio spoke up again, “I get it. Family can be a mess. Honestly, your mom sounds like a fucking piece of work.”

Agatha’s eyes flicked back to her, surprised by Rio’s response.

“Yeah, she really is,” Agatha said, her voice quieter now, the edge of frustration slipping away. “She’s... relentless. But I guess it doesn’t matter anymore. I’ve stopped letting it get to me. Mostly.”

There was a pause, and Agatha found herself looking at Rio, taking in the way her lips curled around the cigarette between her fingers. For a moment, it was like everything else faded away. She’d spent so much time keeping her guard up, but something about the ease in Rio’s presence made it feel like maybe, just maybe, it was okay to let that guard drop.

“Well, if you ever need to talk, I’m here,” Rio said, the playful glint in her eyes returning. “I’ve got an endless supply of sarcastic commentary and terrible advice. I’m practically a professional at that.”

Agatha snorted, the smallest laugh escaping her lips. “You don’t say.” She glanced at Rio, half-amused, half-surprised by the unexpected comfort in her words. “I’ll keep that in mind. Though I can’t imagine your advice would be very… professional .”

Rio’s smirk widened. “I’m great at giving advice no one should ever actually follow. It's a talent.” She took another long drag from her cigarette, her eyes glinting with that familiar mischievousness. “But really, if you need a distraction, I’m all for some less... emotionally heavy topics. Like, you know, your impressive lack of respect for your own health.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow, already distracted from the knot of emotions her mother had stirred up. “I told you, I’m not a smoker,” she said with a smirk. “This is just… a temporary lapse in judgment.”

Rio’s grin grew wider. “Ok sure, I believe you.” She paused for a second to look Agatha up and down, lowering her voice, “So, what other temporary lapses in judgment do you have, Dr. Harkness?”

Agatha’s breath hitched as Rio’s eyes raked over her. She had to take a second to collect herself before rolling her eyes in mock annoyance. "Nothing concerning you," she replied dryly, flicking the cigarette to the ground and stomping it out beneath her heel.

Rio’s smirk grew somehow even wider. She hummed as her tongue ran along her teeth. “Uh-huh. Sure. But say it like you mean it this time.”

Rio’s laugh was easy, full of that youthful irreverence that Agatha had, for reasons she couldn’t entirely explain, come to enjoy. It was strange, the way Rio could make her feel like she was standing just a little outside her own rigid control. Like maybe it wasn’t so bad to let someone see past the walls she’d built so carefully.

The cold air between them seemed a little less biting now, the tension from earlier easing with the exchange. Rio flicked her cigarette away, and for a moment, they both just stood there, letting the silence settle in a way that didn’t feel awkward but rather… peaceful. Agatha realised that, for the first time in a while, she wasn’t desperate to fill the space with words, or with some kind of control.

Rio looked over at her, as if noticing the same shift. "So," she began, voice low but not without its usual spark, "You ever regret it? Leaving home, I mean."

Agatha blinked, caught off guard by the question. She tilted her head, considering it. “Regret?” she repeated, her voice tinged with uncertainty. She hadn’t really allowed herself to think about it, not like that. Not in such a simple, pointed way. “I don’t know if regret is the word.”

She paused, feeling an unexpected wave of exhaustion wash over her. She didn’t want to get into it again. Didn’t want to explore the moments of doubt that always seemed to sneak in when she thought about her family. But Rio wasn’t asking for some dramatic confession, it seemed.

Rio was just… asking.

“I think," Agatha continued after a long pause, "I think I just felt like I had to. I had to get out. I couldn’t keep pretending I was okay with the life they wanted for me." She glanced at Rio, as if gauging her reaction. “Does that make sense?”

Rio nodded, her expression quiet for a second, and Agatha almost wondered if she was getting too personal. But then Rio spoke again, her voice low, almost thoughtful. “Yeah, it makes sense. I think... if I stayed where I grew up, I’d lose myself. Everyone expects you to be someone else. To fit into some box, you know?”

Agatha looked at her, genuinely surprised by the honesty in Rio’s words. She hadn’t expected that kind of reflection, not from someone who always carried herself with so much confidence, almost like nothing ever rattled her. But maybe she was wrong about Rio. Maybe Rio understood more than she let on.

The thought settled on Agatha like a gentle weight, something unfamiliar but strangely welcome.

“Exactly.” Agatha admitted, her voice softer now. She could feel a shift within her, a brief opening she hadn’t realised she’d needed. “But it’s interesting, to hear it from you. I just always assumed people like you… you have it all figured out.”

Rio’s lips quirked in a half-smile, the usual playful edge to her expression returning. “Oh, I definitely don’t have it all figured out,” she said. “But I’ve learned the hard way that pretending to be what everyone else wants you to be doesn’t exactly bring happiness. Or peace. And if you can’t find that, what’s the point?”

Agatha took in the words, feeling a flicker of something in her chest. A flicker of recognition. It felt strange, how easy it was to talk to Rio in that moment. She had always kept things so compartmentalised, so guarded. But Rio didn’t push, didn’t judge. She simply listened, offering her own kind of unspoken understanding.

The moment hung there between them, but as it faded, Agatha felt herself retreating, slipping back into the familiar armour she wore when she wanted to distance herself from anything too personal, too messy.

"Well, I should probably get back to the lab," Agatha said, the words coming out a little more abruptly than she intended. "There’s still work to do, and I’m sure you have plenty of your own to finish."

Rio’s smirk softened for a second, “Yeah, I guess,” she said, exhaling a final cloud of smoke. “But hey, I wouldn’t mind sticking around for a bit longer. You know, in case you need any more terrible advice.”

She gave a small nod, her expression neutral. “Maybe,” Agatha said, the word surprisingly soft as she met Rio’s eyes. “I’ll think about it.”

Rio raised an eyebrow, a hint of surprise flickering across her face. “Wow. Thinking about it?” she teased, her voice light, though there was something warmer behind her usual playfulness. “You must be really on edge if you’re actually considering human interaction.”

Agatha’s lips quirked into a faint smile. "Don’t get used to it," she replied dryly, though the edges of her smile lingered.

Rio chuckled, tossing the last of her cigarette to the ground and stubbing it out. “I’ll take that as a maybe.”

Agatha paused, her hand resting on the door handle as she turned back toward Rio. There was a moment of hesitation. This was crazy, right? Her boundaries had completely blurred. Rio was supposed to be her student, their relationship was supposed to be strictly professional. She definitely should not be sharing details of her personal life, or taking advice from her. Still, Agatha found herself almost… considering it.

She glanced back, feeling the weight of her own hesitation before the words slipped out. “Actually, do you still have that lighter out?” She tried for nonchalance. “I might need another before I can go back inside.”

Rio’s eyebrows arched in surprise, and a slow smirk crept over her face. “Oh, and who’s ‘not a smoker’ now, huh?”

Agatha huffed lightly as she walked back out into the alley, a faint exhale that was more of a stall than an answer. She pulled another cigarette from the pack, her fingers only slightly less steady this time. She leaned against the brick wall behind her as she positioned it between her lips, noticing the way Rio’s gaze dipped down, catching on her mouth with just the briefest flicker. It was subtle, almost imperceptible, something she could have easily brushed off, but Agatha felt it like a spark.

She really should have learned the first time. She should have just asked Rio to hand her the lighter and lit the damn thing herself. Because as soon as Rio leaned in close again, Agatha felt herself completely forget every rule, every boundary she had ever learned. She didn't need this, didn’t need the steady heat of Rio’s presence blurring every line of professionalism. But then Rio stepped forward, the lighter catching in her hand, and Agatha’s heart beat just a fraction faster.

This time, Agatha barely noticed the flame as it sparked between them; her focus was locked on Rio’s eyes, unwavering and steady as she held the lighter close. Agatha leaned forward, inhaling just a little too quickly as Rio kept her gaze trained on her, an intensity there that felt almost electric. Smoke filled her lungs and the warmth between them lingered as she leant her head back, letting it rest against the cold brick behind her. She closed her eyes, focusing on the rhythm of her breathing as she tilted her face up to the sky.

But even with her eyes shut, she could feel Rio watching her. It was unmistakable, that heat lingering on her skin, tracing the exposed curve of her neck. It took every ounce of her composure to keep her breath steady as she opened her eyes again. And sure enough, there was Rio, who hadn’t stepped back at all. Hadn’t moved an inch.

Agatha should feel trapped. She was backed against the wall, Rio barely an inch away from her. But instead all she could focus on was the tingling heat between them, both grounding and disorienting.

Her breath caught, a shiver running down her spine as she felt Rio’s hand shift, slipping the lighter back into her pocket. But her gaze stayed locked on Agatha’s mouth, lingering in a way that was undeniably close, undeniably unprofessional.

“...Rio,” Agatha murmured, the word barely a breath as it left her lips, betraying her more than she’d meant it to.

Rio’s gaze lifted, catching hers with that same steady, knowing look, a smirk hovering at the corner of her mouth.

“Agatha.” she replied, her voice rich with something unspoken, something neither of them were quite naming yet.

Agatha blinked, momentarily thrown by the way her name sounded in Rio’s voice. Casual, intimate, as if the usual formality between them didn’t exist. It was bold, almost infuriating, that she had used her first name. But there was something else there, too, something Agatha couldn’t quite bring herself to resent. Instead, the sound of her name left a warm, unfamiliar weight in her chest, unsettling and strangely… endearing.

Rio took one more half-step forward, her coat brushing against Agatha’s. Slowly, Rio’s hand lifted, reaching up as if it were the most natural thing in the world, her fingers brushing against Agatha’s cheek as she tucked a loose strand of hair behind her ear.

Agatha felt herself leaning into the touch, just a fraction, her eyes fluttering shut for a second as she felt a warmth spreading through her that she knew she shouldn’t feel. She forced her eyes open just as Rio’s gaze flicked down to her mouth again, her eyes lingering as if drawn by some invisible pull.

Agatha’s heart thundered as she felt the same pull, an ache she could feel in the pit of her stomach. But then, clarity struck, sharp and sudden. This was a mess waiting to happen. This was crazy. Reckless.

She straightened, mustering enough control to pull herself back, her head nearly hitting the wall with how fast she withdrew. “I really do need to be getting back to the lab.” The words came out shaky, breathless. Nowhere near the composed dismissal she’d intended.

Rio let out a quiet, almost indulgent laugh, her amusement soft but palpable as Agatha took a step to the side. “Fine, as you wish,” Rio murmured, stepping back as well, voice light but threaded with that same knowing warmth. “You’re welcome for the light. And the terrible advice.” She took a final drag from her cigarette, exhaling slowly, smoke curling in the air between them. “See you tomorrow, Dr. Harkness.”

The way she emphasised the title made Agatha’s breath catch, something about the mocking glint in Rio’s eye reminding her just how close she’d let things get. She gave a short nod, barely trusting herself to say anything further, and turned toward the door.

Her hand shook as she turned the handle and slipped back inside, the cold already fading in the warmth of the lab, but the buzz in her chest lingering stubbornly.

Chapter Notes

i have been procrastinating aaallll of my actual work and just writing this fic instead so heres the next chapterr!! hope u enjoyyy <3

See the end of the chapter for more notes

The early morning air was cool and dense in Agatha’s apartment as she moved through her routine, each step intentionally slow, as if stretching out the motions would allow her to regain control over the thoughts slipping away from her. She walked over to the kitchen counter, grabbing her thermos and carefully pouring coffee from the pot. The sharp, bitter aroma filled the air, but it did little to clear her mind. Rio’s words from last night lingered there, blurring the line between memory and something Agatha refused to name.

"What other temporary lapses in judgment do you have, Dr. Harkness?" Rio had asked, voice low, nearly touching her skin.

Agatha could still feel the heat of Rio’s breath, close enough that if she’d leaned in even a fraction more, their lips would have met.

The almost-kiss. A momentary, irrational impulse that had seized her without warning, leaving her breathless and unsteady. Agatha shook her head, forcing herself to focus, but the words the memory, only burrowed in deeper.

It was a lapse in judgment. A temporary lapse in judgement. Exactly as Rio had said. She had been emotional and vulnerable in that moment and had seen support in Rio. Sure, maybe her thoughts had gotten a little muddled in the process, but all she had wanted was comfort. And that was all it was, she told herself firmly, pouring coffee into her thermos with sharp, precise movements.

She didn’t know what had come over her. Well, she did know, and it was only a reminder of why she needed to keep her distance, keep this professional, strictly about the science. Not that Rio would make it easy.

Her apartment was a sanctuary of clean lines and calm spaces, her own carefully crafted retreat. But even in the quiet of her flat, she couldn’t escape the moment that replayed in her mind. She had bought it years ago after her first major promotion, just months after she had left home and started her climb up the career ladder. At the time, it was a triumph that had felt hollow without her mother there to see it.

A two-bedroom in Kensington, spacious by London standards, with high ceilings and sleek, clean lines. The floor-to-ceiling windows in the living room usually cast a golden glow over the plush rug and carefully curated bookshelves, a view that overlooked the bustling high street below. But in the early autumn morning, the windows stood in inky darkness, reflecting only the dim light of her bedside lamp and the quiet sophistication of the space she had so meticulously crafted.

Finally ready, Agatha gathered her things and stepped out, locking the door behind her. She moved through the familiar streets, the early morning quiet only broken by the faint rumble of distant traffic. She descended into the Tube station, thoughts already cycling through her long list of tasks. Today, she had a full agenda: gather the students, get updates on their project ideas, prepare them for the next phase of their research. She wanted them to be sharp, even if she wasn’t directly involved in each project like she was for Rio’s. Today she also had a session with the students for her own research; she'd decided to skip her usual lecture and instead put them to work on some tasks she needed done. With Rio’s project picking up soon, it was going to take up a lot of her time. She didn’t want her own publication to suffer; she’d need to find some balance.

By the time she stepped off the tube, the city was waking up, the air brisk as she climbed the steps back into daylight. She cut through familiar streets, quickly entering the lab building.

Agatha strode through the hall, her heels echoing in the early quiet. She pushed open the door to the common room, her gaze scanning for each of her students. Her gaze stopped on Rio first, whose eyes lifted the instant Agatha entered, her gaze meeting Agatha's with a boldness that left Agatha unexpectedly breathless.

The memory of last night came rushing back. Rio’s brown eyes fixed on her lips, Rio's face close to hers. What almost happened in the smoky dark, what could have happened if she just had a little less self control. She felt an uncomfortable twist in her chest. Agatha quickly forced her gaze away, collecting herself with a quiet breath.

Rio sat with a casual poise, that infuriating smirk already in place. The slightest tilt of her brow as if she knew exactly what Agatha was thinking. She felt an uncomfortable twist in her chest. Agatha quickly forced her gaze away, collecting herself with a quiet breath.

She addressed her students curtly, gesturing for them to begin with their project updates. “Billy, you’re up. Let’s hear it.”

Billy swallowed, looking briefly down at his notes before launching into his update. “Ok, um, for my project I’m studying Tau protein as a biomarker for Alzheimer’s,” he began, his voice wavering just slightly. “Tau tangles are a hallmark of the disease, but they’re usually only detected in postmortem tissue. I’m working on a protocol to track Tau in living patients, using spinal fluid samples.” He glanced at her for a sign of approval, but Agatha remained expressionless. “If we can establish a reliable marker for Tau in the early stages, we could identify Alzheimer’s risk much earlier and maybe even monitor how well therapies are working.”

Agatha raised a brow, waiting a beat before pouncing. “And what are the limitations of measuring Tau in spinal fluid? What other variables could interfere with your findings?” she asked, her tone sharp.

Agatha liked to grill her students on their presentations. Sure, anyone could preset a neat, prepared speech when it was all written in front of them. But their ability to adapt when they were pushed, that was what showed real knowledge. Real understanding.

Billy shifted, searching for an answer. “Well, uh, other proteins in the fluid could create noise in the sample, making it difficult to isolate Tau specifically…” He trailed off.

Agatha gave a slow nod. “And how do you plan to mitigate those effects?”

Billy’s cheeks flushed, and he swallowed hard before managing, “I have plans to work on a filtering protocol that I think could help improve specificity.”

“Make sure you do,” she said coolly, moving on. “Alice, your turn.”

Alice looked down briefly at her notes, gathering her thoughts, before speaking. “My research is on dopamine pathways in Parkinson’s disease.” She glanced up, her voice growing steadier. “There’s so much degeneration by the time symptoms appear that it’s difficult to understand which pathways might be driving early symptoms. I’m working on identifying subtle pathway changes that occur right before symptoms start. The goal is to isolate any indicators that might lead to earlier diagnosis, or even targeted therapies.”

Agatha tapped her fingers thoughtfully on the table. “So, what makes you confident that these changes will show up before symptoms begin? What if what you’re seeing is just normal neural variation?”

Alice stiffened, a flicker of doubt flashing across her face, but she managed a response. “I’ll compare data from early-stage Parkinson’s patients with control groups. Collect preliminary evidence to see any patterns. But you’re right; there’s a chance the variation may not be abnormal, so I’m considering alternative explanations as I go.”

“Good,” Agatha replied, her gaze softening just slightly. “Keep challenging your assumptions.” She turned to Jen. “Jen, you’re up. Let’s hear it.”

Jen took a breath, looking at Agatha directly, the quiet determination in her eyes catching Agatha’s attention. “My project focuses on the CAG repeat expansions in the HTT gene - the mutation responsible for Huntington’s disease,” she began, her voice calm. “The number of these repeats directly correlates with disease onset and severity, but there's still a lot to understand about the underlying mechanism.” She paused to glance at her notes, then continued, “I’m exploring how different lengths of CAG repeats impact early gene expression changes, especially in the brain regions affected first by the disease. By identifying these changes, I hope to clarify some mechanisms of disease progression and potentially uncover a few early markers for intervention.”

Agatha leaned forward, pressing her fingers together. “What makes you think these gene expressions will be significant enough to act as markers? Isn’t it likely the effect is too subtle to detect?”

Jen’s answer came without hesitation. “The changes are subtle, yes, but previous studies show that even small expression shifts can be amplified over time in these regions, eventually impacting entire pathways. I’ve been using sequencing techniques, which are showing some promising early trends.”

Agatha was momentarily taken aback. She leaned back, arching a brow, testing her further. “And how do you plan to differentiate those early markers from secondary effects? Isn’t there a risk of confusing causation with correlation?”

Jen’s eyes sparked with quiet confidence. “I’ve designed the study to track expression changes longitudinally, so I’ll be able to compare baseline levels with the changes that emerge over time. This should help isolate causative markers from downstream effects.” She looked at Agatha, unflinching, as if inviting her to challenge her further.

For a second, Agatha felt a flicker of admiration. Jen was showing real promise, a keen attention to detail. Perhaps she’d misjudged her.

Finally, she turned toward Rio, who was watching her with that same unshakable intensity that made her breath hitch for a moment. She cleared her throat. “Rio, you’re next.”

Rio shifted in her seat, that familiar glint in her eye as she looked at Agatha, as if they were about to start a game only the two of them understood. She held Agatha’s gaze, unbothered, and began her presentation.

“My… or I guess our project is a cross-sectional study of epilepsy and Alzheimer’s pathology,” she said, pausing briefly to correct her language, but her voice was steady and deliberate.

“We’ll be using stained brain tissue slides from Alzheimer’s patients, epilepsy patients, and—” she leaned forward slightly, her voice dropping a fraction “a subset of Alzheimer’s patients who had also experienced seizures. By analysing these specific groups, we aim to see if seizure activity accelerates the usual progression of Alzheimer’s.”

Agatha folded her arms, feigning boredom, though her mind was already evaluating Rio’s composure. Confident as always, Agatha thought, with a flicker of begrudging respect that annoyed her, as well as a churning in her stomach that lately had seemed to appear every time she was in Rio’s presence. “And what’s the control for seizure activity? How do you intend to separate correlation from causation?”

Rio smirked, meeting Agatha’s gaze directly, an unflinching spark in her eyes. “We’ll use standard staining methods on each slide to mark Tau proteins. By comparing slides from Alzheimer’s patients with and without a history of seizures, we can see whether additional Tau build-up is truly caused by seizure activity.” Her eyes gleamed as she continued, “Of course, if it’s causative, I’m sure you’ll let me take credit for that breakthrough, Dr. Harkness.” Rio chimed, with an overdramatic batting of her eyelashes.

A faint, involuntary laugh escaped Agatha, though she quickly masked it with a critical look and an eye roll. “Don’t count on it, Vidal. Now, tell me, if the effect of seizures is our target, what exactly do you think tracking Tau deposits will add to the analysis?”

Rio’s expression was unyielding, her tone brimming with mock innocence. “Well, Dr Harkness, as I’m sure any first-year neuroscience student could tell you, a deposit of Tau proteins in the hippocampus is the main physical marker of Alzheimer’s disease.” She kept her gaze locked with Agatha’s as she added, “So, we’ll see if there is increased Tau deposition in patients who’ve had seizures, to see if the seizure stress triggers the degeneration in Alzheimer’s.”

Agatha’s jaw tightened as she struggled to maintain her composure under Rio’s relentless focus, but a reluctant admiration was growing under her frustration. She knows her shit, Agatha admitted, annoyed at how effortlessly Rio was handling her questions. “And what about the sampling issues? The slides we’ll be using are all from different points in the disease progression, will that not effect the validity of our findings?”

“You have a point.” Rio’s expression never wavered. “That’s why I’m proposing we categorise them by the stage their Alzheimer’s was when they died and analyse each subset individually. It’s ambitious, sure, but I assumed you’d appreciate that. The rigour.” Her smirk was challenging, as if daring Agatha to argue.

Agatha raised a brow, letting out a hum of begrudging agreement. “And how do you plan to control for damage to the brain cells from the preservation process? The staining alone could skew our data.”

Rio shrugged, casual as ever, as if she’d anticipated every question. “Not if we’re careful. I’ll prepare fresh sections from the highest-quality samples and validate against controls before running our analysis. But I could always consult the esteemed Dr. Harkness for her expertise, if she’s interested.” Her tone was suggestive, with a glimmer that sent a rush of heat up Agatha’s spine.

Agatha’s chest tightened, though she hid her reaction with a sharp reply. “As I’ve said repeatedly, Vidal, flattery will get you nowhere.” It felt like she and Rio were the only ones in the room. “So, what’s your final hypothesis, then?” she asked, almost daring her to trip up.

Rio leaned in slightly, her gaze narrowing, as if this were a private challenge between them. “I hypothesise that the presence of seizure-induced stress accelerates the progression of Alzheimer’s disease. Is that all fine with you, Dr. Harkness?” Her words were almost a whisper, slow and charged with something she knew would set Agatha on edge.

Agatha inhaled sharply, ignoring the tingling warmth that Rio’s gaze sparked. She knows what she’s doing, she thought, both irritated and impressed. She glanced around the room, finally aware of the other students, all wide-eyed and silent, trying to make sense of the tension that thickened the air. She cleared her throat, fixing her gaze on Rio with a detached, professional look that took much more effort to conjure than she cared to admit.

“Very well, Vidal,” she said, voice tight, her pulse still quicker than it should have been. “Let’s hope you can back up that theory with results.”

Rio’s smirk deepened as Agatha finished, and for a moment, there was a charged silence in the room. Then Rio leaned back, her gaze never wavering. “Let’s hope we can back up the theory with results,” she said, a slight challenge in her voice. “Remember, Dr. Harkness, you’re just as involved in this as me.”

Agatha felt her cheeks flush, heat prickling at her skin as she struggled to keep her expression neutral. The gall of this girl, reminding Agatha of her own stake in the project. Of how their work was now bound together inextricably. She cleared her throat, willing herself to stay composed, yet couldn’t help but feel a flicker of something unsettling and thrilling.

“Don’t forget your place, Vidal,” she said curtly, but the words lacked the bite she intended. All she saw was Rio’s steady, amused gaze, as though daring her to admit that, in this, they were equals.

Agatha straightened, fixing her gaze on the group as a whole. "Okay. I'm impressed with everyone’s project ideas; there’s some real potential here. You have up to two years to work on this research," she said, her tone brisk, professional. "I’ll be checking in regularly, and I want written updates each month. For the next few weeks, I recommend you start by drafting equipment lists, detailing what slides or samples you’ll need to study, and submit them to the lab admins who’ll get it sorted for you. You can go grab lunch now if you’d like, but I expect to see you back in the lab in half an hour for my session. You’ll all be assisting with my research."

She turned to refill her thermos with coffee, a familiar ritual that gave her a moment to collect herself. She could hear them beginning to file out, shuffling footsteps moving toward the door.

No, Agatha thought with a sigh. If there’s one thing I know about Rio Vidal, it’s that she loves to linger where she isn’t needed. Or wanted, she added mentally, though she was having trouble convincing herself that last part was true. But why would she want Rio to stay? She’d already challenged her enough for the day. This was purely aggravating. Right?

She poured the coffee with her back still turned, her voice coming out sharper than intended. “You’re still here, aren’t you?”

“Why did you ask me so many questions?” Rio’s voice came from just behind her, a low murmur that carried a hint of amusement. “You only asked the others one or two, yet the project you already know the most about… you suddenly had all the questions in the world.”

Agatha scoffed, feigning indifference as she stirred sugar into her coffee. “My job to push you. To test your limits.” She glanced over her shoulder, hoping she looked unbothered. Rio met her gaze with a look of cool challenge, her expression unreadable, save for the slight curve of her mouth.

Rio tilted her head slightly, the hint of a smirk on her lips. “Some people might say it seems like favouritism, Dr. Harkness.” Rio paused, her tone feigning innocence, “Not me of course, but some people.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, suppressing the faint twist of irritation and something else, something she refused to name, as she turned back to her coffee. She felt a rush of heat creep into her cheeks, unbidden, and she kept her gaze firmly on her thermos as she screwed the lid back on. “Vidal, I think you should worry more about our research plan than about whatever nonsense you think is going on in my head.” She hoped the words sounded indifferent, but there was a tension in her voice that made her bite the inside of her cheek as her gaze flitted back up to Rio.

She only raised her eyebrow even further, unperturbed. “’Vidal’. Wow, suddenly we’re so formal? Last night it was Rio’.” she said lightly, lingering in the doorway as if considering saying more.

Agatha turned back to her coffee, taking a steadying breath before screwing the lid onto her thermos. She was about to make some quick reply, something to deflect the tension when she noticed Rio hadn’t moved, hadn’t turned to leave.

A silence stretched between them, uncomfortable and taut, until Rio broke it with a question that froze her in place.

“Are we gonna talk about last night?”

Agatha felt her heart stutter in her chest, her pulse quickening despite herself. She opened her mouth to respond, but no words came, her throat suddenly dry. Seconds passed, thick with unspoken words, as she kept her back to Rio, clinging to the illusion of composure.

Finally, Rio let out a soft chuckle, “Fine. I’ll see you after lunch then…” She paused, dropping her voice, “..Dr Harkness.” her tone teasing but there was a hint of something else as well. Something Agatha didn’t want to think about.

Agatha watched her leave, feeling the air settle uncomfortably in the quiet that followed. The exchange played over in her mind, Rio’s words replaying with that mocking tilt, and the way her own responses had been much less controlled than she’d wanted. She felt an unwelcome sense of intrigue beneath her irritation, and it lingered, unwanted, as she headed back to her office, her grip tightening around her thermos.

Chapter Notes

next chapter yay I lowkey have no clue how im staying so consistent with daily updates ... (I do know. its by procrastinating ALL my uni work)

(also I just made a twt for fic updates!! check endnotes for the @)

See the end of the chapter for more notes

The students were already gathered in the lab when Agatha arrived, their faces a mix of nervous anticipation and determination. Billy was flipping through his notes, Jen was fiddling with a pen, and Alice was adjusting the settings on one of the lab microscopes. Agatha set her bag down with a sense of purpose, surveying the room. She couldn’t help but notice, however, the distinct absence of Rio.

Her voice was sharp and cutting as she asked, “Has anyone seen Vidal?”

The three exchanged uneasy glances. Billy was the first to speak, his voice small. “Uh… no. Not since before lunch.”

Agatha let out a slow sigh, irritation bubbling. Typical. She pinched the bridge of her nose briefly before straightening, her tone brisk. “Fine. We’ll start without her.”

She moved to the middle of the lab, her heels clicking with purpose on the tiled floor. As she turned to face her students, she clasped her hands together. “Today’s session is not just about your own individual projects.” She began, her voice firm and deliberate. “This is about assisting with my research, and the stakes are far higher.”

The room was silent, the weight of her words hanging in the air. She took a step closer, her gaze sweeping across the trio. “Any mistakes you make today, any oversight, any lapse in judgment, will either compromise this groundbreaking research, or it will leave me cleaning up after you. And I assure you, I do not take kindly to either.”

Just as the tension in the room reached its peak, the lab door creaked open. Agatha didn’t have to look to know who it was; the telltale languidness of Rio’s steps gave her away.

“Nice of you to finally join us,” Agatha said coldly, her focus still on the others as she scribbled something in her notebook. She could feel Rio’s gaze, that unrelenting weight of her presence, but she refused to give her the satisfaction of reacting.

Finally, Agatha turned, her expression carefully neutral as she addressed Rio directly. “I was just telling the others how important this work is. How assisting with my research means there are greater consequences than working on your own projects.”

Rio leaned casually against the doorframe, the corner of her mouth twitching up into a smirk. “Oh, of course,” she said, her voice dripping with mock sincerity. “I imagine everything has higher stakes when the infamous Dr. Agatha Harkness is involved.”

Agatha scoffed, narrowing her eyes. “Well,” she said, her tone cool and cutting, “I was also about to say how vital it is that everyone is fully committed and serious about this research. Even more so than their own. But I suppose you’ve already shown me that you couldn’t care less. So, Vidal,” she continued, her gaze sharp, “If you’d rather not be here, I mean, you know where the door is.”

The room went silent, all eyes shifting nervously between the two. Rio’s smirk deepened as she tilted her head as if deep in contemplation, her gaze steady and teasing. “Tempting,” she said, her voice low and playful. “But then who would keep you on your toes, Dr. Harkness?”

Agatha’s jaw tightened, a flush of heat rising to her cheeks despite her best efforts to remain composed. She lifted her chin, fixing Rio with a steely look. “If you’re staying, then I expect you to take this seriously.”

Rio pushed off the doorframe with a lazy shrug. “Of course, Dr. Harkness. You’ve made it very clear how high the stakes are.” Her voice was light, but her eyes gleamed with mischief as she started to move to join the others.

Agatha’s fingers twitched at her sides, the tension simmering just below the surface as she forced herself to return to the task at hand. She ignored the flicker of Rio’s amused expression and turned back to the others. “Let’s begin,” she said sharply, her voice regaining its edge. “This is not a place for distractions.”

Rio raised an eyebrow as she strode further into the room, her steps painstakingly slow and deliberate as Agatha spoke. Her path took her close to Agatha, far closer than necessary, and she paused just long enough as she passed to lean in close to Agatha, her voice a hushed murmur that only Agatha could hear.

“No distractions, hmm?” Rio said, her tone laced with playful defiance. “Well then, maybe I should just…” She gestured lazily toward the door, her lips curving into that maddening smirk.

Agatha’s breath hitched, a sharp intake that betrayed her perfectly composed exterior for a fraction of a second. The nerve. Her thoughts raced, laced with a mix of fury and something she didn’t want to name. How on earth did this girl know the effect she was having? How dare she imply-

Agatha fixed Rio with a glare so sharp it could cut glass. “Will you just be quiet and let me get on with this, Vidal?” she hissed, her voice stern and brimming with authority. Her hand shot out, pointing to the lab bench where the others sat in confusion, pretending not to notice the tension crackling between them.

Rio’s smirk widened into a grin, her delight almost childlike as she took in the fury simmering in Agatha’s eyes. With an exaggerated shrug, she muttered, “Whatever you say, Dr. Harkness,” before sauntering over to the bench. She flopped into a seat, her movements unhurried, and leaned back casually, her smirk so wide she was all but giggling to herself.

Agatha could feel the heat rising to her cheeks, a combination of rage and a far more unwelcome feeling she ruthlessly tamped down. She straightened her spine and returned to the center of the room, doing her best to regain her composure. Behind her, she could hear Rio stifling a laugh, and it only made her irritation grow.

“Now,” Agatha said sharply, her tone carrying more edge than intended. “Let’s get started. I trust we’re all finally ready to focus now.”

Out of the corner of her eye, she caught Rio’s smug grin, and her hand tightened around the pen she was holding. This is going to be a long afternoon.

Agatha cleared her throat, drawing everyone's attention back to her. “All right, listen closely because I’m only going to explain this once,” she began, her voice crisp and commanding. “Your task today is straightforward but vital to this study. We are sorting through autopsy reports of individuals whose brains I have been analysing as part of my research on depression and Alzheimer’s.”

She gestured to a tall stack of neatly organised reports on the counter beside her. “First, you will go through these reports and note down whether each patient was on antidepressants prior to their death.”

“Once that’s done, you will take the case numbers, find the corresponding brain donation, which should be in one of the buckets in the ‘ room of doom’ over there” She pointed to the sliding door at the end of the lab.

“Once you have the brain, you will place it on the scale over there.” She motioned toward the electronic scale on the opposite counter. “Record the weight. It’s a simple, systematic process. Have I made myself clear?”

The students nodded in unison, eager to prove themselves.

“Good. Then get started,” Agatha commanded, gesturing to the reports.

The students scrambled toward the stack of papers like a flock of startled birds, all except Rio, who lagged behind with deliberate nonchalance. Halfway to the stack, she stopped, turning back to Agatha with that infuriatingly confident gaze.

“When you started talking about the tremendous stakes of today’s work, Dr. Harkness, I really thought we might be doing more than reading through patient notes and putting brains on scales,” Rio said, her tone laced with teasing sarcasm.

Agatha’s jaw tightened. She forced herself to exhale slowly before responding. “Vidal,” she said, her voice measured but firm, “You need to understand that there is no unimportant part of research. This work is just as crucial as any dissection. Now, if you’re done complaining, perhaps you’d like to join your peers in being productive.”

Rio didn’t reply, just smirked and grabbed her share of the reports.

Agatha returned to her station across the lab, where she busied herself sorting microscope slides. Every so often, she glanced up to check on the students’ progress. Her gaze, despite her best efforts, often landed on Rio, who was engrossed in the reports, her pen moving quickly across the page.

One time, as Agatha looked up, she was startled to find Rio’s eyes already on her. The younger woman’s expression was uncharacteristically thoughtful. It wasn’t mocking, as Agatha might have expected, but rather curious, even admiring. Agatha raised an eyebrow, the gesture sharp and questioning, as if to say, Look who’s staring now.

Rio’s eyes widened in brief surprise before she quickly looked back down at her work. Agatha smirked to herself, though she quickly shook it off. No distractions. she reminded herself firmly.

An hour passed in relative quiet, broken eventually by Billy’s voice from across the lab. Quiet but carrying a faint, incredulous tone. “Rio… how do you talk to Dr. Harkness like that?”

Agatha nearly laughed, but she kept her expression neutral, pretending to be preoccupied with the slides. Billy clearly thought she couldn’t hear him.

“Yeah” Alice chimed in, her voice a hushed whisper but sounding a little in awe. “No judgment or anything, but I honestly feel like crying every time I talk to her. How are you so…confident?”

Agatha felt a smug satisfaction settle over her. Good. At least some of her students knew how to respect authority. She could hear Rio snickering quietly, evidently enjoying their fascination.

Then Jen piped up, her voice carrying a sharper edge. “Yeah, what is going on with that, anyway? And why are you so cocky about it? What, you think you’re better than us just because you’re in some… intellectual ping-pong game with Dr. Harkness?”

Agatha found herself rolling her eyes at no one in particular. Still listening from across the lab as Billy hissed a frantic “Shhh!” trying to shush Jen, but Rio only laughed louder.

Agatha didn’t need to look up to know Rio would be taking the comment in stride. But curiosity got the better of her, and she cast a sidelong glance toward the benches, just in time to catch Rio’s mischievous smirk aimed right back at her, lifting her chin slightly, her eyes glinting in the same mischievous way Agatha had come to recognise. It was so fleeting, but the look in Rio’s eyes felt conspiratorial. As if they were sharing some inside joke, an unspoken dare.

“Jen,” Rio said as she tuned back to Jen, the tease unmistakable in her voice, “if you’re so jealous of me, why don’t you just work a little harder and impress Dr. Harkness yourself instead of…whatever it is you’re trying to do, reading into the way I talk.”

Agatha shook her head, half-amused, half-irritated. Unbelievable. The nerve of this girl, almost directly quoting Agatha’s own words from earlier:

“Vidal, I think you should worry more about our research plan than about whatever nonsense you think is going on in my head”

And that tone, like she didn’t care if Agatha noticed or not. Honestly, she couldn’t help but feel grudging admiration for Rio’s audacity. The girl had guts, Agatha would give her that much. But, she decided she’d had enough of the escalating chatter. With a sharp clap of her hands, she strode over to the center of the lab and drew everyone's attention back to her.

“Right, everyone. That’s enough for today. Thank you for your help. Let’s all hope none of you managed to screw up my research, shall we?” Her eyes flicked pointedly to Rio, who simply smirked in response. Agatha ignored it, turning her attention back to the group. “See you all tomorrow.”

The students began to gather their things, shuffling toward the door. Agatha stepped back, watching them file out, her expression unreadable until Rio was the last one left, her deliberate pace slowing as she approached the exit. Just as Rio reached the threshold, Agatha stepped forward, blocking her path.

Rio halted, looking up with her usual air of intrigue and just enough insolence to needle Agatha’s patience. She raised an eyebrow, her lips quirking upward “Yes, Dr. Harkness? Is there perhaps… something you’d like to discuss before I leave?”

Agatha stiffened. Does she have to bring up last night with every look and every word? She straightened her posture, folding her arms across her chest, refusing to be baited into whatever game the girl was trying to play.

“No, Vidal, there’s nothing to discuss,” she said, her tone clipped. “I simply wanted to let you know that I’ll need you in the lab early tomorrow. We’ll be starting on the new slides for the epilepsy project, and I don’t want to waste time waiting for you.”

Rio tilted her head, her smirk curling wider, a flicker of amusement dancing in her eyes. “Dr. Harkness,” she drawled “I’m always in early. Surely, you’ve noticed by now. So, what’s this really about? Did you just want an excuse to keep me behind?”

Agatha’s eyes narrowed, her exasperation barely contained. She let out a low, sardonic laugh and rolled her eyes.

“Vidal, for goodness’ sake.” She started, her tone exasperated, “I simply wanted to tell you that you need to meet me here at 8 a.m. sharp. Stop imagining that everything I do somehow revolves around you.”

Without waiting for a reply, Agatha turned sharply on her heel, taking a step toward her desk, then hesitated. Looking back over her shoulder, she brought her hand to her mouth in a mock whisper. “It’s pathetic.”

She didn’t wait to hear Rio’s response. She didn’t have to. The stunned look on Rio’s face as she stood frozen in the doorway was satisfaction enough. Agatha walked briskly out of the lab, her heels clicking decisively on the tiled floor.

Behind her, Rio blinked, incredulous, before breaking into an unexpected laugh. “Touché, Dr. Harkness,” she murmured to herself, shaking her head as she finally followed the others out.
