chapter 10

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

The cold morning wrapped around Agatha like a warning. She stood just outside the lab’s glass doors, letting the biting cold settle her nerves. The sun hadn’t yet risen high enough to warm anything but the faintest edges of the horizon, leaving the campus paths dusted with frost. Her breath fogged in the air, dissipating as quickly as her resolve threatened to.

Her fingers flexed against the strap of her leather satchel, the only outward sign of the discipline she was trying to force upon herself. Get a grip, she thought. She had always prided herself on being unshakable. Dedicated, focused, and utterly removed from the petty dramas that plagued lesser academics. Whatever this strange pull toward Rio Vidal was, it had to be extinguished. You cannot get distracted today. You have a lab to run, research to oversee, and deadlines to meet. This fixation with Rio Vidal is neither relevant nor acceptable.

The thought of Rio unsettled her in ways she couldn’t name. That sharp wit, the quiet confidence, the maddening smirk that always seemed a fraction too knowing. It was enough to make anyone bristle. But bristle wasn’t the right word for what Rio made her feel, was it? Agatha shook her head, as though the motion could physically dislodge the train of thought. There was no time for foolishness. Not just because it was unprofessional, but because it made her feel off-balance, something she could not afford.

Today, I am in control.

She exhaled sharply, her breath visible in the cold, and stepped inside.

The lab was quiet, the kind of quiet Agatha relished. The overhead lights buzzed faintly, illuminating the sterile space filled with equipment, trays of glass slides, and the hum of possibilities. It was 7:45, fifteen minutes before she had told Rio to be here, but as she moved further inside, her footsteps echoing softly, she noticed someone already at one of the benches.

Of course.

Rio sat with her sleeves pushed up and a faint smear of ink across her wrist, her dark hair half-tucked behind her ears. She was bent over a stack of papers, her hands steady as she flicked through them with meticulous care. Her usual air of nonchalance was replaced by something sharper, something that reminded Agatha, against her better judgment, why Professor Calderu had sent Rio to her lab in the first place.

But the moment passed, and Rio, sensing Agatha’s presence, glanced up.

"Morning, Dr Harkness," she said, her voice carrying that signature blend of challenge and sarcasm.

Agatha set her bag down on the counter with precision, smoothing the front of her tailored blazer as she turned toward Rio. "You're here early, Vidal," she said coolly. "Finally grasping the value of punctuality?"

Rio’s lips curved into that maddening half-smile as she leaned back on her stool. "Well, I mean, you went to all the effort to keep me behind after yesterday’s session just to tell me to be in early. So, here I am." She said with a shrug.

Agatha’s lips thinned, though she refused to give Rio the satisfaction of a visible reaction. Always with the clever answers, she thought. Always trying to see how far you can push.

"Let’s see if you can put that enthusiasm to productive use," she replied crisply, walking past Rio to the workstation where the new slides had been laid out. She retrieved a clipboard, scanning its contents before speaking again. "We’ll divide the work today. I’ll handle the slides from the control group, patients with Alzheimer’s only. And you," she continued, turning to Rio, "will focus on the experimental group, the slides from patients with both Alzheimer’s and epilepsy."

Rio’s expression shifted slightly, though it was difficult to tell whether it was intrigue or something else.

"Your job is critical," Agatha added, her tone firm. "If there’s any correlation to be found, it will likely appear here. I trust you understand the importance of precision in this task."

Rio gave a small nod, her gaze steady. "Crystal clear."

Agatha watched her for a moment, then placed the clipboard down with deliberate care. Her hand lingered on the edge of the counter.

"Before you begin," she said, her voice taking on a sharper edge, "let’s test your understanding. Vidal, tell me, were are looking for deposits of Tau protein, correct?” Rio gave a small nod, “Well, how do we visualise these deposits on a microscope slide?"

Rio didn’t miss a beat. Setting down her pipette, she turned toward Agatha fully, meeting her gaze with that same infuriating calm. "We use immunohistochemistry," she began, her voice steady. "The slides have been treated with an antibody specific to Tau, which binds to it. Then we apply a second antibody linked to a coloured enzyme to visualise the areas of Tau under the microscope. The deposits will show up as distinct coloured areas."

Agatha held her gaze, searching for any hint of hesitation or inaccuracy in Rio’s answer. There was none. She didn’t respond immediately. She let the silence stretch, taking in the quiet confidence with which Rio had spoken. There was no over-explanation, no trace of uncertainty. It was the kind of answer Agatha might have given as a PhD student, and the realisation unsettled her.

"Good," she said finally, her voice measured. She gave a small nod, stepping back. "Now get started."

Without another word, Rio turned back to her work, her movements precise and deliberate. Agatha remained for a moment longer, watching as Rio began to set up her station. There was something undeniably magnetic about the way she carried herself, an assurance that Agatha found both enviable and infuriating.

Shaking her head slightly, Agatha returned to her own work. She had no time for distractions, least of all the kind Rio Vidal seemed to excel at causing.

The lab fell into a comfortable silence, broken only by the faint clatter of glassware and the occasional scribble of notes. Yet, beneath the surface, the tension remained, a current neither of them acknowledged but both were acutely aware of.

Agatha focused on her slides, but every so often, her gaze flickered toward Rio, drawn as if by some invisible force. What was it about her? It wasn’t just the confidence or the skill; Agatha had worked with talented students before. There was something in Rio’s composure, the way she carried herself as though she were immune to the usual pressures of the lab, that unnerved her.

Agatha’s fingers tightened slightly around the edge of the microscope, and she forced herself to focus. This is nothing. She’s just another student.

But even as she thought it, Agatha knew she was lying to herself.

The hours ticked by in near silence, broken only by the soft rustle of papers, the faint hum of the centrifuge, and the occasional scratch of pen on paper. Agatha remained focused on her slides, eyes scanning for patterns, her brain filtering through years of accumulated expertise. But no matter how hard she tried to concentrate, her attention kept slipping.

Each time she glanced toward Rio, she found herself unraveling a little.

Rio’s movements were fluid, precise, she handled the slides with a practiced ease that belied her youth, her brow furrowed in concentration. Every now and then, Agatha would tear her gaze away, chastising herself for her lack of discipline. But more often than not, when she glanced back up she’d find Rio already looking at her, a flicker of something mischievous sparking in her dark eyes.

When their eyes met, Rio would smirk, a subtle curve of her lips that infuriated Agatha more than it should. Rio would snap her head back down to her work with almost theatrical nonchalance, as if she’d been caught mid prank. Agatha, trying to maintain her composure, would roll her eyes and force herself to return to her own slides, her stomach knotting in a way she didn’t want to acknowledge.

The minutes stretched into hours. They worked like that the whole time, silent, focused, but always hyperaware of the other’s presence.

It wasn’t until Rio gasped loudly beside her that the fragile equilibrium broke.

Agatha’s head snapped up, her slide forgotten. "What’s the matter?" she asked sharply, more alarmed than she cared to admit.

Rio didn’t respond immediately. She was staring at the microscope in front of her, her face lit with an intensity Agatha had never seen in her. "I just finished with the first set of slides," Rio said, her voice unsteady with excitement. "There’s... there’s a massive amount of Tau buildup in all of them."

Agatha blinked, processing the implications of this. Before she could respond, Rio was already typing something into the computer in front of her, her fingers flying over the keyboard.

"What are you doing?" Agatha demanded, stepping closer.

"Just running the stats quickly." Rio replied, her voice distracted, her focus entirely on the monitor.

The screen beeped.

Rio froze for a moment, staring at the results. Then, in an action that caught Agatha completely off guard, she jumped to her feet, clasping her hands over her mouth. "Oh my god," she whispered through her fingers. “Oh my god!” She repeated, now closer to a yelp than anything else.

Agatha’s brow furrowed, alarmed by the uncharacteristic reaction. She walked briskly to Rio’s side. "What is it? Let me see."

Rio stepped back, letting Agatha take her place at the computer. On the screen was a graph, the data plotted with unmistakable precision. At the top of the analysis, a number glinted in green: Correlation = 0.95 .

Agatha’s jaw dropped. "0.95?!" she said, incredulous. Her eyes darted hysterically between the data and Rio, searching for any sign of error. "Is that real? Are you sure you put in the numbers correctly?"

"Yes, I’m sure!" She said, her voice breaking slightly, as if the weight of the discovery was just now hitting her. Rio rubbed her face with both hands, muttering under her breath, "Holy shit."

Agatha allowed herself a small laugh of disbelief. "Yeah," she said quietly, her lips curling into a rare smile. "Holy shit is right."

They stood there for a moment, side by side, staring at the screen. The enormity of what they had just uncovered settled over them like a tangible force. Agatha knew she should be focused on the implications of the discovery, the awards it would spawn, the doors it would open, the lives it might save. But she couldn’t stop herself from glancing over at Rio.

Her expression was radiant, her usual cool demeanour completely stripped away, replaced by an almost childlike glee. Her eyes sparkled as she gazed at the data, and her smile was so unguarded, so utterly genuine, that Agatha felt something inside her soften.

She should have been thinking about Tau deposits, about Alzheimer’s, about the groundbreaking work they were doing. But all she could think about was how Rio looked in that moment, as if she had just glimpsed a piece of the universe’s secret truth.

Before she could stop herself, Agatha felt a small smile tugging at her lips. She didn’t fight it. Rio turned to her then, and their eyes met, the weight of their findings swirling unspoken between them. For a brief, dizzying moment, the boundaries Agatha had so carefully constructed seemed to blur.

"Wow," Agatha said softly, her voice almost reverent. “You… this is... impressive. Congratulations, Rio."

Rio nodded, her smile turning shy for the first time since Agatha had known her. "Yeah. We did good I guess." she said, her voice quiet but filled with awe.

Agatha shook her head slightly. "No," she said firmly, stepping closer, her expression serious. " You did good. This was your find. You suggested this project. You saw the potential here before anyone else." She gestured toward the screen, where the data still glimmered like a revelation. "You may be on your way to changing the field permanently."

Rio’s gaze snapped back to her, her grin faltering into something almost vulnerable. The words seemed to hit her, as though she hadn’t quite allowed herself to believe in the gravity of her own accomplishment until Agatha said it aloud.

Her grin returned slowly, wider than before, and it lit her entire face with an unguarded excitement. Agatha found herself momentarily disarmed by the purity of it. So different from Rio’s usual cocky smirk.

Agatha allowed her smile to grow as well. "Welcome to the club," she said, her tone lightening. "It feels good, doesn’t it?"

Rio let out a disbelieving laugh, her hand raking through her dark hair as she tried to absorb everything. "Yeah," she said, her voice warm with amazement. "It really does."

Agatha’s chest tightened at the sound of her laugh, at the way Rio’s voice carried an awe so genuine it was contagious. All she could think about was how Rio looked at this moment, so alive, so utterly present, her joy unfiltered.

The weight of their discovery lingered between them, the moment stretched taut with unspoken meaning. Agatha felt herself drawn in despite herself, her carefully erected walls threatening to crumble. She had always prided herself on remaining untouchable, but right now, standing beside Rio, she felt undeniably human.

"You should do something to celebrate," Agatha said finally. Her tone gentle but insistent, trying to pull them both back to reality. "This is a big moment in your career. You should be proud of yourself."

Rio thought for a moment, then tilted her head as her smirk slowly returned. That teasing smirk that always left Agatha simultaneously amused and on edge. Agatha’s stomach flipped as she saw something brewing behind Rio’s dark eyes, the kind of idea that was bound to make her regret offering any kindness at all.

“Actually.” Rio said, drawing out the word as though savouring it, "I think I just might have an idea." She straightened, crossing her arms loosely over her chest. "Dr. Harkness," she began, her voice light and mockingly formal, "Would you like to get a drink with me? You know, just to celebrate, of course.”

The words hit Agatha like a jolt, her stomach tightening with alarm. She blinked at Rio, stunned. "Excuse me?" she managed, her voice sharp with disbelief.

Rio’s smirk widened, clearly enjoying her reaction. "I mean," she said with exaggerated innocence, "You’re just as much a part of this project as I am. Come on, just a drink. We need to celebrate somehow, right?"

Agatha opened her mouth to argue, but no words came out. This was a bad idea. This was a very bad idea. The lines she had so carefully drawn between herself and her students were suddenly blurring, smudged by Rio’s unrelenting confidence. A drink? The idea felt so casual, so wildly inappropriate, and yet...

She glanced at Rio again, her expression caught somewhere between disbelief and exasperation. Rio was grinning now, wide and unrepentant, her earlier vulnerability completely replaced by her trademark audacity.

"You’re insane," Agatha muttered, rolling her eyes.

"Hmm maybe that’s true.” Rio replied, “But, you know you want to say yes." She quipped, her tone maddeningly light.

Every part of Agatha’s mind screamed at her to refuse, to put an end to this before it spiralled further. But the words wouldn’t come. Her eyes flicked again to Rio, at the gleam in her eyes, the flush of triumph still colouring her cheeks, and something inside her wavered.

Agatha swallowed hard, her throat suddenly dry. Against every ounce of better judgment she possessed, she heard herself say, "Sure, why not?"

Rio’s face lit up instantly, her smirk giving way to a grin so radiant it almost knocked the air out of Agatha’s lungs. "Great," she said, already reaching for her coat, her movements brimming with energy. "You won’t regret it, I promise."

Agatha wasn’t so sure about that. Her pulse quickened as she watched Rio shrug on her coat, her confidence so assured it was almost contagious.

This was a mistake. A massive mistake. But as she found herself following Rio to the door, a small part of her couldn’t help but think that maybe, just maybe, this wasn’t the worst idea she’d ever had.

Or maybe it was.

She sighed inwardly, following Rio toward the lab door. Only time would tell.

chapter 11

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

The cold night air clung to Agatha's skin, sharp and biting against the heat lingering from the lab. She hadn't planned on following Rio. Hadn't planned on anything, really. But here she was, her feet crunching against the frost-tipped pavement, trailing after her student.

Rio moved with that effortless confidence that had been grating on Agatha's nerves since the day they met. Even now, as the wind tugged at her coat and the darkness wrapped around them, she walked like she owned the street, her head tilted slightly, hands tucked in her pockets, as if this were all some grand joke she was in on.

When Rio turned, her smirk was already in place, sharp and knowing. Agatha tried to steel herself, but the expression still lit a fire in her chest. Half anger, half something she was scared to name. Agatha’s shoulers shuddered again.

“Here,” Rio said suddenly, pulling her scarf from around her neck and holding it out. The motion was casual, like it meant nothing at all. But her eyes, bright with amusement, gave her away.

“I don’t need it,” Agatha replied, her voice clipped as she waved the offer away.

Rio didn’t budge. “Oh, come on. I’m just repaying the favour.” The smirk grew as she added, “For when you lent me yours. Remember?”

Agatha’s breath hitched, and she hated herself for it. Damn Rio and her audacity. “Fine,” she muttered, snatching the scarf and wrapping it quickly around herself, as if speed might diminish the intimacy of the gesture.

The fabric was warm against her skin, and she couldn’t stop the sigh of relief that escaped her lips. It carried the faint, scent of Rio’s perfume. Something subtle and grounding, citrus. She pulled the scarf tighter, more for the cold than anything else, she told herself.

Rio watched her with a smugness that made Agatha want to roll her eyes again. “So,” Rio said, breaking the silence, “Where are we going?”

Agatha tilted her head, mirroring Rio’s smirk with one of her own. If Rio was going to mess with her head, she might as well return the favour. Two can play this game, she thought, the corner of her mouth twitching upward.

They reached the next corner, and Agatha let her hand brush the small of Rio’s back, a light touch, fleeting but deliberate. She felt the faintest twitch of surprise from Rio and bit back a grin. Gotcha.

“This way,” Agatha said smoothly, guiding Rio around the corner.

Rio shot her a sidelong glance, her smirk momentarily faltering before she caught herself.

Agatha chuckled softly, her breath fogging in the cold air. “There’s a pub just around here. I used to go there all the time when I was doing my PhD.”

“Oh that must’ve been a while ago,” Rio teased, and Agatha fought the urge to laugh outright, instead just rolling her eyes at her.

They reached the pub, a cozy, unassuming place with warm light spilling onto the street from its fogged-up windows. Laughter and the hum of conversation greeted them as Agatha pushed the door open, the scent of beer and roasted peanuts wafting out to meet them.

Rio paused in the doorway, turning to raise an eyebrow at Agatha, who held the door and gestured into the pub. “Ladies first,” Agatha said, the smirk on her face razor-sharp.

Rio placed a hand over her chest in mock astonishment. “Well, how kind of you.” Her laugh was warm and easy as she stepped inside, and Agatha couldn’t help the slight curve of her lips as she followed.

Agatha followed Rio into the pub, the familiar hum of laughter and clinking glasses enveloping them as the warmth chased away the evening chill. She took a moment to glance around, a twinge of nostalgia creeping in as she spotted the familiar faded wood of the bar and the same peeling poster advertising live music nights. It had been years since she’d last stepped foot in this place, and yet, it felt oddly unchanged.

Rio’s voice cut through her thoughts. “Well, this is cozy,” she said, sliding into a table at the corner. She propped her elbows on the table and leaned forward, her dark eyes glinting with amusement. “Can’t imagine you hanging out here, though. Seems too... lively for someone as refined as you.”

Agatha raised a brow as she slipped into the seat across from her, the scarf still wrapped snugly around her neck. “Don’t let the lab coat fool you, Vidal. I had a life before I became The Wicked Witch. ” Her tone was light, but her gaze sharpened, daring Rio to make another quip.

“Oh, I have no doubt,” Rio replied, a grin spreading across her face. “Let me guess. You were the type to sit in the corner, nursing a single drink while brooding over your thesis?”

Agatha smirked, leaning forward slightly, her fingers tapping rhythmically on the edge of the table. “Well, you're not entirely wrong,” she said, her voice laced with amusement. “I wasn’t exactly known for my social skills back then. But I certainly didn’t brood over my thesis. It was more like... strategise. Plot. Overthrowing the establishment, one breakthrough at a time.”

Rio's grin widened, and she leaned forward, elbows back on the table, clearly enjoying the banter. “Ah yes, now I see. This does seem like the perfect spot for plotting world domination.”

Agatha rolled her eyes as she leaned forward, mirroring Rio. “Oh, please. If I were plotting world domination, I wouldn’t waste my time in a place like this.”

Rio laughed, a low, warm sound that sent a ripple of something through Agatha that she refused to name. “Of course not. You’d be in a secret underground lair, probably with a dozen whiteboards and and diagrams and a plan that’s been in the works for decades.”

Agatha smirked, letting the jab roll off her. “You sound awfully confident for someone who would clearly be one of my minions.”

Rio arched an eyebrow, leaning further forward on her elbows with that insufferable smirk of hers. “Minion? Oh no, if anything, I’d be the one challenging you for the throne.” Rio said as she laughed, the sound warm, unguarded. It caught Agatha off guard, and she found herself smiling despite herself.

“Alright, then,” Rio said, tilting her head. “What’s your poison, Dr. Harkness? Let me guess, you’re a red wine type? Something dry, probably with a name no one can pronounce.”

Agatha rolled her eyes. “You’re insufferable.” But she couldn’t help the smirk tugging at her lips. “And wrong. I’ll take a gin and tonic.”

Rio let out a low laugh, standing and heading toward the bar. “Oh, well, my apologies then. One gin and tonic coming right up.” she said over her shoulder.

Agatha watched her go, her gaze lingering a moment longer than it should have. Shaking her head, she exhaled slowly and glanced around the room, trying to ground herself. What was she even doing here? It wasn’t like her to follow her students out for drinks, especially not students who tested her patience at every turn. And yet, there was something about Rio, her irreverence, her sharp wit, the way she seemed utterly unbothered by Agatha’s authority, that drew her in. No matter how much she tried to resist it.

Rio returned a few minutes later, balancing two glasses with surprising grace. She set the gin and tonic down in front of Agatha before sliding back into her seat, her own glass of amber liquid catching the dim light.

“Whiskey?” Agatha asked, arching a brow.

“Scotch,” Rio corrected. “Neat.”

“Of course,” Agatha muttered, lifting her glass and taking a sip. The cool, crisp taste was a welcome distraction from the warmth that still lingered in her chest. A warmth she decided to blame on the scarf and not on the woman sitting across from her.

“So,” Rio said, her gaze fixed on Agatha who finally removed the scarf from around her neck, “What were you like back then? During your PhD? Let me guess. Impossibly brilliant, impossibly intimidating, and maybe a little insufferable.”

Agatha chuckled despite herself. “You’re not entirely wrong.”

“I knew it.” Rio leaned back, her smirk softening into something almost genuine. “You’re still all those things, by the way.”

Agatha froze, her glass halfway to her lips. The comment wasn’t delivered with Rio’s usual sarcasm; it was quiet, almost sincere. She cleared her throat, setting the glass down with a soft clink. “Careful, Vidal. You’re dangerously close to sounding like you admire me.”

Rio’s grin returned, sharp and teasing. “Oh, I wouldn’t go that far.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, but there was no mistaking the faint flush that crept up her neck.

Rio took a slow sip from her glass, watching Agatha with a thoughtful expression. “So, what was your first breakthrough?” she asked, her voice casual, though there was an underlying curiosity there.

Agatha’s fingers curled around her glass as she leaned back in her seat, the question pulling her away from the easy banter they’d been exchanging. She took a moment, a flicker of something deeper passing through her gaze before she answered.

“My first breakthrough?” Agatha raised an eyebrow, the question tugging her back to a memory she hadn't visited in years. She leaned back in her chair, swirling her drink thoughtfully.

"It really wasn’t some eureka moment," she said slowly, her gaze turning distant for a moment. "It was a gradual thing. It was when I was working on neuroplasticity in Alzheimer's models. It wasn’t flashy, but it shifted the way we thought about long-term memory consolidation. I remember sitting in the lab for hours and hours. Running the same experiments over and over, waiting for that one result. When it came, I was… well, I was shocked. But also, I knew then that I could do more than just follow the path laid out by others."

Rio nodded, clearly impressed. Her voice softened just a fraction. "Sounds like you were unstoppable. How did it feel, in the moment? To know you'd changed the game?"

Agatha considered the question, her fingers absently tracing the rim of her glass. "It felt like freedom. Like all the rules I’d been following up to that point didn’t matter anymore. It was terrifying, too. Because suddenly, everyone expects you to do more, to live up to that moment."

Rio’s smirk faded slightly, replaced by a genuine curiosity. "I get that. The pressure must’ve been unreal." Agatha met her gaze, her heart giving an unexpected lurch at the quiet intensity behind Rio’s words.

Agatha met her gaze, the weight of Rio’s attention settling over her like a cloak. She nodded. But before she could add anything else, Rio leaned in, her voice turning teasing once more.

“So, I’ve been wondering. What does the esteemed Dr. Agatha Harkness do in her free time?” she asked, leaning forward again, eyes twinkling with the familiar spark of mischief. “I can’t help but imagine you just sitting and reading neuroscience papers all evening when you go home. Please tell me you have actual hobbies.”

Agatha laughed, rolling her eyes, the tension easing for a brief second. “I have hobbies, Vidal,” she said, a teasing edge in her voice.

Rio leaned in further, her elbows resting on the table. “Oh yeah? I don’t believe you.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow, unimpressed by Rio’s challenge. “I’ll have you know I’m an avid TV watcher in my free time. This stays between us, though, because I’m not proud of it, but... I’ve been on my third rewatch of Grey’s Anatomy .” She glanced down at her lap, a flush creeping up her neck as she admitted it.

Rio froze, her eyes widening in surprise. “ Grey’s Anatomy ?!” she nearly shouted, her voice rising a few octaves, all trace of her usual coolness gone. “Wow, I was not expecting that. You are full of surprises.”

Agatha felt the heat rise in her cheeks, desperately wishing she could sink into the floor. “Don’t make it worse, Vidal,” she muttered, glancing back up, her tone half-amused, half-exasperated.

But Rio, clearly enjoying the moment, slapped her hand down on the table with a laugh. “I can’t believe it. Dr. Harkness, the unapproachable, terrifying neuroscientist, is obsessed with Grey’s Anatomy*.* That’s... that’s gold.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, desperately trying to reclaim her composure. “It’s a guilty pleasure, alright?” she said, though the lightness in her voice betrayed her words. “Can we just pretend this conversation never happened?”

Rio leaned back, shaking her head, her smirk never wavering. “Never. This is too good. I’ll be telling the whole lab about it, you know. ‘Did you know Dr. Harkness watches Grey’s Anatomy religiously?’”

Agatha shot her a warning look, but Rio was already teasing her in her usual way. “I’m never going to let this go,” Rio said, eyes still gleaming with amusement.

Agatha sighed, but the irritation was half-hearted. She took another sip of her gin, then glanced at Rio. “Alright, fine. What about you? What do you do in your free time?”

Rio raised an eyebrow, her gaze turning reflective for a moment. “Well, I play electric guitar. I play in a band sometimes.” She said it so casually.

But this new information hit Agatha harder than she expected. She froze for a moment, the image of Rio with a guitar in her hands, eyes focused and intent, sent a jolt through Agatha’s chest. Her breath caught for a fraction of a second before she quickly composed herself.

No, no. Stop it, Harkness. She snapped herself out of the mental haze, forcing her eyes back to Rio, only to find her looking at her with that annoyingly self-assured smirk

Agatha cleared her throat, breaking her gaze from Rio’s. “A band?” she repeated, forcing her voice to sound light. “Now that I didn’t expect.”

Rio leaned back, her grin broadening, clearly noticing Agatha’s momentary lapse and revelling in it. "Yeah. You’d be surprised how many people don’t guess that about me."

Agatha swallowed hard, her gaze fixed on the table as she tried to focus, to reign herself in. Focus. She took another sip of her gin, her hands suddenly feeling a little too warm around the glass.

There was a silence then, the kind that stretched long enough to feel almost tangible, both of them caught in an unspoken moment. Agatha tried to shake off the effect Rio’s words were having on her, but she couldn’t quite manage it. Rio’s presence, her confidence, her very ease, it was starting to chip away at the walls Agatha had so carefully constructed around herself.

And in that quiet, fleeting moment, the tension between them became palpable. It wasn’t just the banter anymore. It wasn’t just the challenge or the sparring. There was something else, something undeniably magnetic.

The soft hum of the pub faded as Agatha realised she was looking at Rio, really looking at her, like she hadn’t before. And Rio, for her part, seemed to sense the shift. Her smirk softened, her gaze becoming unreadable as she studied Agatha in return.

“So,” Rio began, her voice smooth, low, and teasing, “You look like you’ve got a thousand questions. Go ahead, ask away. I’ll answer anything”

Agatha raised an eyebrow, her pulse quickening despite herself. “Oh, I’m sure you would.” Her voice was sharp, but there was something in her tone, something unspoken. She leaned back slightly, crossing her arms, trying to regain some semblance of control. “I’m curious, though... You, in a band? That’s definitely not what I expected from someone who’s so quick in the lab.”

Rio’s smirk never faltered. “Yeah, well, you’d be surprised what a little music can do to loosen up someone like me,” she said, leaning in just enough to make Agatha feel the heat of her presence. “Maybe you should try it sometime.”

Agatha’s breath caught slightly at the suggestive tone in Rio’s voice. She forced herself to meet Rio’s gaze, her eyes narrowing as she fought the sudden wave of heat that rose in her chest. “You think I need loosening up?” Agatha’s words were quiet but charged, each one deliberate, a challenge.

Rio’s grin widened, a mix of amusement and something else that Agatha couldn’t quite place. “Well, maybe not need ... but I think it could do you some good.” Her eyes dropped for a moment, grazed over the lines of Agatha’s face.

Agatha’s heart thudded harder. She swallowed, trying to keep her composure. “I have no interest in picking up a guitar, thank you very much.”

Rio raised an eyebrow, leaning forward until there was barely a sliver of space between them. “Who says you need to pick up a guitar? Everyone has different ways of relaxing.” Her voice dropped lower, smoother, each word laced with something dangerous, something that made Agatha’s pulse jump. “Maybe all you need to loosen up is a little... company.”

Agatha froze for a moment, the air thickening between them as Rio’s words landed. She forced a small, controlled laugh, but it came out breathier than she intended. “Company, huh? You think you’re the one to loosen me up?”

Rio’s smirk deepened, eyes locking onto Agatha’s, as if she was daring her to back down. “I think I might be just the person for the job.” She straightened, glancing around the pub casually, but there was a flicker of something mischievous in her eyes. “But, then again, maybe you prefer to do everything on your own. Can’t let anyone distract you, right?”

Agatha’s lips parted for a moment, her mind fighting to keep up with the sudden change in their conversation. This girl had read right through her. She felt that familiar, tight coil of tension in her chest. It was one thing to have witty exchanges with her students, to put them in their place, but Rio was different. And now, with that playful challenge lingering in the air, Agatha wasn’t sure how much longer she could keep her walls intact.

She leaned in slightly, her voice dropping to match Rio’s tone, the challenge now firmly in her words. “You’re getting awfully bold, Vidal. You sure you want to push your luck?”

Rio didn’t flinch. If anything, her smile widened. “Boldness is kind of my thing.” Her voice was playful, but there was a flicker of something darker underneath it, a promise. “But I think you know that, don’t you?”

Agatha’s breath caught for a moment. The way Rio’s gaze held hers, steady, sure, pulled her in like a magnetic force, and it was getting harder and harder to maintain her distance. Rio wasn’t just a student. She wasn’t just a challenge to be managed. She was something else entirely.

“And please,” Rio continued, her smirk growing ever-wider, “you should call me Rio. You know, now that you’ve told me your deepest darkest secret. I still cannot believe you… Grey’s anatomy… seriously?’

“Shut up.” Agatha respond with a light-hearted scoff. Rio leaned back, crossing her arms with a satisfied grin, clearly enjoying the effect she was having. Agatha could feel the tension hanging between them like a delicate thread, stretched taut and threatening to snap at any moment.

“So, what now?” Rio asked, her voice casual but laced with an edge. “You going to keep trying to maintain control... or are you going to finally admit that I’ve got you a little... off balance?”

Agatha thought about the situation she was in, the ridiculousness of it all. Sitting across from Rio Vidal in a crowded pub, engaging in banter that felt far too charged to be entirely innocent. What am I doing here? she asked herself, but the answer was already painfully obvious.

Her thoughts drifted to Rio. The way her smirk seemed permanently etched on her lips, effortlessly cocky and infuriatingly charming. About the way her dark hair fell around her face, framing her sharp features with an effortless kind of beauty that felt almost unfair.

Rio’s tongue ran lazily over her teeth in a motion that Agatha could only describe as maddening, she was seemingly amused at how caught off-guard Agatha seemed to be. It made Agatha’s stomach twist in ways she didn’t want to analyse. She was losing herself in the little details, her chest tightening as her thoughts spiralled.

This is not good. Not good at all. Agatha straightened in her seat, gripping the edge of the table as if it might ground her. Her head started to swirl, and sure, she could blame it on the gin, but one drink was nothing. She was too self-aware, too sharp to let herself believe it was the alcohol.

No, Agatha Harkness wasn’t stupid. She knew exactly what was happening.

She had known for weeks, in fact. Every quip, every smug look, every defiant word Rio had thrown her way, it had all chipped away at her defences. She’d convinced herself that her irritation was strictly professional, that Rio’s overconfidence simply grated on her nerves. But she couldn’t deny it anymore. The spark she felt wasn’t anger, and the truth had been pressing in on her like a rising tide.

Every time she saw that smirk on Rio’s lips, she wanted, no, needed, to wipe it away. She wanted to grab her by the collar and kiss the stupid grin off her face. That night outside the lab. The teasing, the electricity in the air. It hadn’t been an accident. Not entirely. She could keep telling herself it was just a moment of weakness, a lapse in judgment, but deep down, she knew it had been something else. And now here she was, sitting across from the source of her undoing, feeling her control slip with every passing second.

It was too much.

Agatha cleared her throat, a sharp sound that made Rio’s eyebrow lift in curiosity. She placed her hand on the table, pushing herself to her feet with as much composure as she could muster. “I need some air,” she said, her voice a touch steadier than she expected. “I’m just going to step outside quickly.”

Rio tilted her head, her arms lazily crossing over her chest as she leaned back in her chair. That damned smirk crept back across her lips, her dark eyes glittering as she said nothing, just watching Agatha with that insufferable confidence that made her stomach twist.

Agatha straightened, pulling her coat around her shoulders. “I’m fine,” she added quickly, her voice too sharp, too defensive. “It’s just... hot in here.”

Rio’s smirk widened. She knew that Rio wasn’t fooled by her excuses, not even a little bit.

She turned on her heel before Rio could respond, but she could feel her gaze following her, could practically hear the smug amusement in her silence. She walked to the back of the pub. Each step a little too fast, her heartbeat pounding louder with every passing second.

chapter 12

Chapter Notes

BUCKLE IN U GUYS THIS CHAPTER SHIT IS GOING DOWN 🤭🤭

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Agatha pushed the door open and stepped out, the cold air was a relief, biting against her skin and dragging her back to reality. She stepped into the alley behind the pub, pressing her back against the brick wall and tilting her face up toward the night sky. Her breaths came fast and shallow, and she exhaled slowly, forcing herself to take in the icy air and let it settle the chaos in her mind.

This is ridiculous, she thought. You’re not a teenager. You’re a grown woman, a professor, for God’s sake. Get it together.

But it didn’t matter how much she tried to rationalise it. The image of Rio leaning forward, that smirk softening just enough to make Agatha’s heart stutter, was seared into her mind. And the worst part? She didn’t want to let it go.

Agatha crouched down in the alley, her forehead resting against her knees as she tried to ground herself. The cold air helped, but not nearly enough. Her mind raced, spinning with thoughts she was struggling to suppress. Every inch of her felt on edge, heightened by the weight of what had just happened inside, the way Rio’s gaze seemed to pierce through her. But it was the last thing Agatha had wanted. Becoming so… undone. Pull it together, Harkness, she silently chastised herself.

But then she heard it: the faintest click. Agatha's heart skipped a beat as she stood up, lifting her head to see her, of course, standing in the doorway to the pub, Rio Vidal. Looking effortlessly in control as always. Her dark eyes glinted in the dim light of the alley, a smirk playing on her lips as she leaned against the doorframe, arms crossed.

Really? Could I just have one moment alone to spiral without her showing up? Agatha thought bitterly. But it was too late now. Rio was here, and she wasn’t backing down.

"Hey," Rio greeted casually, her gaze scanning Agatha from head to toe. She seemed to take in the way Agatha the way she stood opposite her, leaning against the wall for support, breath shallow, body tense. "What’s wrong? Someone got you all worked up?"

Agatha rolled her eyes, her frustration bubbling up. She couldn’t start spiralling again, not now. Not with Rio here. “Shut up,” she bit out, trying to mask how her heart was racing at the sound of that infuriatingly smooth voice.

Rio chuckled softly, not phased in the slightest by Agatha's biting tone. She pushed off from the doorframe, stepping forward into the alley, her movements deliberate and confident. Agatha's breath caught in her throat as she found herself unable to look away. She couldn't think. She couldn't focus. Every step Rio took only brought her closer, closer, until Agatha was struggling to breathe under the weight of the tension that crackled between them.

"What do you want, Rio?" Agatha managed, though her voice wavered more than she cared to admit.

Rio simply scoffed, raising an eyebrow with that trademark smirk she always wore. “Agatha,” she drawled, and the sound of her name on Rio’s lips made Agatha’s chest tighten. Damn it. "I think you know what I want. And I have a feeling that you want it too."

Agatha shook her head quickly, trying to regain some semblance of control. She attempted a shrug, though it came out as awkward and forced. “I have no idea what you’re talking about, Rio.”

The smirk on Rio’s face widened, and she stepped even closer, until the space between them was almost nonexistent. "Oh?" she said with a playful scoff, "So you want me to say it?"

Agatha met her gaze head-on, biting back the confusion and desire swirling inside her. She didn’t want to hear it, she couldn’t. But when Rio took another step forward, her voice dropping lower, that smirk still in place, Agatha’s resolve began to crack. "Fine. I’ll tell you what I want, Agatha."

Another step. Now they were so close that Agatha could feel the heat radiating from Rio’s body. She tilted her head slightly, eyes gleaming in the dim alley as she whispered, her breath warm against Agatha’s skin, "I want you . That’s what I want. But I think you knew that, didn’t you?"

Agatha’s breath hitched at the words, the sound coming out more like a whimper than anything she could control. Her mind raced, her heart pounding, and she could feel her whole body betraying her. She tried to push the words out, to fight against it. “Rio, I—this is so unprofessional. I can’t—"

Rio raised a finger slowly, gently, to Agatha’s lips, silencing her protests. Agatha stayed in the alley a moment longer, letting the cold air cool her flushed skin and trying desperately to regain her composure. Tomorrow, she would see Rio again. But tonight? Tonight, she let herself feel it. Just for a little while. The warmth in her chest, the ache in her stomach, the lingering taste of Rio on her lips.

With one last glance down the empty alley, Agatha straightened herself and headed back inside, her mind still spinning, her heart still pounding. She had no idea what tomorrow would bring, but one thing was certain: Rio Vidal was a complication she wasn’t ready for. And maybe, just maybe, she didn’t mind.

“Caught me,” she said, her voice dripping with amusement. “Though I’d argue you’re the one making it difficult to focus.”

Agatha tilted her head, pretending to consider this. “Interesting excuse. Though I can’t say I’m surprised. It must be terribly distracting working with me.”

“Terribly,” Rio replied, her grin widening.

Agatha turned squarely toward Rio, resting her elbows on her knees again and letting her chin lean her clasped hands. She’d perfected this pose. She knew the effect it had, especially on Rio. She’d seen that flicker of something beneath Rio’s usual confidence. She shifted her weight, silently enjoying the subtle unease she had already planted.

“So, do you actually intend to focus on the slides today, Vidal, or is this just an opportunity to gawk at me?” Agatha asked, her voice smooth, testing the waters. She was keenly aware of the slight hitch in Rio’s breath when she spoke. Just enough of a sign that Agatha’s words had landed, but not enough for Rio to show any real weakness.

Rio snorted softly, setting down the glass slide she had been inspecting. “Oh, I’m focusing,” she replied, her tone light but charged. “It’s just… there’s a lot to focus on today.”

Agatha’s lips quirked slightly, and she leaned back in her chair, shifting her gaze to the edge of the desk. She could feel Rio’s eyes on her as she spoke. Curious, almost dangerous. “Really? And here I thought the patient data would have your full attention. Should I be concerned that your attention is… elsewhere?” She let the words hang in the air.

Rio leaned back in her chair, twirling her pen between her fingers. Agatha watched her, waiting for the inevitable retort. “I’m always paying attention, Dr. Harkness. Especially when something” She paused, her gaze sweeping deliberately over Agatha’s face for a moment too long. “…particularly interesting is in front of me.”

Agatha’s pulse picked up, and she struggled to keep her face neutral. She had to remind herself she was the one in control here. She had started this little game, after all. “Careful, Rio. ” she murmured, her voice dropping, laced with something teasing yet sharp. “You’re treading on dangerous ground. If you’re not careful, you might say something you’ll regret.”

“Regret?” Rio scoffed, her voice low and playful. “I don’t regret much, Dr. Harkness. In fact, if last night taught me anything, it’s that-”

Agatha’s heart stuttered in her chest, and she interrupted with barely controlled impatience. “Vidal. I’m warning you.” Her tone was sharper now.

Rio looked up at her, an expression of exaggerated surprise plastered on her face as she gasped dramatically “What? I **was talking about our breakthrough. I meant that I won’t regret any part of the project.” Her voice was mockingly innocent, but Agatha could hear the playful lilt to it, ‘Why? What did you think I was talking about?’ Rio said, batting her eyelashes.

Agatha exhaled slowly, rolling here eyes. Her thoughts were racing, but she kept her exterior calm. “Let’s just get back to the task at hand, shall we?” She didn’t look at Rio again as she reached for another slide, her fingers almost shaking with the tension that had built up between them.

For a while, they worked in silence again. Or at least, Agatha tried to. She could feel Rio beside her, and every now and then, catching the briefest glance from the corner of her eye. Agatha knew Rio was watching her, but she refused to let herself respond. She focused, determined to stay on task, even as the energy between them crackled.

It didn’t take long before Rio broke the silence. “You know,” she said casually, as though the last few moments hadn’t happened, “If I may say so, you seem awfully on edge today.” Her voice was thick with unspoken meaning, and Agatha could feel the tease in it.

“On edge?” Agatha repeated, her tone incredulous. “Please, Vidal. If anyone’s on edge, it’s you.” She tried to regain the upper hand, but the warmth in her chest was spreading now, and it made her feel almost... exposed.

“Oh?” Rio’s eyebrow arched, a flicker of amusement in her eyes. “And what makes you so sure of that?”

“Call it an observation,” Agatha said, her voice cool, but her fingers suddenly restless on the table. “You’ve been squirming in your seat all morning.” She couldn’t resist the challenge in her voice, the satisfaction she took from seeing Rio lose some of her composure.

Rio barked out a laugh, but the faint blush creeping up her neck didn’t escape Agatha’s notice. “Squirming? That’s a bold accusation, Dr. Harkness.”

“Bold, but accurate,” Agatha countered, her smirk returning. She couldn’t help it—there was something so satisfying about pushing Rio’s buttons, watching her control slip, even just for a moment. The silence stretched between them again, but this time it was different. Agatha could feel the tension pulling tight like a wire. And she knew, just knew , she had to keep pushing.

“Oh, by the way, Dr. Harkness,” Rio said suddenly, her voice low, almost teasing.

Agatha’s head snapped up, her body suddenly tense, her attention shifting entirely to Rio. She felt the hairs on the back of her neck stand on end. “Yes?” she asked, her voice tight with anticipation.

Rio leaned forward, her elbows resting on the table, closing the distance between them. Agatha’s eyes flicked to the space between them, and for the briefest moment, her breath caught. Their faces were close. Too close. But then she saw the others across the room, their backs to them, absorbed in their own work, and a sense of relief flooded her.

Rio flicked her tongue out to wet her lips, and Agatha couldn’t help but follow the movement with her eyes. It was involuntary, a brief flicker of attention to something she hadn’t meant to notice. She forced herself to look back up into Rio’s eyes, but she was already caught.

“Dr. Harkness?” Rio’s voice was quieter now, almost mocking. Agatha felt her pulse quicken, but she was careful not to let it show. “Distracted?”

“What? No. Of course not. What were you about to say?” Agatha’s voice cracked slightly, but she recovered quickly, clearing her throat. She could feel Rio’s amusement, the sharpness in her gaze. It rattled her more than she cared to admit.

“Well,” she begun, her voice casual but tinged with satisfaction, “Professor Calderu mentioned I should update her on any major milestones in our PhD journeys.”

Agatha’s brow furrowed slightly, wary of where this was going. “Did she now?”

Rio nodded, her smirk deepening as she leaned back in her chair, breaking some of the tension but not all of it. “So, I shot her an email this morning about our findings.”

“And?” Agatha prompted, keeping her tone even despite the unease coiling in her chest.

Rio’s smirk widened, as if she were savouring every second of this. “She was very impressed. And, as it turns out, so was the head of the dementia research department at Oxford.”

Agatha blinked, momentarily thrown. “Oxford?”

“Mm hmm,” Rio confirmed, leaning back in her chair with an air of nonchalance that Agatha was certain was at least partially feigned. “Apparently, they’ve got an entire department focused on risk factors for dementia. Calderu reached out to them, and they were so interested in our findings that they’re sponsoring a two-day trip for us to give them a lecture. All expenses paid.”

Agatha felt the words hit her like a bucket of cold water. A trip. Overnight. With Rio. The implications spun wildly in her mind, each one more dangerous than the last.

Rio, oblivious (or much more likely, entirely aware) of the turmoil she was causing, continued. “All we have to do is prepare a lecture for their faculty. And they’ve signed us up to attend a few other lectures while we’re there. Networking opportunities, you know.”

Agatha struggled to form a coherent response. Her brain latched onto the professional aspects of the trip, desperately clinging to them like a lifeline. A lecture at Oxford was a prestigious opportunity, one that could mean everything for Rio’s budding career and for their research. It was, objectively, a huge win for their project.

But then… there was the part of her that couldn’t ignore the sheer recklessness of spending two days in close quarters with Rio Vidal, the thought loomed far too large. No. This was a terrible idea. Completely unprofessional. Risky. And yet…

A thrill of excitement sparked in her chest, unbidden but undeniable. The idea of presenting their work to one of the most prestigious institutions in the world was exhilarating. And, if she were honest with herself, so was the idea of spending two days with Rio, away from the lab, away from the others, away from the carefully maintained boundaries she’d always upheld.

“Oxford.” she repeated, as if saying it aloud would help her process the gravity of the situation.

Suddenly, the full picture hit Agatha with an almost visceral force. As much as she was enjoying the game this morning, watching Rio squirm, prodding her into that state of frustrated composure and watching as she struggled to maintain control, this was crossing a line. No, it was obliterating the line. This trip wasn’t just risky; it was insane . She had made it a rule, a cardinal law etched into her very being, to never get romantically involved with anyone she worked with. And students? That rule didn’t just apply, it multiplied, compounded in its severity.

Her pulse quickened as she tried to focus on the logic. The solution seemed obvious. She simply wouldn’t go. Rio could take the lead at Oxford; it would be an incredible opportunity for her, a career milestone that would outshine most achievements at her stage.

Yes. Agatha could step back, feign having another obligation, or perhaps claim she wanted Rio to have her moment in the spotlight. It would be a perfectly plausible, perfectly professional choice.

And yet. Her jaw tightened as her thoughts swirled. The chance to present their groundbreaking findings to one of the world’s foremost universities, the exposure for their lab would be monumental. The kind of opportunity that came along once in a lifetime. Her presence wasn’t just important ; it was necessary . For professional reasons only. Or, at least, that’s what she told herself as she let the idea of this trip burrow deeper into her mind.

It definitely wasn’t about Rio. It was completely, fully, 100% about the project. About the science. About their collective success. She repeated these justifications like a mantra, even as the thrill of anticipation curled low in her chest, refusing to be ignored.

She let out a quiet sigh, one that betrayed more of her inner turmoil than she’d intended. It was soft but audible in the stillness of the lab. “Well,” she said at last, her voice brisk, businesslike, “it sounds like a great opportunity. But, if we want more than one set of data to discuss in that lecture, I suggest we focus and get a move on with these slides.”

Agatha didn’t glance up, didn’t dare meet Rio’s gaze, but she could feel the shift in the room. There was a pause, a stillness that stretched just a fraction too long before Rio responded.

“Right.” Rio’s voice was calm, but Agatha didn’t miss the slight furrow of her brows, the subtle shift in her posture. She seemed to notice the change in Agatha’s tone, in her demeanour, but to Agatha’s relief she didn’t comment on it. Instead, Rio gave a small nod and turned her attention back to the slides.

For the rest of the afternoon, the lab settled into an uneasy quiet. The faint clicks and soft rustle of glass slides punctuated the silence as they worked. But Agatha could feel the weight of Rio’s eyes fliking up every few minutes, glancing at her from across the table. It wasn’t overt. It was subtle, almost imperceptible, but Agatha caught it each time in her periphery. Rio was watching her, as though trying to read her, to piece together whatever had caused the shift. Agatha kept her gaze firmly fixed on the microscope, her expression neutral.

But inside, her thoughts churned relentlessly, a storm of logic and doubt and something far more dangerous, something she refused to name. Whatever it was, she buried it beneath a layer of composure, gripping the work in front of her like a lifeline.

Chapter 14

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Agatha strode purposefully through the hallways of the lab, the heels of her boots clicking against the floor. She needed to clear her mind of the chaos that had been consuming her since that evening . It had been a mistake, a lapse in judgment she wouldn’t allow herself to repeat. But of course, she knew better. She was well aware that she had been living in denial for weeks. The problem with being an expert on the brain was that she knew exactly what was at play in her mind: the avoidance, the cognitive dissonance, the internal tug of war between logic and reason. She would deal with that later, though. She pushed the thought aside as she reached the meeting room. Today wasn’t about her personal life. Today was about the future of neuroscience.

The funding allocation meeting was the most cutthroat event of the year. The department’s senior scientists and students would battle for resources to push their projects forward. Agatha and Rio were on the edge of something groundbreaking, but without funding, progress would slow.

Agatha steeled herself as she stepped into the meeting room. The low hum of conversation filled the air, the tension was palpable. Everyone here knew what was at stake. Around the long, polished table sat her colleagues, the senior scientists whose opinions and votes would determine the future of their projects. Among them, perched along the edges of the room or huddled near the coffee station, were the students. Eager, hopeful for their slice of the funding.

Her gaze swept across the room, noting who had arrived. Lilia Calderu was seated at the far end of the table. As usual, she exuded a composed authority that Agatha couldn’t help but envy. She straightened her posture. She couldn’t afford to lose focus today.

Agatha took her usual seat, setting her leather notebook on the table and pulling a pen from the inner pocket of her blazer. She opened to a blank page, jotting some notes in the top corner. The motion steadied her, a small act of control in a situation that could easily spiral into chaos. Today was important. The outcomes of this meeting could have major implications for their reserach. Today was not the day for distractions.

Just then, she heard the chair to her right scrape against the floor. She glanced up. Speak of the fucking devil.

Rio Vidal slid into the seat beside her with effortless confidence.. Agatha’s stomach tightened involuntarily, as her gaze caught on Rio’s green blouse, unbuttoned just enough to be noticed, her eyes lingering a moment too long. Rio cleared her throat, a pointed sound that carried a note of amusement. Agatha felt the heat rise in her cheeks. When she raised her head, Rio was watching her, an eyebrow raised in smug triumph. The corner of her mouth curled upward, as if to say look who’s distracted now.

Agatha exhaled slowly, her expression sharpening as she shot Rio a pointed look. Rio merely smirked in response, leaning back in her chair as if she had already won whatever unspoken game they were playing. Agatha tightened her grip on her pen, forcing herself to focus. The meeting hadn’t even started, and Rio was already testing her composure.

Not today. Agatha turned to Rio, her voice low and firm as she whispered, “There’s no time for your antics today. This meeting is really serious.”

Rio leaned back in her chair, scoffing lightly. “Dr. Harkness, I think you feed into my antics more than you think.”

Agatha’s eyes narrowed, her gaze hardening. “Rio, I’m not joking. This is important. The future of our research depends on this. Do not cause a scene.”

Rio’s smirk faltered, she blinked, visibly caught off guard by Agatha’s use of her first name in such a professional setting. Her lips parted as though she might say something, but instead, she pressed them into a thin line, her teasing demeanour evaporating. What replaced it was a look of pure determination, one that Agatha couldn’t quite place but that sent a shiver down her spine.

“Understood,” Rio said softly, nodding firmly.

Agatha barely had time to process the strange pull in her chest before Professor Calderu called the meeting to order. “Alright, let’s begin,” Calderu said, her tone brisk as she scanned the room. “We’ve got several proposals to review today. I’ll call your name, and you’ll have a few minutes to summarise your research and make your case. Let’s keep things concise.”

Calderu motioned to the first researcher, a wiry man with glasses. “You’re up.”

He cleared his throat, rising from his chair. “Thank you, Professor Calderu. Our team is focused on mapping activation of cells in the early stages of Parkinson’s. We’re particularly interested in how the inflammatory response may contribute to the disease. Our data suggests that targeted treatments could significantly delay the onset of symptoms.”

The department heads murmured among themselves as Calderu nodded. “Interesting. We’ll discuss allocation shortly. Next?”

A sharp-looking woman with short hair stood. “Our team is investigating development of the brain while a foetus is in the womb, and how problems in this process can lead to an schizophrenia. We believe that there is a developmental aspect to schizophrenia before a child is even born, that there is an issue with the way the cells divide from the point of fertilisation and this can predispose a child to schizophrenia. We intend to use stem cells to replicate the growth of an embryo in order to study this process, with the aim of gaining a better understanding of how schizophrenia manifests.”

The pitches continued, each more ambitious than the last, as the heads debated and assigned portions of the funding to each. Agatha listened carefully, keeping her expression unreadable. Finally, Calderu glanced at her clipboard and called, “Dr. Harkness and Miss Vidal.”

Agatha exhaled slowly, steadying herself. This was her moment. She cleared her throat and glanced around the table, her gaze flickling to each department head in turn. It was all about power and control, Agatha’s forte. She leaned forward, her fingers on the table. “Thank you, Professor Calderu,” she began, her voice steady, calculated. “Our research focuses on a critical but underexplored question: whether seizures act as accelerators for degeneration in Alzheimer’s disease. Specifically, we’re examining how seizures may contribute to increased Tau deposition.”

Calderu’s expression remained impassive, but Agatha caught the flicker of interest in a few of the department heads.

“Our preliminary findings,” Agatha continued, “based on Miss Vidal’s work, suggest a strong correlation. In just one month, we’ve already identified evidence that seizures exacerbate Tau deposition. With further support, we believe this could lead to groundbreaking therapies to slow, or even prevent, Alzheimer’s.”

She glanced at Rio, expecting her usual smirk or quip, but what she saw instead made her voice falter. Rio was staring up at her with wide eyes, her expression completely open and almost awestruck. She looked utterly captivated, as if Agatha’s words were the most profound thing she’d heard.

Agatha felt her pulse quicken, heat rising to her cheeks. She quickly turned her attention back to Calderu and concluded, “With the right funding, I know we can take this project from promising to revolutionary. Thank you.”

Calderu nodded, turning to the other department heads for discussion. Agatha leaned back in her chair. She exhaled and glanced at Rio again, she wasn’t smirking, nor was she wearing her usual air of defiance. Instead, she smiled at Agatha. Genuine, hopeful. Agatha glanced down and saw her fingers tightly crossed in her lap, her knuckles almost turning white from the force. Something about that gesture made Agatha’s heart stutter. It was so pure, almost… cute.

Before she could dwell on the thought, Calderu cleared her throat. “We’ve reached a decision. You’ll be receiving three percent of the department’s funding.”

Agatha froze. “Three percent?” she repeated with a scoff, her voice sharp. “You must be joking.”

Calderu met her glare with a calm, unyielding expression. “Dr. Harkness, your project is promising, but it’s also very new. We need to see more evidence of its potential before committing additional resources.”

Agatha opened her mouth, but no words came out. She couldn’t believe what she was hearing. Then, beside her, Rio stood. “Professor Calderu, you can’t be serious!”

Agatha shot out a hand, tugging at Rio’s arm. “Vidal, sit down,” she hissed. “She’s made her decision, there’s nothing we can do.”

But Rio shook her hand off, her gaze steady and unflinching. “No. I’m sorry, Dr. Harkness, I won’t sit down.” She turned back to Calderu, her voice rising. “With all due respect, Professor Calderu, this is complete bullshit!”

The room let out a collective gasp. Agatha was frozen, all she could go was stare up at Rio. She could feel the eyes of the entire room burning into them, but Rio was undeterred, her voice resolute and fierce.

“You were literally emailing me just yesterday about how incredible you thought our findings were,” Rio said, her voice rising slightly as she gestured toward Calderu. “We have a solid hypothesis. One that could help millions of people. Yes, we only started this project a month ago, but we already have results. Major results. That should count as a strength, not a strike against us!”

Agatha’s pulse was pounding, her hand hovering uselessly at her side as she stared up at Rio. This was not the casual, overconfident Rio she knew. This Rio was passionate, determined, and utterly unapologetic. She wasn’t just angry, she was furious. And it really was doing something terrible to Agatha’s brain. Rio’s cheeks were flushed with anger, her voice was filled with conviction, and to Agatha’s growing horror, she was finding this insanely attractive.

“Miss Vidal,” Calderu began, her tone cool but with a slight edge of warning.

But Rio wasn’t finished. She turned to Agatha, their gazes locking as she pressed on, unwavering. “And don’t even get me started on the fact that Dr. Agatha Harkness is leading this project. Am I the only one who realizes the implications of that?”

Holy shit. Agatha blinked. This girl must be trying to kill her. She really must want Agatha to melt into a puddle on the meeting room floor.

Rio turned to address the room now, her voice loud. “Dr. Harkness is a legend in neuroscience. She has more awards and publications than everyone in this room combined! Any project she's involved in is sure to have everything thought out, every factor accounted for, every variable controlled!”

Oh no.

“This isn’t just some little PhD project. This is someone who knows how to push the boundaries of what’s possible. She is the cutting-edge.” Rio’s voice softened just slightly, her words turning into a challenge as her gaze swept the room. “If you can’t see the potential here, that’s your loss. But I promise you, this project will prove you wrong.” Rio finally sat down, her chest heaving slightly as she stared defiantly at Calderu.

Agatha didn’t know where to look. The sheer intensity of Rio’s defense of their work, of her, had her heart pounding in ways it absolutely should not have been. She was aware of every small detail. The flush on Rio’s cheeks, the slight tremor in her hands, the way she’d said Agatha’s name like it was a badge of honour.

Agatha was well and truly falling apart.

Calderu exhaled slowly, flipping through her notes. “Fine,” she said at last. “Miss Vidal, since you feel so strongly, we’ll increase the allocation. Ten percent.”

Rio’s head shot up, her eyes wide. “Really?”

Calderu gave a curt nod. “But only because I agree that the preliminary data is promising. But do not question my judgement again, Vidal. And don't make me regret this.”

Rio’s face broke into a wide grin, and she turned to Agatha, her eyes lit with joy. It was so genuine that Agatha couldn’t help but return the smile. She bit her bottom lip to keep from laughing outright.

Rio was... un-fucking-believable. As the next researcher began their pitch, Agatha leaned in close to Rio, her voice a whisper. “So much for not causing a scene.”

Rio’s smile faltered, her breath hitching as she glanced around the room. “I’m sorry,” she whispered back, her voice quiet. “I don’t know what came over me, I just-”

Agatha placed a hand on Rio’s arm, cutting her off. Rio looked up sharply, meeting Agatha’s gaze.

“Don’t you dare be sorry, Rio” Agatha said, her tone soft but firm. “You just got us ten percent of the department’s funding. Thank you.”

Rio stared at her, blinking rapidly before a small smile tugged at her lips. She nodded once, the determination in her eyes softening into something that looked almost vulnerable. Agatha leaned back in her seat, but she couldn’t stop the flicker of warmth in her chest. Rio Vidal was going to be the death of her. And, for once, Agatha wasn’t entirely sure she minded.

Chapter End Notes
