chapter 15

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

When the funding meeting finally drew to a close, Agatha stood from her chair with a sigh, smoothing down her blazer. Rio mirrored her movements as she met Agatha’s gaze, her expression unreadable. They fell into step together, walking side by side down the hallway, the only sound was the rhythmic thud of their footsteps, but neither was ready to break the silence just yet. They were still slightly stunned by what had happened.

It was Agatha who finally spoke, her voice calm and professional once more. “Right, if you could head back down to the lab and continue looking through the slides, that would be great.”

Rio turned her head slightly, meeting Agatha’s gaze with that same unshakable confidence. She gave a small nod but said nothing, then began to turn down the corridor leading to the lab. Before Agatha could stop herself, the word slipped out. “Wait.”

Rio paused mid step, glancing back over her shoulder with a raised eyebrow, curiosity lighting her face.

Agatha hesitated for a moment, then steeled herself, forcing her tone into something close enough to composed. “Thank you again. That was… a completely insane thing to do,” she said quietly, a small laugh escaping her lips despite herself. “But it worked. It worked very well.”

Rio’s face softened, the corner of her mouth curling into a knowing smile. She chuckled quietly. “Well,” she said with a small shrug, “usually the most insane ways to do things are the ways that work.” With that, she turned and disappeared down the corridor toward the lab.

Agatha watched her go, the faintest hint of a smile tugging at her lips. Unbelievable, she thought to herself, as she lingered in the hallway, listening to the fading of her footsteps. With a deflated sigh, Agatha turned and headed back to her office.

The door clicked shut behind her and she collapsed into her chair, running her hands over her face. How the hell did I get myself into this mess? Dr. Agatha Harkness, the Wicked Witch of the Lab, cold, calculating, professional. She had built her reputation on control. Yet here she was, falling apart over a girl. It was pathetic. Completely pathetic.

She groaned into her hands, her breath warm against her palms. Forcing the whirlwind of emotions to the back of her mind, she sat up straight, squared her shoulders, and opened her laptop. Her depression and Alzheimer’s proposal was nearly ready for submission. Just a few more tweaks, and she could send it off to journals for peer-review. Agatha latched onto the work like a drowning person reaching for a lifeboat, determined to find any stability she could muster in the data and analysis.

The hours slipped by unnoticed as she lost herself in her writing. Outside, the sun dipped below the horizon, casting the room into shadow. Only the pale glow of her desk lamp lit the stacks of papers and notebooks scattered on her desk. A knock at the door broke her from her focus. She blinked at the screen, momentarily disoriented. “Come in,” she called, finishing the sentence she was typing as the door creaked open.

“Hey,” came Rio’s voice, soft.

Agatha froze mid sentence, her fingers hovering over her keyboard. When she looked up, Rio stood in the doorway, one hand on the frame, her expression relaxed but watchful. That usual air of confidence lingered, but there was something else beneath it tonight, something gentler. Agatha’s stomach tightened.

Gesturing to the chair across from her desk, Agatha cleared her throat. “What’s up, Rio? How are the slides coming along?”

Rio stepped in and took the offered seat, crossing one leg over the other with casual ease. “Great. I’ve gotten through half of the second set. I should be able to finish another one or two slides before I head out tonight.”

Agatha nodded briskly, grateful for the straightforward answer. “That’s good. And they’re all following the same trend? Increased Tau in patients with seizures?”

Rio gave a small nod, her lips twitching upward. “Mm-hmm. Looks like we’ll have solid data to present when we go up to Oxford tomorrow.”

Agatha’s heart sank at the mention of the trip. She had been trying not to think about it, sharing close quarters, hours spent together with the impossibility of avoiding the pull Rio seemed to exert on her. But now, with Rio sitting here, her presence filling the room in a way that felt impossible to ignore, the thought was unbearable.

Agatha forced herself to clear her throat, her fingers tightening around the edge of her desk as if the solid wood might anchor her. The room suddenly felt unbearably small, the air dense with unspoken tension. She glanced at Rio, who sat sprawled in the chair opposite her, exuding her usual casualness. Her dark eyes were bright with curiosity, her head tilting ever so slightly as if to encourage Agatha to speak.

“Rio, the other night…” The words came out rougher than she intended, her voice betraying the nerves she had tried to conceal. Rio’s eyebrows lifted in surprise, and Agatha caught the faintest flicker of amusement in her expression. She leaned forward, her interest clearly piqued. Agatha’s chest tightened at the shift, her heart thudding a little harder against her ribs. She took a steadying breath, willing her voice to stay even. “I’m sorry. I shouldn’t have done that. It was inappropriate. An abuse of my power.”

The corner of Rio’s mouth quirked upward, her lips curling into a sly smirk that sent a wave of frustration and something else, something dangerous, coursing through Agatha. “An abuse of power?” Rio repeated, her voice teasing and low, almost a whisper “Really? The way I remember it, you weren’t exactly in a position of power, Agatha.”

Agatha’s jaw tightened, the heat rising to her cheeks betraying the irritation she had meant to suppress. Of course she had to make this difficult. “Can you just be quiet and let me finish,” she snapped, though her tone lacked any bite.

Rio didn’t respond, instead sitting back in her chair, her smirk unwavering. The movement made her look even more relaxed, as if she knew she had the upper hand, and it set Agatha on edge.

Still, Agatha pressed on, her voice slow and calm despite her racing pulse. “Look, I won’t deny that I wanted it to happen. But it can’t happen again.” She shifted in her seat, her gaze locking onto Rio’s. The words felt heavy as they left her lips, but she forced herself to keep speaking. “It would be disastrous for the lab, for both ours careers, for the research. Do you understand?”

For a moment, Rio didn’t answer. She just stared at Agatha, her sharp features softening as her smirk faded into something quieter, more reflective. The silence stretched between them, crackling with tension so thick it felt tangible. Finally, Rio gave a slow, measured nod. “Of course. Whatever you think is best, Dr. Harkness.”

The way she said the title sent a ripple of unease through Agatha. There was no sarcasm, no teasing lilt. Instead, the words felt like a subtle acknowledgment of boundaries. Boundaries that Agatha wasn’t even sure she wanted to maintain. Maybe, just maybe, she thought, if Rio could respect those boundaries, she could manage to control herself.

But then Rio leaned forward again, her movements deliberate and unhurried, her dark eyes glinting with something unreadable. Her voice was softer now as she said, “What I actually came to talk about was your research. Your depression and Alzheimer’s study.”

Agatha blinked at her , caught off guard. “Oh?”

Rio nodded, her gaze steady. “I know you’ve been focused on our study lately, and I just wanted to make sure it wasn’t interfering with your other work.” Her gaze softened slightly, her lips curving in a faint smile. “If you need help drafting, sending peer review requests, anything, I’d be happy to pitch in. I wouldn’t want your own paper to suffer because you’re stuck babysitting me.”

The offer struck Agatha like a slap. For a moment, she could only stare at Rio, unsure how to respond. She wasn’t used to this genuine, thoughtful side of her that seemed to slip through when she least expected it. It was disarming, and worse, it made her chest ache with something she couldn’t quite name. Then, unexpectedly, a small laugh escaped her. “That’s kind of you, Rio, but I’ve handled multiple projects simultaneously before. I’ll be fine.” Rio’s smile grew, a warmth in her expression that left Agatha feeling strangely vulnerable. Vulnerable enough to add “But if I ever need an extra hand, I know where to find you. Thank you for the offer.”

The silence that followed felt heavy with things unsaid. Rio’s gaze lingered, and Agatha could feel her resolve slipping under the weight of it. Finally, Rio gave a small nod and stood up, her usual smirk returning. “Well, goodnight, Dr. Harkness. I’ll see you tomorrow.”

Agatha watched her leave, her footsteps echoing faintly in the quiet corridor beyond. The moment the door clicked shut, Agatha let out a long breath and dropped her forehead to the desk with a soft thud. Oh god. What the hell am I doing?

Her mind raced, spiralling too fast for her to catch hold of any single thought. She could just about handle Rio’s teasing, her sharp tongue, her relentless smirks. But this? This side of Rio, earnest, warm, and so annoyingly thoughtful, was going to undo her entirely.

Her pulse was still hammering, and Agatha could feel the flutter in her chest, the anxious knot tightening deeper with every second. She rubbed her face roughly with both hands, trying to stave off the overwhelming heat that had rushed to her cheeks. It wasn’t just the words, though, it was everything. The way Rio had looked at her, the genuine concern in her voice. It felt too much, too intense, and for a moment, Agatha felt like she couldn’t breathe, like the walls of her office were closing in on her.

What the hell am I doing? She needed to get a grip. She couldn’t afford to be falling apart like this, especially not over someone like Rio. She had spent years building a reputation for herself as the most controlled, the most focused researcher in the department. But here she was, becomiung a mess over a student, unable to think straight.

She closed her eyes, drawing in a steadying breath, but the image of Rio, the teasing smile, the softness in her gaze, it kept flickering in her mind. Agatha's thoughts spun too fast. She needed distance, something to pull her back from the edge. She could feel the tension coiling in her stomach, the adrenaline still coursing through her veins.

She pushed herself up from the desk, and paced around the room for a moment, trying to regain any semblance of control. Her fingers trembled. Damn it, why was she trembling? She cursed softly under her breath and reached into the drawer for her pack of cigarettes. Yes, typically she would only turn to them after one her mother's calls, but could you really blame her? She was well and truly crashing out over here. Tonight, she needed something, anything, to clear the chaos in her mind.

She shrugged on her coat, making her way to the side door of the lab, the cool evening air offering a temporary escape from the suffocating warmth of her office. The cold stung her cheeks, but it was a welcome distraction from the mess she was in. She lit the cigarette with a flick of her lighter and inhaled, smoke filling her lungs. For a moment, she felt the tension ease, just enough to gather her thoughts.

But the reprieve was short-lived. She heard the door behind her creak open, and the sound of footsteps on the concrete made her stiffen instinctively. She didn’t need to turn around to know who it was.

“Rio,” Agatha groaned, her frustration spilling out as she let her head fall back dramatically with another loud groan, closing her eyes in exasperation. “What are you doing here?”

She could hear Rio’s quiet chuckle behind her before she even turned to face her. When she did, she found Rio standing in the doorway, her posture easy and confident.

“Same as you, by the looks of it.” Rio’s smirk was sly, knowing, as she took a few steps forward. “Why? Trying to avoid me?”

Agatha glared at her, but her heart was racing again, pulse thudding in her ears as Rio stepped closer to her. Stop this. Just stop, she told herself. But Rio’s gaze was steady, so intent, that Agatha couldn’t look away. She took another drag from her cigarette, exhaling slowly as she tried (and failed) to compose herself.

Rio cocked an eyebrow. There was a teasing edge to her voice. “What happened to ‘not being a smoker,’ Dr Harkness?”

Agatha exhaled, the smoke curling around her as she turned her gaze back to Rio. “I told you, I’m not. I just needed to clear my head.”

Rio’s eyes narrowed slightly, a small laugh escaping her. She stepped even closer, her voice dropping low. “Clear your head, huh? So… I’ve driven you to substance use? Is that what you’re telling me?”

Agatha let out a sharp laugh. She muttered, “Shut up,” Her pulse getting quicker and quicker as Rio tilted her head and ran her tongue over her bottom teeth in that effortless way that drove Agatha insane. The tightness in her chest returned, and her breath caught. Damn her. Damn her.

Rio chuckled softly, her voice barely above a whisper as she spoke. “What can I say? I just have that effect, I guess.”

Rio laughed, running a hand through her hair as she ran her tongue over her teeth yet again. And suddenly, Agatha’s knees were weak. Her head was reeling. Her thoughts jumbled. She couldn’t take this anymore. Before she could even think, before she could stop herself, she moved.

In one swift motion, she grabbed Rio’s collar and shoved her back against the cold brick wall of the building. Her lips crashed into Rio’s, hot, desperate, unrelenting. Silencing every thought, every reservation. Agatha’s mind was a blur of chaos and heat, but her body was surprisingly still, her movements controlled as she pressed Rio harder against the cold wall. Rio gasped into Agatha’s mouth as Agatha kissed her with purpose, her lips crashing into hers with so much force that there was no room for hesitation or second thoughts. There was no softness to it, no tentative exploration, Agatha was taking back control of everything that had been spiralling from her grasp over the last few days. The tension, the longing, all of it poured into the kiss.

Her hands slid from Rio’s collar, settling firmly on the wall either side of her shoulders, holding her in place with an almost possessive grip. Agatha felt the warmth of Rio’s body against her own, the firm press of her chest, and it ignited something deeper, something primal inside her. She really didn’t care that it was wrong. She didn’t care about the consequences. All that mattered in this moment was the pull between them, the one she had been trying to fight for much too long.

Agatha’s lips were insistent, taking what she wanted. She felt Rio tense beneath her for a moment, taken aback, before Rio’s hands finally found her waist, pulling her closer. But Agatha held the upper hand, her body firm against Rio’s, pushing her back into the stone behind her. She could feel Rio’s breath hitch in the space between their lips, the tiny gasp when Agatha nipped at her bottom lip, teasing her, just enough to make her tremble.

Rio’s mouth parted under hers, and Agatha took advantage of the opening, her tongue sliding in to deepen the kiss. There was no hesitation now; Agatha was fully in control. She guided Rio, moving her hands to the back of Rio’s neck to pull her closer, the urgency building with each movement. Agatha could feel Rio’s pulse under her fingertips, the way she responded to every shift in Agatha’s body. Her breath quickened, but Agatha remained steady, her movements deliberate and commanding.

As she pulled back for a brief second, her lips hovering inches from Rio’s, Agatha could see the wildness in her eyes as their gazes met, something raw, untamed, like a fire she had just sparked. Rio’s eyes drifted back to Agatha’s lips as she leaned in, this time more slowly, deeper, more deliberate.

When she finally pulled away again, this time for good, her breath was shaky, but she manageed to meet Rio’s gaze, her eyes dark and intense. Agatha held her there, one hand still grasping her hair and the other flat against the wall above Rio’s shoulder. They were barely an inch apart, their lips still swollen from the kiss. Agatha’s body was still pressed to Rio’s, and she didn’t pull away. Instead, she let the moment hang, the tension lingering in the cold air. Rio was panting slightly, lips parted as if she couldn’t quite catch her breath. She met Agatha’s gaze, her expression a mixture of surprise and amusement. Her lips curled into a slow, knowing smile, and Agatha could see the change there, the shift in the way Rio looked at her.

‘So much for ‘this can never happen again’. I mean-” Rio started with a laugh, still breathless from the kiss, ‘you really have an astounding lack of self-control.’

A smile spread across Agatha’s face as she dropped both hands to Rio’s shoulders, meeting her gaze with a bemused laugh. ‘Tell me about it.’

Agatha tilted her head slightly, her thumbs brushing against the fabric of Rio's shirt as she held her steady. The faint smirk on her lips betrayed more amusement than regret, though her mind was already cataloging the possible consequences of what she’d just done. Still, in this moment, with Rio pinned beneath her, eyes bright with mischief, it was hard to feel anything but exhilaration.

Rio’s grin widened, her chest still rising and falling heavily as she caught her breath. She tilted her head, eyes sharp and playful. "You know, for someone who’s supposed to be my boss, you’ve got a real habit of breaking all your own rules."

Agatha raised an eyebrow, her fingers flexing slightly where they rested on Rio’s shoulders. The corner of her mouth tugged upward in a faint smirk. "And for someone who claims to be a model PhD student, you have a remarkable talent for provoking your boss into doing so."

Rio laughed softly, the sound low and warm in the chilly night air. "Provoking? Is that what we’re calling it now?" She leaned in just enough for Agatha to feel the brush of her breath, her voice dropping. "I think you might be giving me too much credit."

"Credit where credit is due." Agatha replied, her voice steady. "Maybe you’re infuriating, insubordinate, and entirely too smug for your own good. Yet, here we are."

Rio straightened, her own smirk never wavering. "You make it sound like I’m the one who dragged you out here and-" She gestured vaguely to the space between them, lips quirking upward. "-pinned you to the wall."

Agatha rolled her eyes, though the flush creeping up her neck betrayed her. "God, you’re insufferable," she muttered, but there was no real bite to the words. “And don’t act so innocent. You know exactly what you’re doing, Rio. You’ve been pushing my buttons since the day you walked into this lab.”

Rio laughed at that, the sound warm and unguarded, and for a moment, it disarmed Agatha completely. “You’re not wrong,” Rio admitted, “But I didn’t think you’d ever snap like that. I underestimated you, Dr. Harkness.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow, “Well, now you know. Push me far enough, and I push back.”

Rio let out a laugh. “Well, yes. I can see that now.” She said, her smirk widening as she shifted gestured to where Agatha still had her pushed back against the wall.

“Don’t even start,” Agatha warned, though the edge in her voice was softened by the faintest hint of a smile. She let her hands slip from Rio’s shoulders, brushing down her arms before finally stepping back to finally put some distance between them, though it felt harder than it should have. Her pulse was still racing, and she could feel the heat of Rio’s gaze on her even as she tried to compose herself. She folded her arms across her chest, fixing Rio with a look that was equal parts stern and amused.

Rio watched her closely, her smirk fading into something more serious. “So, what now?” she asked, her voice quieter but no less challenging. “Do we just pretend this didn’t happen? Just go up to Oxford tomorrow and act like you didn’t just… kiss me senseless out here?”

Agatha hesitated, her hands falling to her sides. She looked at Rio, really looked at her. The flushed cheeks, the way her chest still rose and fell with uneven breaths. She felt a pang of something she couldn’t quite name, something dangerously close to affection.

“That’s exactly what we do,” Agatha said finally, her voice firm despite the knot tightening in her stomach. “We move on. This-” she gestured between them, her lips pressing into a thin line, “-was a lapse in judgment.” But the moment she said the words she regretted them, she could already see the glint of amusement in Rio’s eyes, the way her lips quirked into that insufferable smirk.

“A lapse in judgment, huh?” Rio mused, drawing the words out with mock solemnity as she tapped her chin. “Now, where have I heard that before?” She made an exaggerated show of looking around, her eyes scanning the alley until they landed to their right. With a dramatic snap of her fingers, she pointed to the spot just to their right, where Agatha distinctly remembered their first almost-kiss. “Oh!” Rio exclaimed, her voice thick with playful innocence. “Right there, actually.”

Agatha crossed her arms tightly over her chest, as if that could shield her from the flood of heat rising to her face. “You’re enjoying this far too much.”

Rio turned back to her, grin wide “Can you blame me? You’re usually so untouchable. Watching you fall apart like this…it’s fascinating.”

“Fall apart?” Agatha repeated, her voice sharp as she straightened her spine. “I’m not falling apart.”

Rio’s smirk widened. “Aren’t you? Because, for someone who insists this was a mistake, you seem awfully… invested in justifying it.”

Agatha took a deliberate step closer, her heels clicking against the tile with a precision that matched the steely determination in her gaze. "What may or may not be invested in is none of your concern, Rio.”

Rio just raised an eyebrow, letting out a small scoff, “Oh, really? So what do you suggest we do next then, just completely ignore whatever this is?”

Agatha’s jaw tightened, she took a slow, deliberate step forward, closing the gap between them once again. She met Rio’s gaze head-on, her expression calm but unyielding. “What we do next is we both forget this ever happened. You go home, and I… I get back to work."

Rio chuckled, her head tilting slightly as she watched Agatha. "You’re really something, you know that? All business, even after…" She gestured vaguely between them, her smirk returning. "Whatever that was."

Agatha didn’t rise to the bait. Instead, she crossed her arms and gave Rio a pointed look. "I mean it, Rio. If you respect me at all, you’ll leave this alone."

Rio studied her for a long moment, her expression unreadable. Then, with a slow nod, she took a step back, her smirk softening into something gentler. “Alright, if that’s what you want.”

“It is,” Agatha replied, though the words felt hollow even as she said them.

Rio hesitated, her gaze lingering on Agatha for just a fraction too long before she turned toward the door. “Goodnight, Agatha,” she said over her shoulder, her tone softer now, almost… tender.

“Goodnight, Rio,” Agatha murmured, watching her leave. As the door clicked shut, she let out a breath she hadn’t realised she was holding. Her chest ached with the weight of everything that had happened. The tension getting tighter with every passing second.

chapter 16

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

The late afternoon sun cast a glow over Marylebone station as Agatha stood on the platform, her small suitcase at her side, one hand gripping the handle while the other fiddled absentmindedly with the edge of her scarf. She checked her watch and sighed.

Where was Rio?

Her gaze swept over the platform as she tugged her black trench coat tighter around herself. Irritation prickled at her, but it was laced with something less familiar. Anticipation, perhaps. Just then, a flash of movement caught her eye. Rio emerged from the stream of travellers, her stride casual. She raised one hand in a small wave, a smile starting to tug at her lips. Agatha felt her breath hitch before she could reign in her reaction.

Rio approached, her bag slung over her shoulder. She was a vision of effortlessness, faded blue jeans, a black tank top that clung to her frame, and a loose leather jacket that shifted with each step. Agatha’s mouth went dry. This is going to be a very long two days.

“Sorry I’m late,” Rio said, her eyes flicking over Agatha briefly, “Blame the Tube.” she wrapped her scarf tighter, shoving her free hand into the pocket of her jacket. “Fuck, it is freezing!” she muttered, her teeth flashing in a quick grin.

Agatha allowed a soft laugh to escape her. “Hello to you too.” she said, pulling her scarf tighter around her neck. “You know,” Agatha continued, unable to keep the amusement out of her voice, “If you wore something warmer than a tank top, you might not be so freezing.”

Rio stopped, one eyebrow quirking as her smirk grew. “What, not a fan of my outfit?”

Agatha froze for a second before recovering, though she could feel a faint blush creeping up her neck. She tilted her head, her lips curving into a small smirk of her own. “I didn’t say that.” She paused, letting her words hang in the air. “I can definitely imagine you in a band now. It’s hard to picture it with the clothes you wear to the lab.”

Rio chuckled, her voice low, sending an slight shiver down Agatha’s spine. “Oh, so you think I don’t dress grungy enough in the lab? Should I be wearing combat boots and ripped jeans every day? Maybe add a nose ring for good measure?”

“Yes, that’s exactly what I think you should wear,” Agatha shot back, “Much more professional.”

Rio grinned as they started to walk toward the train. Agatha felt Rio’s gaze on her but refused to meet it, focusing instead on the rhythm of her heels clicking against the platform. When they reached the train, Agatha stepped aside, gesturing for Rio to go first. "After you," she said.

Rio laughed as Agatha met her gaze finally. "Oh, how kind." she teased, climbing aboard. She turned back to Agatha, holding her hand out with an exaggerated bow. "Your turn, m’lady."

Agatha blinked, momentarily stunned. She rolled her eyes as she finally took Rio’s hand and stepped onto the train, ‘You’re insufferable.’ She muttered, brushing past her to find their seats.

"Admit it," Rio said as she followed. "You’d miss it if I wasn’t."

Agatha didn't dignify that with a response., Instead, she just continued to walk down the train car. When they reached an empty table, Agatha stepped aside, offering a hand to Rio. “Here, let me-”

“I’ve got it,” Rio interrupted, waving her off with an easy shrug. She hoisted her duffel bag into the overhead shelf with an ease that made Agatha’s breath hitch. Agatha shook her head, trying to calm her mind and took her seat by the window, carefully placing her suitcase beside her.

Rio flung herself into the seat opposite, shrugging off her leather jacket and tossing it next to her. The movement revealed a tattoo on her left shoulder. A swirling, intricate design of ivy and vines inked in delicate lines. It wasn’t large, but it drew Agatha’s attention. Her gaze lingered much longer than she intended.

"You're staring," Rio said suddenly, her tone teasing. Her signature smirk spread across her face as she cocked an eyebrow.

Agatha startled, flicking her gaze up quickly. "I’m not," she blurted, though her voice lacked its usual steadiness. She adjusted the scarf around her neck, as though it could mask her faltering composure.

Rio chuckled, leaning back in her seat with an air of triumph. "Wow. You almost sounded half convincing. You’re getting better at this."

Agatha rolled her eyes, but a laugh slipped past her lips, softening her sharpness. "Fine," she admitted, tilting her head slightly as her eyes flicked back to the tattoo, this time with less hesitation. "So, when did you get that done?"

Rio’s smirk widened as she leaned forward, resting her elbows on the table between them. "Which one?" she asked, her voice playful.

Agatha blinked. "There’s more?" She had tried not to let her surprise show, but her raised eyebrows betrayed her curiosity.

"Maybe," Rio said, a teasing lilt in her voice. "Depends on how much you want to know."

Agatha scoffed but couldn’t suppress the smile that tugged at her lips. "Let’s stick with the visible one for now," she said, gesturing toward Rio’s shoulder.

Rio tilted her head as if considering how much to reveal. "Got it when I was eighteen. Some friends and I were backpacking through Spain, and we found this tiny studio in Barcelona. The artist barely spoke English, and I was the only one of my friends who spoke Spanish." She laughed, the sound warm, and Agatha found herself leaning forward without meaning to. "I wasn’t even planning on getting a tattoo. But after translating for my friends for hours, the artist asked me if I wanted anything, so I thought.. fuck it, why not? I had been wanting this design and it just seemed like a perfect moment. It’s the only tattoo I’ve got that actually means something."

Agatha’s curiosity piqued. "And what does it mean?" she asked, her tone casual, though she was keenly aware of the weight behind her question.

Rio shrugged, but there was a softness to her expression now, her usual bravado momentarily dimmed. "Growth. Making my mark on the world, I guess." she said simply, running her fingers lightly over the ink. "It was right after I got my Bachelor’s. I was so excited to make a difference in the field." She let out a long sigh, “Ivy grows in any conditions, it asserts itself and makes it’s mark. I wanted to remind myself that I could do the same with my research.’

Agatha’s chest tightened at the quiet sincerity in Rio’s voice. It was rare for her to see this side of her, the Rio who wasn’t always smirking or teasing, who carried something deeper beneath the surface. She didn’t know what to say, so she settled for a simple nod. "It suits you," she said softly.

Rio’s gaze snapped back to her, something unreadable flashing in her dark eyes. "Yeah?" she said as a small smile grew on her face. “Well, what about you? You hiding any tattoos?”

Agatha hesitated for the briefest moment, her lips quirking into a coy smile. "Maybe," she said, her voice light but deliberate.

Rio’s eyebrows shot up, her smirk morphing into something closer to genuine surprise. "Maybe?" she repeated, clearly not expecting her answer.

"That’s all you’re getting," Agatha said smoothly, sitting straighter and folding her hands in her lap as if the conversation were already over.

Rio narrowed her eyes, her arms and tilting her head as she studied Agatha. "Alright, now I’m intrigued. What is it? A butterfly? A little heart somewhere discreet? Or, wait-" Her grin turned wicked. "Is it something scandalous?"

Agatha gave an exasperated laugh, shaking her head. "You are so dramatic."

"So you do have one!" Rio pointed an accusing finger at her, grin widening. "Come on, you can’t just say 'maybe' and then leave me hanging. Where is it?"

Agatha held her ground, raising an unimpressed eyebrow. "Do you really think I’m going to tell you that?"

Rio leaned back, folding her hands behind her head with a mock sigh. "You’re no fun. I tell you the heartfelt story behind my tattoo, and you won’t even throw me a hint.” Rio leaned forward as she continued with her overdramatic pleading, "You can’t just drop a ‘maybe’ and not at least tell me where it is."

Agatha allowed a moment to stretch between them before meeting Rio’s gaze. "You will never be finding out where it is."

Rio leaned back in her seat, her smirk returning in full force, but there was a new glint in her eyes, something teasing. "We’ll see about that," she said, her voice low and deliberate.

The words sent a jolt through Agatha, and for a second, her thoughts raced. The ease of Rio’s confidence, the implication in her tone was maddening, unsettling, and yet... thrilling. Images she didn’t dare entertain flitted through her mind, and she had to force herself to look out the window to regain her composure. She focused on the passing scenery outside the window as if it could ground her.

"Confident as always," Agatha said finally, managing to keep her voice steady, though her fingers fidgeted with the edge of her scarf.

Rio sat back again, clearly pleased with herself. "It’s one of my best qualities," she said with a wink.

Agatha laughed softly, shaking her head. "And humility is right up there with it, I assume?"

"Naturally," Rio quipped, her grin unrepentant.

Agatha stole a quick glance at Rio, who was now leaning back in her seat with an air of victory. For all her overconfidence, there was something disarming about her. Agatha hated how easily she found herself drawn in, and how much she didn’t hate it at all.

The train continued to rumble along, the scenery outside blurring into shades of green and gold, but Agatha barely noticed. Her thoughts kept circling back to Rio’s words, her tone, the way her dark eyes seemed to catch every flicker of emotion Agatha tried to suppress. It was going to be a long two days.

Rio stretched lazily, her arms reaching high above her head. The movement caused her tank top to ride up slightly, revealing a narrow strip of tanned skin between the hem and her jeans. Agatha’s eyes flicked down before she could stop herself. Heat flared in her cheeks, and she quickly looked away, pretending to adjust her scarf.

Rio lowered her arms, catching Agatha’s fleeting movement out of the corner of her eye. A small smirk tugged at her lips, but she said nothing, grabbing her leather jacket and scarf from the seat beside her. She slung the jacket over one shoulder with practiced ease, pulling her scarf loosely around her neck. Agatha followed suit, smoothing out her coat and wrapping her scarf snugly against the chill she knew awaited them.

They stepped off the train together, the crisp evening air biting at their faces. The platform was busy but not overwhelmingly so, a mix of students, tourists, and the occasional professional briskly moving through the crowd.

As they exited the station, the city opened up before them in all its postcard-perfect charm. The streets were lined with townhouses and cobblestones that glistened faintly from recent rain. Agatha’s gaze lingered on the quaint facades of the houses, lit by orange street lamps in the darkness of the evening.

They walked in comfortable silence for a while, their footsteps falling in sync as they navigated the narrow pavements. The occasional breeze stirred fallen leaves, and Agatha took a moment to appreciate the serenity of the city.

“Have you spent much time in Oxford?” Rio’s voice broke the silence, light but curious. Agatha glanced at her, there was genuine interest in her expression.

“Well, I did my master’s at Oxford, so yes,” Agatha replied. “I was up here for a few years. I didn’t love it, to be honest. There’s not much going on compared to London.”

Rio tilted her head. “Huh. So you must know a few people at the Uni, then?”

Agatha nodded, tucking a stray strand of hair behind her ear. “Most of the neuroscience faculty, yes. Though the lab we’re visiting is new, so I don’t know anyone there. Still, it’ll be nice to catch up with some old friends. I’m meeting a woman I studied with for breakfast tomorrow, actually.”

Rio stopped in her tracks, placing a hand dramatically over her chest, her expression dramatically wounded. “So you’re deserting me? Wow, Dr. Harkness, I’m crushed. And here I thought we were bonding.”

Agatha rolled her eyes, though she couldn’t suppress the small smile tugging at her lips. “It’s breakfast, Rio. You’ll survive an hour or two without me.”

“Will I, though?” Rio replied, her voice dripping with exaggerated despair. “I mean, what will I do?”

“You seem perfectly capable of entertaining yourself,” Agatha said dryly, though her tone was more amused than cutting.

Rio’s grin widened. “True, but it’s more fun with you around. You keep me on my toes.”

Agatha felt warmth rise in her cheeks and turned her attention back to the street ahead. “I’m sure you’ll manage just fine,” she said briskly, trying to shake the strange fluttering in her chest. She quickened her pace slightly, hoping Rio wouldn’t notice the faint pink blooming on her face. Stop it, Agatha.

The faint hum of conversation mixed with the sound of a crackling fireplace. Striding up to the front desk, she offered the receptionist a polite but clipped smile.

“We’re checking in. It’s under Harkness. ”

The woman behind the desk nodded cheerfully. “Perfect, just a second,” she said, her fingers flying across the keyboard. After a moment, she reached under the counter and handed Agatha a single key card with a pleasant smile. “Here you are!”

Agatha frowned slightly but said nothing at first. Turning to hand the key to Rio, who was leaning casually against her suitcase with a smirk already forming, Agatha glanced back toward the receptionist, expecting another key to follow. The receptionist raised an eyebrow at her, smile still wide. “Oh, did you want two keys for the room?”

Agatha stared, blinking back at her in bewilderment. “What do you mean ‘room,’ singular?”

The woman hesitated, looking back at her screen. “You’re down for one room with two queen beds. Is that not correct?”

Behind her, Agatha heard the unmistakable sound of Rio snickering. She didn’t bother turning around, instead hissing through gritted teeth, “Please shut up.”

Rio’s laughter only grew more amused, but Agatha ignored it, turning her full attention back to the receptionist. Her lips pressed into a thin line as she crossed her arms over her chest, the stance both calculated and reflexive. What the hell was this incompetence?

“No… Jocelyn ,” Agatha said, reading the name off the badge on her shirt, her voice dripping with irritation. She leaned slightly forward, tone sharpening, “That is not correct.”

Jocelyn visibly shrank under Agatha’s glare. “I- I’m so sorry, Miss Harkness-”

“ Dr. Harkness,” Agatha snapped, cutting her off.

Rio snorted behind her, the sound low and unrepentant. Jocelyn looked like she wanted the floor to swallow her whole, but Agatha wasn’t about to let up.

“Dr. Harkness,” Jocelyn corrected hurriedly, her voice trembling slightly. “I really do apologise, but we’re fully booked. There’s nothing I can do!”

Agatha scoffed, rolling her eyes so hard it was a wonder they didn’t disappear into the back of her head. She glared at Jocelyn one last time, enough to leave the poor woman trembling, and then spun on her heel, striding briskly toward the lift.

Behind her, Rio’s soft laughter followed like a shadow.

“You are enjoying this far too much,” Agatha said, throwing a pointed glare over her shoulder as the elevator doors slid open.

Rio’s grin widened as she tugged her bag along and stepped into the lift behind Agatha, the doors sliding shut. “Oh, immensely.” Rio replied, her voice buzzing with amusement.

Agatha turned her gaze forward, resolutely ignoring Rio who leaned against the wall, her laughter simmering into a smirk that Agatha refused to acknowledge. “Don’t even start,” Agatha said, raising a finger as Rio opened her mouth. Her tone was cutting, her eyes narrowed. “I do not want to hear whatever smart-ass comment you feel is necessary in this moment.”

Rio feigned an offended gasp, her hand pressed dramatically to her chest. “Wow. You think so little of me,” she said.

Agatha turned to meet her gaze, expecting another sarcastic quip. But Rio’s expression had shifted, her smirk morphing into something far more dangerous. She was leaning casually against the wall, her jacket slipping off one shoulder to reveal the edge of her tattoo on her collarbone. Her hair was slightly tousled from the wind, and her dark eyes gleamed with mischief.

Agatha swallowed hard, forcing herself to look back at the elevator doors.

“I was simply going to point out that I’m sure you can manage being a few meters away from me for two days…” Rio continued, pushing off the wall and closing the space between them in one measured step. Agatha was forced to meet her gaze again as her voice dipped lower, intimate and deliberate. “…I mean, given you had your tongue down my throat just last night, Agatha. ”

Agatha’s breath hitched. Her chest tightened, her face heating with a mix of fury and something far more unwelcome. She opened her mouth to respond, but no words came, her sharp wit momentarily silenced by the audacity of the woman standing too close, looking too smug, and speaking too softly.

How dare she.

Agatha’s jaw tightened, her eyes narrowing at Rio as the elevator hummed softly around them. The air between them felt stifling, charged, and unbearably intimate. Agatha straightened her posture, pulling herself out of the gravitational pull Rio seemed to radiate effortlessly. She refused to let her composure slip further, but even now, she could feel the heat in her chest, the remnants of last night that still clung to her like a second skin.

“That was a slip,” Agatha said firmly, her voice steady despite the rush of heat on her skin. The doors of the lift chimed and opened, and Agatha stepped out quickly, striding down the hallway with more purpose than she actually felt. She hoped her confidence would mask the lingering chaos inside her. “It was a lapse in-”

“A lapse in judgment, yes, we’ve been over this,” Rio’s voice called from behind her. “It’s getting old.”

Agatha’s pace faltered for a moment, but she caught herself, determined not to show any weakness. She reached the door to their room and turned with a swift motion to face Rio. “Well, it’s true. It was a lapse in judgment,” Agatha shot back, her words sharp but controlled. She held Rio’s gaze with an intensity she hoped would ward off any further teasing.

Rio’s grin deepened, her posture relaxed as she leaned a hand on the wall beside the door, her body angled toward Agatha in an infuriatingly casual way. Her voice was low, almost teasing. “Okay. I’m not arguing with that. Just… curious as to when your judgment might lapse again?”

Agatha’s breath caught at the implication, her chest tightening. She scoffed, turning the key in the door with unnecessary force. "It won’t," she said, almost too quickly, as she stepped into the room, not sparing Rio another glance.

Rio followed her inside, and Agatha heard the soft rustle of her suitcase hitting the floor behind her. Agatha turned to face the room, but her gaze shifted involuntarily Rio. Agatha’s coughed, making her voice as cold as she could manage, the last thread of her patience unraveling. “Just stay on your side of this room, and everything will be fine.”

Rio scoffed dramatically, flopping down on the bed furthest from the door, her body sprawling out with complete ease. “Mm-hmm. Whatever you want to believe.”

Agatha didn’t respond, instead moving toward her own bed, keeping her distance. But before she could fully retreat, Rio propped herself up on one elbow, her smirk widening. She laughed to herself, clearly amused, then leaned toward Agatha with exaggerated theatrics. “But I’d give it three hours at most before you jump me.”

Agatha froze, the words hitting her like a punch to the stomach. She stared at Rio, speechless for a moment, and then quickly turned away, though her heart thudded painfully in her chest. She couldn’t believe what Rio was saying, couldn’t believe how casually she was making her feel so exposed.

Rio continued, her voice low and mocking. “Can you at least give me a little more warning before you slam me into a wall this time? Maybe I should wear a back brace or something. I mean, you could seriously damage my spine, Agatha.”

Agatha scoffed, trying to ignore the flutter of frustration mixed with something else… something far more dangerous. She crossed her arms over her chest, standing tall even though her insides were boiling. She refused to let Rio get to her, the words that escaped her were sharp and deliberate. “Someone’s getting very comfortable using my first name. You really think you should address your teacher like that?”

Rio raised an eyebrow, as though daring Agatha to go further. “You really think you can comment on my professionalism, after pinning me to a fucking wall for God knows how long last night?” she shot back with a laugh, leaning back against the headboard.

The audacity. Agatha’s face flushed with both anger and embarrassment, her body stiffening at the reminder of last night. She knew it had been a moment of weakness she shouldn’t entertain, but the memory of Rio’s lips against hers still lingered like a shadow. The idea of admitting any of this aloud was unthinkable, so she said nothing. Instead, she turned away, her hands clenching into fists at her sides as she tried to focus on something, anything, other than Rio’s proximity.

The tension in the room thickened as Agatha remained silent, unwilling to give Rio the satisfaction of another response. But she could feel the weight of Rio’s gaze on her, the insistent pull of her presence that made it impossible to simply forget. Rio laughed, a low, self-satisfied sound that told Agatha she was well aware of the effect she was having on her. And Agatha wasn’t sure whether she wanted to strangle her or kiss her again.

Agatha scoffed and turned her attention to her suitcase, unzipping it with sharp, precise movements. "Whatever," she muttered, more to herself than to Rio. "Let’s just go to bed."

Rio, who had been lounging on her bed, immediately sat up. “But we haven’t eaten,” she pointed out, her voice light and teasing but with a hint of genuine concern. “Come on, you must be hungry. Let’s get food. I promise I won’t be annoying.”

Agatha glanced over her shoulder at her, eyebrow raised in a skeptical arch. “I highly doubt that,” she said dryly, but her stomach growled faintly, betraying her resolve. She sighed. “Fine. It’s late, though. Nothing will be open.”

Rio grinned triumphantly, already pulling out her phone and typing with quick, confident motions. She looked up a moment later, her eyes gleaming with excitement. “There’s a Burger King just around the corner. We could grab food there.”

Agatha froze mid-motion, an incredulous expression creeping across her face. She turned fully to look at Rio, her arms crossed tightly over her chest. “Burger King?” she repeated, her voice laced with disdain. “No way in hell.”

Rio laughed, a low, melodic sound, and hopped up from the bed. She crossed the room in a few quick steps, her movements light and unbothered, and grabbed Agatha’s arms with both hands. Before Agatha could protest, Rio was tugging her up, a playful energy radiating from her. “Come on, Agatha,” Rio cajoled, grinning up at her like an overeager child. “It’s all that’s open, and I’m starving. And it’s not even that bad. Don’t be a snob.”

Agatha tried to hold her ground, to glare and resist the infectious energy that Rio seemed to carry everywhere with her. But the sheer enthusiasm on Rio’s face chipped away at her resolve. Agatha could feel the corners of her own mouth twitching upward despite herself.

She let out a reluctant laugh, shaking her head as she finally gave in. “Fine,” she said, rolling her eyes but unable to suppress the small smile tugging at her lips. “Let’s go.”

Rio whooped victoriously, already letting go of Agatha to grab her jacket. “See?” she said, throwing it on and grabbing her wallet. “You’re not so impossible after all.”

Agatha shook her head again, suppressing a chuckle as she grabbed her coat. “Don’t push your luck, Vidal,” she warned, her voice sharp but softened by the amusement that lingered in her tone.

Rio held the door open for her, bowing dramatically as Agatha stepped past her into the hallway. “Wouldn’t dream of it, Dr. Harkness,” Rio said, her voice dripping with playful sarcasm.

As they made their way out of the hotel and into the cool night air, Agatha couldn’t help but feel the weight of the tension between them lightening for a moment. Rio walked beside her, hands stuffed into her jacket pockets, her energy calmer now but no less magnetic. Agatha glanced at her out of the corner of her eye, her thoughts a swirling mix of irritation and curiosity. For someone who could drive her to the edge of her patience, Rio also had a way of disarming her in ways she hadn’t expected.

chapter 17

Chapter Notes

I AM SO SORRY THAT ITS BEEN SO LONG SINCE CH16!!! this week is crazy ive had sooo many things to do but its here finally I hope u enjoyyy!!!!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

The park across the street from the Burger King was quiet and nearly empty, except for the rustling leaves and the faint hum of distant traffic. Agatha and Rio settled onto a bench beneath a glowing streetlamp, its warm light casting soft shadows on their faces. The smell of freshly fried food wafted between them as they unwrapped their burgers, the crinkle of paper loud in the still night.

Rio was the first to dig in, tearing into her burger eagerly. She let out a muffled groan of delight, her voice low. “Ugh, that’s fucking amazing.”

Agatha paused mid-unwrapping, glancing over at Rio. She was entirely absorbed in her food, her expression a mix of bliss and focus as she chewed. A smile tugged at Agatha’s lips before she could stop it, a small laugh escaping her. “Slow down,” she said, shaking her head. “You’ll choke.”

Rio looked up at her, mouth still full, eyes wide with exaggerated innocence. “But I’m hungry ,” she said through her full cheeks, her voice muffled but insistent.

Agatha couldn’t help but laugh again, louder this time, her head leaning back slightly as the sound bubbled out. The moment felt strange, easy, and almost too natural. Like slipping into an old habit she hadn’t known she missed.

Shaking her head with a faint smile, she finally took a bite of her own burger. She chewed slowly, then nodded in reluctant approval. “Oh wow, that is good.”

Rio laughed, triumphant, and nudged her shoulder lightly. “See? I told you you’d like it!”

The silence between them stretched comfortably for a few moments, broken only by the faint hum of the city and occasional rustle of leaves in the soft breeze. Agatha took another bite as her eyes flicked to Rio. She had finished her food and was licking her lips absentmindedly, utterly unaware of the way the streetlamp’s glow softened her features. Her hair shifted slightly in the wind, tousling just enough to make her look effortlessly beautiful.

Agatha’s breath hitched. A quiet, unconscious reaction she immediately cursed herself for. Rio noticed, of course. She always noticed. Her smirk appeared, a brief flash of amusement across her face before it softened into something more genuine. Her eyes lit with curiosity as she turned slightly toward Agatha. “So,” Rio began, her tone casual but tinged with mischief, “this seems like a good moment to tell me about your mysterious tattoo.”

Agatha groaned, rolling her eyes. “Wow. Will you give it a rest?”

“Nope.” Rio said, leaning closer and resting her chin in her hand, her smile growing. “Please?” she added, batting her lashes with an overdramatic pout.

Agatha sighed, setting her food wrappers down on the bench next to her. She turned back to Rio, whose expression was nothing short of childlike enthusiasm. Her leg brushed against Rio’s as she turned to face her, the contact sending a jolt through Agatha. She forced herself to focus, clearing her throat.

“You really want to know?” Agatha asked, raising an eyebrow.

Rio nodded eagerly, her grin widening.

“It’s really not as exciting as you think it is, Rio. I promise.” Agatha shook her head and began to unbutton the top of her shirt, her movements deliberate and composed.

Rio’s eyes widened, and she let out a laugh, surprise lacing her voice. “Wow, Agatha. I was joking when I said I’d give it three hours, but, I mean, sure, whatever you want.”

Agatha cut her off with a pointed glare. “Will you shut up ? My clothes are not going anywhere. I’m just trying to show you the tattoo.”

She undid one more button and tugged her collar down just enough to reveal the small, elegant tattoo inked across her sternum: the letter N in swirling, delicate blue lines.

Rio’s laughter stopped as her gaze zeroed in on the expanse of skin that was exposed. Her expression shifted, surprise melting into quiet fascination. Her eyes were wide, her focus unwavering.

Agatha cleared her throat, trying to dispel the heat building in the air between them. “Distracted, are we?” she asked dryly, drawing Rio’s attention back to her face.

Rio smirked, recovering quickly. “So, who’s N ?” she asked, leaning back slightly but still studying the tattoo. A gasp escaped her a moment later, her grin growing mischievous again. “Oh my God. Agatha Harkness, did you get an ex’s initial tattooed on you?”

Agatha let out a small laugh, shaking her head. “No, nothing half as scandalous.” She glanced down at the tattoo and softened, her voice quieter as she explained, “The N is for Nicholas, my son’s name.”

Rio froze, her breath catching. “I didn’t know you have a son.”

Agatha met her gaze slowly, her voice dropping as she corrected, “ Had . I had a son.”

The words hung in the air, heavy and unyielding. Agatha felt tears threatening to surface, but she blinked them back, refusing to let them fall. Across from her, Rio’s face fell, her playful demeanour evaporating in an instant.

“Agatha, I’m- I’m so sorry. I didn’t know.”

Agatha let out a quiet, humourless laugh, shaking her head. “Don’t be silly. Of course you didn’t. I don’t really... tell people about it. I-” She paused, her thoughts drifting back through the years.

The realisation struck her like a sharp blow to the chest. She really hadn’t told anyone. Not since her mother, who had been more critical than comforting. Work colleagues had never been close enough to tell, and friends… well, she hadn’t seen most of her old friends for years. The most defining moment of her life, her deepest wound, and no one but her mother knew. It had loomed over her like a shadow every day for the last five years and… somehow she had not told a single person.

Agatha blinked and met Rio’s gaze again, her voice tinged with disbelief. “Come to think of it, I don’t think I’ve told anyone about it.”

Rio’s expression softened even further, her brows lifting in concern. For a moment, the memory’s weight felt lighter, as if Rio’s quiet presence could ease the ache.

“What... what happened?” Rio asked gently, her voice tentative yet filled with genuine care. “I mean, only if you want to talk about it. I just- I think it might be good for you, you know? To talk to someone.” She shrugged, her eyes never leaving Agatha’s.

Agatha’s heart twisted at the tenderness in Rio’s gaze. She let out a long sigh and began to close her shirt, turning away slightly.

“It was about five years ago,” she said softly, her voice steady despite the tightness in her throat. “He was very sick. There was nothing we could have done, I knew that when he was born. The doctors gave him a year to live, and somehow, he managed six. He was never supposed to live that long. It was a blessing, honestly.” She paused, her fingers trembling slightly as she fastened the last button. “But...”

Her voice cracked, and she swallowed hard, forcing herself to continue. “Still, the fact that it was a miracle he even lived to six doesn’t make it any less painful.”

Agatha stared down at her lap, blinking rapidly in a futile attempt to keep the tears at bay. She wouldn’t look at Rio. Not now, not when the vulnerability she worked so hard to bury was threatening to spill out. She’d already let her guard down far too much around this woman. To let Rio see her cry would be the final blow to her pride.

But then, she felt it. A soft, deliberate touch. Rio’s hand gently brushed a stray strand of hair from Agatha’s face, her fingertips light and careful. Agatha’s head lifted almost involuntarily, her watery gaze meeting Rio’s. Her heart stuttered at the look she found there. Rio’s expression was unguarded, full of tenderness and understanding. For a moment, Agatha forgot how to breathe.

Rio didn’t pull her hand away. When the tear Agatha had been fighting against escaped, sliding silently down her cheek, Rio’s fingers moved to her face, brushing the tear away with an intimacy that made Agatha’s chest ache.

“It’s okay.” Rio whispered, her voice impossibly soft.

A quiet laugh escaped Agatha as she glanced down again, shaking her head. “This is so pathetic, I’m sorry.”

Rio lowered her hand then, but instead of retreating, she reached for Agatha’s. Her fingers closed over Agatha’s own, warm and steady, grounding her. She gave Agatha’s hand a gentle squeeze.

“It’s not pathetic,” Rio said firmly. “And you know that, Agatha. You’re not stupid.”

Agatha’s eyes flicked back to Rio, startled by the intensity in her tone.

Rio’s grip on her hand tightened slightly, her thumb beginning to rub soothing circles over the back of Agatha’s hand. Her gaze didn’t waver as she continued, “I know what you’re doing. You’re trying to regain control because you feel like you’re losing it right now. But you don’t have to. Not with me.”

The words settled over Agatha, simultaneously disarming and terrifying.

Rio’s voice softened, her tone almost coaxing. “You don’t have to put on this facade around me if you don’t want to. You can be that badass, incredible scientist at work, but also let go of power sometimes. You need balance. You can’t be on all the time, Agatha. It’s exhausting.”

Agatha’s breath hitched, her chest tightening as she absorbed Rio’s words. She felt exposed in a way she never had before, stripped bare in front of someone who seemed to see past every defence she had so carefully built.

“And,” Rio continued, her thumb still tracing along Agatha’s hand, “you can hand over control from time to time, you know. You may even find you like it.”

The implication in her tone was unmistakable. Agatha felt her heart stutter. Her lips parted, a retort forming on her tongue, but the weight of Rio’s hand on hers and the openness in her expression stopped her. She swallowed hard, her mind racing.

“I...” Agatha started, her voice faltering.

“It’s okay,” Rio said again, softer this time, her eyes never leaving Agatha’s. “Take your time. I’m not going anywhere.”

And for the first time in a very long time, Agatha believed someone when they said those words.

Rio glanced at their intertwined hands, then back up at Agatha, her lips curling into a soft smile. “We should head back to the hotel,” she said gently, her voice breaking the quiet intimacy between them without shattering it completely. “It’s late.”

Agatha nodded, pulling her hand back carefully, the absence of Rio’s touch leaving her skin cold. Rio stood first, her movements slow, as though unwilling to disrupt the moment entirely. Agatha followed, smoothing her coat before stepping away from the bench.

The walk back to the hotel began in a comfortable silence, the kind that didn’t demand filling. The cool night air brushed against them, the soft glow of the city lights reflecting off the damp cobblestones. Agatha tucked her hands into her pockets, her thoughts swirling quietly. It was unusual to feel this calm in someone else’s presence. With Rio, there was no need to fill the quiet with meaningless chatter, and for once, Agatha appreciated the reprieve from her own overthinking.

But then, just as they passed under the arch of an old lamppost, Rio let out a soft chuckle.

Agatha turned her head, raising an eyebrow at her companion. “What?”

Rio’s lips twitched into a grin, her eyes glinting with amusement. “I was just picturing you as a master’s student here in Oxford,” she said, her voice warm with teasing. “Walking this same path home after a night out.'

Agatha snorted, shaking her head. “You're idiotic.”

“Unless…” Rio gave her a sideways glance, her grin growing. “You didn’t go out, did you? Just stayed in your room all night, pouring over textbooks and making notes?"

Agatha placed a hand on her chest in mock offense. “I’m wounded at how much of a loser you seem to think I am.” She laughed, the sound unexpectedly light in the quiet of the night.

Rio stopped too, turning to face her fully, clearly enjoying herself. “Am I wrong, though? Did you even have a social life back then, or was your idea of a wild time reorganising your planner?”

Agatha rolled her eyes, though she couldn’t help the small smile tugging at her lips. “I’ll have you know I did go out while I was here. The whole ‘wicked witch of neuro’ persona didn’t start until much later.”

“Ah, so you weren’t always terrifying,” Rio said with mock relief, walking ahead a few steps before turning to face Agatha again, her hands tucked into her jacket pockets. “Tell me, what was wild-child Agatha like? Did she have an edgy haircut? Get kicked out of pubs for yelling at people who didn’t know the difference between neuroscience and psychology?”

“Hardly,” Agatha said with a laugh, falling into step beside her. “But I might have had a rebellious phase or two. You don’t get to be the best without blowing off steam every once in a while.”

Rio raised an eyebrow. “Define ‘rebellious.’ Please tell me it involves something scandalous.”

Agatha gave her a knowing look, her lips curling in a smirk. “Wouldn’t you like to know?”

“Oh, I definitely would,” Rio shot back, grinning. “I can’t imagine you as anything but-”

“Terrifying?” Agatha cut in with a playful tilt of her head.

“Focused,” Rio corrected, though her tone was just as teasing. “Maybe a little terrifying.”

Agatha laughed again, the sound ringing out into the night, surprising even herself with how easy it felt. As they reached the corner of the street that led to their hotel, Rio bumped her shoulder lightly against Agatha’s, the contact brief but warm. “I’m starting to think I’ve underestimated you.”

“Good,” Agatha said smoothly, her smirk returning. “Keeps you on your toes.”

They lapsed into silence again, but this it was light, warm. The kind of quiet that felt like a conversation in itself. As the hotel drew closer, Agatha couldn’t help but think about how Rio had slipped into her life so seamlessly, stirring up emotions she hadn’t felt in years.

When they reached the hotel, the silence followed them into the elevator. Rio leaned casually against the wall, her hands shoved into the pockets of her leather jacket, her expression unreadable. Agatha could feel the weight of her presence, every stolen glance in the reflective walls amplified in the stillness.

By the time they made it to their floor, the tension was so thick you could cut it with a knife. Agatha walked ahead, pulling out the keycard as they reached their door. She swiped it once. The red light blinked. Twice. Red again. She shook her head as she tried a third time.

“Need a hand?” Rio asked, her voice warm and tinged with amusement.

“I’ve got it,” Agatha snapped, though her voice lacked its usual bite.

She finally got the door open and stepped inside, flicking on the light as she did. The room was just as they’d left it: two queen beds, one pristine, the other in disarray from Rio’s earlier sprawl. Agatha headed straight for her suitcase, a feeble attempt to distract herself by unpacking her toiletries.

The door shut softly behind her, followed by the unmistakable click of the lock sliding into place. Agatha stiffened. She turned, her eyes meeting Rio’s. The other woman leaned against the doorframe, her hands still tucked in her jacket pockets, her dark eyes holding an intensity that made Agatha’s stomach flip.

“What?” Agatha demanded, more defensive than she intended. “Something on your mind, Rio?” Agatha asked, her tone sharp out of habit, though the edges softened in the intimacy of the moment.

Rio tilted her head, a faint smirk tugging at the corner of her lips. She took a step forward, her movements unhurried but deliberate. “Yeah,” she said, her voice low, “You.”

Agatha’s breath caught. Rio was close now, so close that the faint scent citrus filled the air between them. She didn’t move as Rio reached up, her fingers brushing Agatha’s cheek with a gentleness that felt utterly at odds with the tension simmering in the room.

Agatha opened her mouth, the words tumbling out before she could stop them. “Rio, I shouldn’t be doing this again... I can’t...” Her voice wavered, but she held Rio’s gaze, her chest tightening with the weight of the confession.

Rio’s expression softened, her dark eyes searching Agatha’s face, but she didn’t step back. Instead, she tilted her head, her brows lifting in a calm, almost teasing challenge. “So tell me to stop.”

Agatha blinked, momentarily stunned by the simplicity of the statement, the steady resolve in her voice. Rio took a small step closer, her voice lower now, but no less firm. “Tell me to step away, and I will. Just say the word.”

Agatha opened her mouth again, but no sound came. Her heart thundered in her chest, every nerve alive with tension. This was dangerous territory, and her instinct to pull away screamed loud and insistent. Her rational mind screamed at her to push Rio away, to regain control of the moment, but her body betrayed her. She couldn’t bring herself to say it, to tell Rio to stop. Not when the air between them felt charged with something she hadn’t let herself feel in years.

So instead, she let out a shaky breath. “Don’t..” she managed to murmur. At that, Rio closed the space between them, her lips meeting Agatha’s in a kiss that was both confident and tender.

The world tilted.

Agatha froze at first, her body going rigid as her mind scrambled for purchase. But then Rio’s thumb stroked her cheek, grounding her in a way that silenced the chaos in her mind. Slowly, she melted, her hands hesitantly finding their way to Rio’s waist.

The kiss deepened, and with it, Agatha felt herself unravel. Rio’s lips were firm, her touch careful but insistent. Every thought, every defence Agatha had built over the years, crumbled in the wake of Rio’s unwavering certainty.

Rio stepped closer, her body brushing against Agatha’s in a way that sent heat spiralling through her. Rio’s gaze held Agatha’s, intense and unrelenting as she stepped into her space. Without breaking eye contact, she shrugged off her leather jacket, the motion fluid and deliberate. The soft thud of the jacket hitting the floor seemed to echo in the charged air between them. Now standing bare-armed, her movements deliberate, Rio reached out, her hands steady as they settled on Agatha’s arms. She guided her to sit on the edge of the bed with a pressure that was firm but not forceful, leaving no room for doubt.

“Rio,” Agatha started, her voice barely above a whisper, but the other woman was already leaning in. “What are you-”

Rio silenced her with a finger pressed gently against her lips, her dark eyes locking onto Agatha’s with a mix of amusement and unmistakable intensity. “Agatha,” she said softly, her tone steady but firm, “remember what I said earlier… you don’t always have to be in control.”

The words hung in the air, heavy and deliberate, as Rio let her finger trail away, brushing along Agatha’s jaw before she leaned in closer. Her breath was warm against Agatha’s ear as she whispered, her voice dropping to a low, teasing murmur.

“You might find you like handing over power... in certain situations.”

Agatha shivered at the words, her pulse racing as Rio pulled back just enough to look into her eyes, a small, knowing smirk tugging at her lips before she leaned in to kiss her again. It was intense and commanding, Rio’s lips moving against hers with a purpose that stole the air from Agatha’s lungs. The taste of her mixed with the pressure of the kiss as Rio deepened it, tilting her head to push further, leaving no space for second-guessing.

Agatha gasped softly, her hands gripping at Rio’s hips before instinctively tugging at the hem of her shirt. Rio pulled back just enough to smirk down at her, then straightened. Without a word, she grabbed the hem of her own shirt, pulling it over her head in one swift motion. The movement left her hair tousled and her toned shoulders and collarbones on full display, her confidence radiating in every motion.

“You’re staring,” Rio teased, her voice low, but the heat in her eyes betrayed her own intentions.

Agatha swallowed hard, but any retort she might have made died on her lips as Rio reached for her. With sure hands, Rio slipped her fingers under the hem of Agatha’s shirt, her knuckles brushing against warm skin as she tugged the fabric up. Agatha woke slowly, soft golden light spilling into the room and painting the walls in warm hues. She blinked groggily, her vision swimming as she tried to make sense of her surroundings. This wasn’t her bedroom.

As she shifted slightly, she felt warmth. Solid, gentle warmth, close against her side. Her heart gave a jolt as she flicked her eyes to her right. Oh shit.

Rio.

Wanda was too busy dissolving into laughter to respond immediately. Agatha groaned, rolling her eyes at her friend’s amusement. “And don’t use the word ‘crush,’” she added sternly. “That makes me sound twelve years old.”

But Wanda was already doubling over, her giggles uncontrollable. “I just… wow,” she managed between laughs. “Never in my life did I think I’d see the day. Stone-cold Agatha Harkness, of all people, catching feelings for a student !”

Agatha scoffed, pushing her chair back as she rose to her feet. She grabbed her coat and said dryly, “I’m leaving. I swear to god, Wanda.”

Wanda stood too, catching Agatha’s arm as she tried to move past. “No, no! I’m sorry!” she said through her laughter, her face alight with amusement and sincerity. “I actually think it’s really cute. I mean it.”

Agatha shook her head, exasperated but unable to keep the corner of her mouth from twitching upward. “Right. Well, I really do need to go if I want to make it to this lecture on time.”

Wanda sighed, stepping in for a quick hug. “Wait,” she said suddenly, her grip tightening slightly as a thought occurred to her. “Will the student be giving the lecture with you?”

Agatha fixed Wanda with a glare that could have frozen fire. “I’m leaving now. Goodbye,” she deadpanned, though her lips curved into a small, reluctant smile as she hugged Wanda again.

“Bye, Agatha.” Wanda replied, still grinning as she stepped back. “Don’t think this is the last you’re hearing about it!”

Agatha rolled her eyes, shook her head, and walked out the door, laughing softly under her breath as she went.
