Agatha paused outside the door of the hotel room, her hand hovering over the handle as she took a breath. Wanda’s words from earlier replayed in her mind, clear as a bell: You should go for it.

She had been contemplating it for the entire walk back. The rational side of her, the one that liked order and control, screamed at her to keep her distance. To keep things professional. But the other part of her, the part that flared whenever Rio laughed too loudly, or glanced at her with those sharp, dark eyes, wasn’t ready to let go of the possibility of more. You have to decide, Agatha. She thought to herself. You can’t keep dancing around this forever. She shook her head, clearing the fog of indecision.

“Not now,” she muttered, her voice barely audible.

She braced herself, squaring her shoulders as she finally pushed open the door. The sight that greeted her made her breath catch.

Rio stood in the center of the room, a picture of casual confidence in black tailored trousers and an open white shirt. The shirt hung loose, framing the sharp angles of her collarbone and the curve of her black lace bra. Her hair was slightly mussed, as if she’d just run her fingers through it in frustration, and her long, lean frame was caught mid-motion as she tugged on the cuffs of her shirt.

Agatha’s brain screeched to a halt. Her first instinct was to avert her eyes, to not stare, but her gaze betrayed her, tracing the lines of Rio’s torso and the casual grace of her movements. Get it together, she chastised herself, but her body didn’t listen. Rio must have felt the weight of her stare because she turned her head, a slow grin spreading across her face as their eyes met.

“Agatha?” Rio said, her tone laced with amusement as she arched a brow. “You good?”

The sound of her name jolted Agatha back into her own skin. She forced herself to meet Rio’s gaze, although her face burned. Clearing her throat, she stepped fully into the room and busied herself with unbuttoning her coat, hanging it neatly on the back of the chair by the desk.

“How long do we have?” Agatha asked, willing her voice to sound calm.

Rio glanced at her watch. “Uh, like ten minutes,” she said absently. A moment later, her eyes widened as the fact sunk in, “Shit! Ten minutes? Really?”

She turned back to the mirror in a flurry of motion, grabbing her hairbrush off the counter and hastily running it through her dark locks. Agatha leaned against the desk, watching the chaos unfold with a bemused smile tugging at her lips. Rio’s movements were quick but uncoordinated, her usual air of control dissolving as she tried to do everything at once - brush her hair, tuck in her shirt, and locate her mascara all at the same time.

“You’ve had so long to get ready,” Agatha said, a teasing lilt in her voice. “What have you even been doing this whole time?”

Rio paused, her hairbrush stopping mid-stroke. She turned her head slightly, glancing at Agatha over her shoulder.

“Preparing for the lecture,” she said, as if it were the most obvious thing in the world to be prepping for a lecture that they had very much under control. Thye had been planning it since they got the email from Calderu and all the details should have been ironed out by now. Rio continued, “I was thinking through possible questions they might ask, making sure I know how to answer them. I don’t want to get caught out and seem like a total idiot during my first lecture.”

Agatha tilted her head, studying her. There was something undeniably endearing about Rio in this moment. For all her sharp wit and seemingly effortless confidence, it was clear she cared deeply about this, and it struck a chord in Agatha.

“You couldn’t seem like an idiot if you tried,” Agatha said softly, barely louder than a whisper, the words slipping out before she could stop herself.

Rio froze. Slowly, she turned to face Agatha fully, her dark eyes narrowing slightly as a small, surprised smile tugged at the corners of her lips. “What was that?”

Agatha’s eyes widened slightly as she shook her head quickly, crossing her arms over her chest in a half-hearted attempt to deflect. “Oh, nothing,” she said, trying to sound casual.

Rio wasn’t buying it. Her smile grew wider, a mischievous glint lighting up her face. She leaned back against the chest of drawers , crossing her arms loosely as she tilted her head. “Really? Because to me, it sounded like you were complimenting me.”

Agatha scoffed, rolling her eyes in an exaggerated gesture as she straightened from the desk. “Just shut up and finish getting ready so we can leave,” she said, her voice sharper than she intended.

Rio laughed softly, turning back to the mirror but clearly pleased with herself. “Whatever you say, Sunshine.” she quipped, brushing on the last swipe of mascara with a flourish.

Agatha grabbed her bag, checking its contents as a distraction. Her heart was still racing, and her thoughts felt tangled. She glanced up briefly to see Rio straightening her shirt and adjusting the sleeves, the faintest smile still playing on her lips. Agatha shook her head to herself. Focus, she thought again. But the warmth in her chest at the sight of Rio’s quiet confidence was hard to ignore.

It was a short walk to the university, and Agatha found herself unusually quiet as they made their way down the tree-lined path. When they reached the gates of St. John’s College, nostalgia swept over her in a wave. The stone buildings and the green lawns stretched out like an echo of her youth. She couldn’t help but be drawn into memories of the countless mornings rushing to lectures, the afternoons with Wanda sprawled out under the sun, textbooks open but rarely read as they gossiped about professors and shared dreams of the future.

Agatha shook herself from her reverie as they walked through the gate, turning her attention back to Rio. But just as they crossed the threshold, Rio slowed her pace.

“Rio, what-” Agatha began, but stopped when she caught sight of Rio’s face. Her brows were raised, her eyes slightly wide, and her lips curved into a faint, disbelieving smile. Rio’s gaze was fixed straight ahead, her body unusually still.

“What’s wrong with you?” Agatha asked, trying to inject some impatience into her voice. “We’re going to be late.”

Rio didn’t answer right away. Instead, a quiet laugh slipped from her lips, soft and tinged with something Agatha couldn’t quite place. Following her gaze, Agatha turned to see what had captured Rio’s attention.

Standing near the entrance to the courtyard was a young woman with wavy brown hair that framed her face in soft, loose curls. She was scrolling through her phone, oblivious to their presence. She wore a fitted turtleneck, her jeans and boots perfectly casual yet put-together. There was something magnetic about her, the way she stood, the slight curve of her lips as she scrolled, it all spoke to an easy confidence that reminded her far too much of Rio herself.

“Who’s that?” Agatha asked, her voice coming out sharper than she intended.

Rio laughed again, this time under her breath, before finally turning to Agatha with a smirk. “That,” she said, her tone light but amused, “is Sophie. My ex.”

Agatha’s stomach dropped. She blinked, thrown off-balance, and forced herself to keep her expression neutral.

Oh.

Before she could muster a response, Sophie looked up from her phone. Her gaze scanned the courtyard, and then her face lit up with recognition.

“Rio?” she called, her voice warm and unmistakably pleased.

Rio’s posture shifted immediately, her usual confident ease softening into something looser, more genuine. “Sophie. Wow, long time no see.” she said, a smile spreading across her face.

Agatha barely had time to process the words before Sophie closed the distance between them, throwing her arms around Rio in a hug. The casual familiarity of the embrace made something twist painfully in Agatha’s chest. Her eyes flicked over the scene, taking in the way Rio’s hands rested lightly on Sophie’s back, her expression soft with fondness.

Agatha’s mouth tightened, but she stayed rooted to the spot, her fingers curling into fists at her sides. Why does this bother me so much? she thought, trying and failing to shake off the irrational emotions swelling within her.

When they pulled apart, Rio tilted her head, her smile lingering. “So,” she said, her tone light and genuinely curious, “you’re doing your PhD at Oxford, huh? Impressive.”

Sophie grinned, tucking a stray lock of hair behind her ear. “Yeah. It’s been a whirlwind, but I’m loving it.”

Agatha stood rooted to the spot, her lips pressed into a thin line. She felt like an outsider, a voyeur watching an exchange she had no business being part of.

Then Sophie turned her attention to her, her brow furrowing slightly. “And who’s this?”

Rio’s response was immediate, though her voice took on a slightly different tone, careful and deliberate. “This is my…” she paused for a second, her gaze flicking to Agatha for a second, “…my PhD supervisor, Agatha Harkness.”

The words hit Agatha like a slap. For a moment, she didn’t know why it bothered her so much, Rio was technically correct, after all, but something about the way she said it made her stomach drop. Her lips parted slightly, but no words came out as the odd weight of disappointment settled in her chest.

What did you expect her to say? Agatha thought, trying to rationalise the sudden ache. This is my supervisor slash co-researcher who I’ve hooked up with a couple times? Agatha shook the thoughts away. This was silly.

Sophie’s eyes widened slightly, a flash of recognition crossing her face. “Wait,” she said, her voice laced with awe. “ The Agatha Harkness? As in the most published woman in neuroscience?”

Agatha’s instinctive pride at the attention barely cut through the completely irrational hate she harboured for this woman. She forced a polite smile, waving a hand as if to brush off the compliment. “Oh, I don’t know about that,” she said smoothly, though her voice was tighter than usual.

Sophie laughed softly, clearly unconvinced. “No, seriously. I’ve read your papers. Your work is… incredible.”

Rio’s gaze flicked between Sophie and Agatha, her smirk returning as she caught the way Agatha’s jaw was clenched. Agatha cleared her throat, shifting her weight slightly as she fought to regain her composure. “That’s very kind of you, thank you. But we really should get going. We have a lecture to give.”

Rio glanced at her, an amused gleam in her eye, before nodding. “Right. Duty calls.”

Sophie smiled, stepping back. “Well, it was great to see you again, Rio. And, Dr Harkness, it was an honour to meet you.”

Agatha inclined her head politely, already turning away.

As they walked toward the lecture hall, Agatha felt the tension coil in her shoulders. She couldn’t stop replaying the way Rio had smiled at Sophie, the way her voice had softened, the easy familiarity between them. She told herself it didn’t matter, but the knot in her chest said otherwise.

After a moment, Rio spoke, her voice low and teasing. “What’s with the face?”

Agatha shot her a sharp look. “No face.”

Rio smirked, falling into step beside her. “You’re cute when you’re jealous, you know.”

Agatha huffed, her eyes fixed straight ahead. “I’m not jealous, don’t flatter yourself.”

Rio chuckled softly, falling into step beside her. Get a grip, Agatha told herself, her nails digging into the strap of her bag. Agatha’s mind churned, her jealousy simmering just beneath the surface. She replayed the moment over and over, the way Rio’s arms had wrapped around Sophie with that casual ease, the fondness in her eyes, the softness in her voice when she said her name. It was infuriating, irrational, and yet Agatha couldn’t deny how deeply it bothered her. The pang in her chest was more than jealousy… it was fear. Fear of what it meant that she cared this much. But as the ache persisted, as her grip on her composure grew more tenuous, a startling thought crept into her mind: Maybe I should stop fighting this.

What was the point of resisting anymore? She had spent weeks pretending that what was happening between her and Rio was nothing but a passing flirtation, something she could dismiss, compartmentalise, and eventually forget. But she couldn’t ignore the way Rio made her feel - how alive and disarmed she was in her presence, how the smallest of smiles or a teasing remark could tilt her entire world. Maybe it was time to stop running from this, to stop pretending that her feelings didn’t exist. The idea was terrifying, butit was also freeing in a way she hadn’t expected.

The lecture hall was already buzzing when Agatha and Rio entered, the hum of voices and rustling papers filling the air. Agatha scanned the room, noting the faces of eager students and seasoned academics alike, all awaiting their presentation. Despite her lingering frustration from their earlier encounter, she shook it off, forcing herself to focus. This was her domain, the stage where she thrived.

Rio followed her to the front of the room, setting her bag on the table and glancing around with a mixture of curiosity and nerves. Agatha noticed the faint shift in her posture, the way her hands flexed slightly as if to dispel tension. It was subtle, almost imperceptible, but Agatha saw it all the same.

“Ready?” Agatha murmured as she adjusted the microphone on the podium.

Rio gave her a quick smile, her eyes sparkling despite her obvious apprehension. “Born ready.”

The projector flickered to life, illuminating the screen behind them with the title slide: “Can Seizures Increase Tau Deposition , leading to Alzheimer’s disease?’ her professional mask slipping into place as she began to speak.

“Good afternoon, everyone. Thank you for joining us today. Ms Vidal and I are here to discuss our findings on the relationship between epilepsy and Alzheimer’s, with a particular focus on the role of seizures in Tau deposition.”

As Agatha launched into the presentation, her voice steady and confident, she felt herself settle into the rhythm of the lecture. She outlined the basic mechanisms of tau aggregation and its impact on neuronal function, clicking through slides filled with diagrams and graphs. The room seemed captivated, eyes fixed on her as she explained their research with her characteristic poise and authority.

Rio stood slightly to the side, hands clasped behind her back, her gaze fixed on Agatha with a mix of awe and respect. Every so often, Agatha caught a glimpse of her, noticing the way Rio's focus seemed to falter, as if she were momentarily lost in admiration rather than the lecture itself, her expression soft and captivated.

Suddenly, a hand shot up in the audience, and a sharp-looking man in the second row began to speak, “This is fascinating work, but do you have any concrete findings to support your proposed correlation between seizure activity and Tau deposition? Is it just theoretical at this stage, or do you have data?”

Agatha paused, her gaze flicking to Rio. Without a word, she tilted her head slightly and gave a small nod, a silent cue.

Rio raised her eyebrows, but stepped forward, clearing her throat. “We do, actually,” she said, her voice steady but carrying a spark of enthusiasm. “In our preliminary studies, we conducted an analysis of post-mortem brain tissue from patients with epilepsy and found a statistically significant increase in Tau levels compared to controls. In one specific subset, those with frequent seizures showed nearly double the accumulation.”

Her hands moved expressively as she spoke, pointing toward a slide that displayed their data. Her voice grew stronger, more animated, as she explained the methodology and highlighted the key findings.

Agatha turned to watch her, momentarily forgetting the audience. There was something magnetic about Rio in that moment. The way her eyes lit up when she spoke, the fervor in her tone as she described their work with such clarity and conviction. Agatha felt herself drawn in, mesmerised by the sheer passion that radiated from her. Rio’s intelligence shone like a beacon, and it wasn’t just the words she said, it was the way she carried herself, the confidence in her movements, the way her lips quirked slightly when she hit a point she was particularly proud of. Agatha barely noticed the approving nods from the audience or the way a few people scribbled notes furiously.

Rio finished her explanation, glancing briefly at Agatha as if seeking reassurance. Agatha snapped out of her reverie, nodding once, her lips curving into the faintest smile. “Well explained,” Agatha whispered to her before turning back to the audience. “I think that answers the question.”

The discussion continued, but Agatha couldn’t fully focus anymore. Rio had stolen her attention completely, and for the first time, she wasn’t sure she wanted to take it back.

After answering a few more questions, the lecture finally came to a close. To Agatha’s quiet amusement, Rio had taken the lead during the Q&A session, fielding most of the questions with remarkable ease. Each time someone tried to challenge her, she had countered with confidence and precision, leaving no room for doubt. Agatha couldn’t quite place the swell of emotions building inside her as they walked out of the lecture hall. It wasn’t just relief or admiration, it was something more. Pride, perhaps.

She glanced at Rio as they stepped into the crisp afternoon air, her lips curving into a genuine smile. They crossed the street to the small café nestled between two old stone buildings, the scent of freshly brewed coffee wafting through the air as they stepped inside. After ordering, they settled into a corner table with two steaming cups of coffee, the bustling noise of the café creating a cozy background hum.

Agatha smiled as she sat down, “You did good, Rio. Well done.”

Rio turned to her, her face lighting up with a grin. “Well, all that practice I did paid off, I guess.”

Agatha laughed softly, shaking her head. “You know, you can be very mature and impressive when you’re not actively arguing with everything I say.”

Rio smirked as she picked up her cup. “Thank you… I think? I can’t tell if that’s a compliment or an insult.”

Agatha chuckled, taking a sip of her coffee. “Bit of both, maybe.”

Rio leaned back in her chair with a dramatic sigh. “But oh my god, that one question from that guy? What even was that? ‘If seizure activity makes up part of the aetiology of Alzheimers, does that mean you could cure Alzheimer’s by just slowing seizures?’ I mean, does the guy know the definition of a risk factor? Like, what am I even supposed to say to that…”

Agatha laughed, nearly choking on her drink. “Oh, Rio. That’s something you’re going to have to get used to in this field. Men in science have an unbelievable knack for disguising absurdity as expertise. They have these insane superiority complexes, and when they realize a woman knows more than they do, it’s like their brains short-circuit. So they just… blurt out the first idiotic question that comes to mind. And of course, they try to couch it in semi-sophisticated wording to maintain the illusion of competence. Most of the time it boils down to absolute idiocy”

Rio laughed, shaking her head. “So basically, science is like a giant masquerade ball of fragile male egos?”

Agatha smirked. “Absolutely. But you handled it very well.”

Rio’s laughter softened, her expression shifting into something gentler. She looked down at her cup for a moment, then back up at Agatha, her smile more genuine now. “Thank you,” she said, her voice quieter but no less sincere.

Agatha’s chest tightened, caught off guard by the warmth in Rio’s gaze. She looked away, focusing on her coffee, but she couldn’t stop the corners of her mouth from lifting in response. “You’re welcome,” she said softly.

Rio took a sip of her coffee, then leaned forward, resting her chin on her hand as she gave Agatha a playful smile. “You know,” she said, her voice light but tinged with something deeper, “you’re surprisingly generous with the compliments today. Is this, like, a once-in-a-lifetime thing? Should I be taking pictures to remember this moment?”

Agatha raised an eyebrow, her lips curving into a smirk. “Don’t push your luck, Rio.”

“Oh, come on,” Rio said, her grin widening. “Admit it. You were proud of me back there. I saw the way you were looking at me during the Q&A.”

Agatha took another sip of her coffee to hide the flush creeping up her neck. “I was observing.”

“Right.” Rio leaned back, crossing her arms with a mock-serious expression. “You were observing with the intensity of someone admiring a fine piece of art. Totally professional.”

Agatha sighed dramatically, but the smile tugging at her lips betrayed her. “You’re insufferable.”

“Yeah,” Rio said, her voice softening as her eyes searched Agatha’s. “But you like me anyway.”

For a moment, the teasing tone between them shifted into something quieter, more intimate. Agatha felt her chest tighten as she met Rio’s gaze, unable to look away. There was a warmth in Rio’s expression that made it impossible to deny the truth anymore, she did like her. More than liked her.

Agatha placed her cup down carefully, her fingers lingering on the edge as she spoke. “You’re... difficult to ignore,” she admitted, her voice lower than usual.

Rio tilted her head, her smile softening. “I’m very okay with you not ignoring me.” Rio leaned forward again, her hand brushing lightly against Agatha’s on the table. The touch was fleeting but enough to send a spark of warmth through Agatha’s chest. “You know, that sounded dangerously close to a confession.”

Agatha’s breath hitched slightly at the sincerity in Rio’s voice. She glanced down at their hands, her fingers twitching as if tempted to close the distance. “Rio-” she began, unsure of what she was even going to say.

Rio leaned closer, her voice soft but teasing. “You don’t have to say anything. Just keep looking at me like that, and I’ll figure it out.”

Agatha laughed despite herself, shaking her head as she finally reached for her coffee again. “You’re impossible.”

Rio’s grin turned softer as she rested her chin on her hand again. “Yeah, but you’re stuck with me.”

Agatha didn’t reply, but her heart felt lighter somehow. Maybe, she thought, being stuck with Rio wasn’t such a bad thing after all. In that moment, Agatha felt a quiet pull, an almost overwhelming urge to surrender to the feelings that had been stirring inside her since Rio had walked into her lab weeks ago. She glanced across at Rio’s dark eyes, still glowing from the exhilaration of their successful lecture, her lips curling into a soft smile as her hair fell around her face, catching the sunlight just enough to give her an almost ethereal glow. Maybe this feeling, this connection, was where she was meant to be. Maybe it was time to stop fighting the inevitable.

But just as the thought settled in her mind, Rio spoke again.

“Oh yeah, by the way…” she said with a chuckle, shaking her head as if still amused by the memory. “The funniest thing happened right before the lecture. Um-”

Agatha raised an eyebrow, urging her to go on.

Rio’s smile faltered slightly as her eyes locked with Agatha’s. “After we bumped into Sophie, she texted me. She asked if I wanted to go out for dinner with her tonight.”

Agatha’s stomach dropped. Her mind raced for a second, a sharp sting of jealousy cutting through her thoughts. She kept her gaze steady, but her heart pounded wildly beneath her calm exterior.

She searched Rio’s intense expression, her breath catching as their eyes held each other. “What, like a date?” Agatha asked, her voice lighter than she intended, almost teasing.

Rio nodded slowly, her gaze unwavering, searching Agatha’s face as she tried to read her reaction. “Yeah, like a date.”

Agatha’s breath hitched as her heart sank. For a moment, the world felt like it shifted beneath her. Her pulse throbbed in her ears, and all she could think was that she didn’t want Rio to go. But then, without thinking, her mouth opened and words blurted out before she had the chance to stop them.

“Well, you should go.”

The admission hung in the air between them, Agatha’s mind spinning, unsure of what had just come out. Her voice sounded far away, distant from her own thoughts.

Rio stared back at her in disbelief, her eyebrows rising as the surprise and hurt flickered across her face for a fleeting moment. But just as quickly, irritation replaced those emotions, her jaw tightening and a sharp scoff escaping her lips. “I should go, really? That’s what you think?”

Agatha couldn’t speak for a second. Her mind was a whirlwind of thoughts; confusion, regret, and something deeper she couldn’t quite place. The weight of her words hit her like a heavy wave, and she felt the sting settle deep in her chest. She wasn’t sure what had compelled her to say that, but there was no going back now. She couldn’t take it back, and the silence stretched out between them. Still, there was no choice but to double down.

Finally, she managed to speak, her voice steady despite the turmoil inside her. “Yeah, you should go. She seems nice, and you two obviously had a connection.”

Rio shook her head, a scoff escaping her lips as her eyes rolled in frustration. Agatha had never seen her like this. So serious, so annoyed, she looked downright infuriated. “Fine, Agatha. I will. I’ll go.”

Agatha stared back at her, her own annoyance bubbling to the surface. The words had come out so easily, and now she regretted them more than she cared to admit. Yet her stubbornness held her firm. “Yeah, fine. Go.”

Rio leaned forward again, her tone dropping to something softer, more biting. “Oh, I will.” She paused, leaning forwards and letting the silence settle before adding, “Unless, Agatha, you can think of any reason why I shouldn’t ?”

Agatha bristled, leaning toward her in return, their elbows now resting on the table between them. Her heart pounded in her chest, her breath coming faster as her mind raced. Why had she said that? Why did it feel like she was watching something slip away? Every instinct told her to list a million reasons she shouldn’t go, to tell her everything she felt, to lean forward and kiss her right here. But her pride wouldn’t let her. “Nope, nothing comes to mind.”

The tension hung thick in the air as they stared each other down, neither willing to back down. Agatha’s fingers tapped anxiously against the table, her mind screaming for a different response, but she couldn’t find the words. Finally, she broke the silence, her voice steady but sharp. “I have some things I need to do this afternoon. I’ll see you back at the hotel.”

Without another word, she rose from her seat, her heels clicking softly against the café floor as she walked toward the door. Once outside, the cool air hit her, but she couldn’t shake the feeling of her hands trembling slightly. She clenched them into fists, taking a deep breath as she walked down the street, her thoughts a chaotic mess of confusion, jealousy, and something more she didn’t quite understand yet.

Chapter Notes

hihi finally im updating omg sorry for the wait!!! <333

Agatha walked aimlessly through a park she had found after wandering down the street for god knows how long. Her boots scuffing against the gravel as the late afternoon sun spilled through the bare trees, but the beauty of it all barely registered. Her mind was a tangled mess, replaying the conversation with Rio on an endless loop.

Why had she told her to go? She didn’t even mean it, of course she didn’t want Rio to go on that date. But when it came time to say it, to let her real feelings slip past her defences, she just couldn’t. And, if she was admitting it, she had been a little annoyed that Rio even brought up the date in the first place. She knew it was unfair of her, after all, Agatha had made a right mess of both of their feelings this morning. But still, she hadn’t expected Rio to go out with someone else. So, she had brushed aside whatever affection she felt for Rio, instead, she had pushed her away.

“Oh, God,” she muttered under her breath, running a hand through her hair.

She quickened her pace, as if walking faster might help her escape the spiralling thoughts. Rio had said she was going. Was she really going? Agatha’s steps faltered as the possibility settled over her. Agatha couldn’t ignore the memory of Rio’s face back in the cafe. The way her shoulders had straightened, the determined glint in her eyes. That hadn’t looked like a bluff.

The thought made Agatha’s chest tighten painfully. Her mind started spiralling again, conjuring images she didn’t want to see: Rio sitting across from Sophie, laughing, smiling, maybe even reaching out to touch her hand. Agatha’s stomach churned at the idea, and she stopped walking, pressing a hand against her middle as if that might ease the sudden nausea.

No. Agatha straightened her shoulders, laughing quietly to herself as she rolled her eyes. There was no way Rio was actually going to go. This was stupid. She absolutely wouldn’t. Rio was fiery, stubborn. She knew how to throw a barb when she wanted to. This was just her way of lashing out.

The air had turned crisp, and the colours in the sky melted into a painterly display of gold, orange, and violet. Despite herself, Agatha found the scene calming, even as her thoughts swirled. The sound of the city hummed in her ears as Agatha strode toward the hotel, a smirk tugging at the corner of her lips. Of course, Rio wasn’t actually going on this “date.” She could imagine it now. Rio sprawled across the bed, casually flipping through a magazine or scrolling on her phone, waiting to tease Agatha about how jealous she’d looked earlier. That’s what this was all about, wasn’t it? Rio was trying to get under her skin, to see if she could needle out a reaction.

Agatha wouldn’t give her the satisfaction. She chuckled under her breath, shaking her head as the lift began to rise.

The hotel’s dim, warm lighting gave the hallway a cozy glow, and her steps slowed as she approached her room. She slid the keycard into the slot, hearing the beep and click of the lock disengaging.

“Rio…” she began, smirking as she pushed the door open. But the words died on her lips.

A sleek black long-sleeve that clung perfectly to her figure and tailored dark green trousers that emphasised her graceful posture. Her hair was swept back into a bun, accentuating the sharp angles of her face. She wore smoky eyeshadow and was currently applying mascara.

For a moment, Agatha just stared, caught completely off guard. But then she recovered, telling herself that this only confirmed what she’d thought all along. Rio wasn’t really going on a date. She was just taking this ruse to the next level, all to rile Agatha up.

“Hi,” Rio said curtly, glancing at Agatha through the mirror before turning back to finish her makeup.

Agatha blinked, then smirked as she dropped her bag onto the floor and strolled further into the room. “What are you doing?” she asked, her tone laced with feigned casualness.

Rio didn’t even look at her this time. “I’m getting ready for my date, Agatha,” she said, her voice clipped but deliberate.

Agatha chuckled softly and rolled her eyes. She flopped onto her bed, grabbing her book from the bedside table and flipping it open to a random page as she muttered, “Oh, sure. Your ‘date.’ ”

She pretended to read, but her attention drifted almost immediately. Her gaze kept flicking up over the top of the book, stealing glances at Rio as she applied eyeliner. Agatha told herself it was just curiosity. Rio was going all out, after all, and it was kind of impressive how far she was willing to take this joke.

Still, the sight of Rio in that outfit, moving with such calm confidence, was… distracting. Agatha adjusted her position on the bed, trying to act like she wasn’t paying attention. She wasn’t falling for it, though. Not a chance.

Rio, apparently noticing the glances, caught her eye through the mirror, her expression cool and unreadable. Agatha quickly dropped her gaze back to the book, biting the inside of her cheek to stifle a reaction. Let her think she’s winning this round, she thought. She’s the one putting on a whole production to get a rise out of me.

But as Rio turned back to her reflection and picked up her lipstick, Agatha couldn’t help but steal another glance. She’d never admit it out loud, but Rio was infuriatingly good at this game.

Agatha watched as Rio slipped a phone and what looked like a small wallet into her pocket, then grabbed her shoes from the corner of the room. Her movements were deliberate, efficient. It was like a punch to the gut when she realised Rio wasn’t just pretending anymore. She was really leaving.

“Hold on,” Agatha said, her voice sharp with disbelief. “Rio, you’re not actually going, are you?”

Rio stopped mid-step at the foot of Agatha’s bed, turning to face her with an expression of pure exasperation. “Yes, Agatha,” she said, her voice steady but pointed. “Yes, I am. I’ve told you twice already, I’m going.”

Agatha scoffed, the sound hollow and forced. “I get the point, okay? This isn’t funny, Rio. Just stop.”

Rio’s eyes darkened, a storm brewing beneath her calm exterior. “Good thing I’m not trying to be funny, then.” she said, her tone biting. “I’m going.”

It was only then that the truth hit Agatha with the force of a wave, leaving her scrambling for air. Her heart stuttered painfully, panic setting in. She’s really going. She’s actually going on this date. Agatha’s mind raced.

“But I-” Agatha stammered, her voice rising in pitch. “You can’t. What? But we-”

“We what, Agatha?” Rio snapped, cutting her off. She stepped closer, her arms crossed tightly over her chest, her stance unyielding. “Please, go on. Because I’d love to hear what you have to say.”

Agatha rose to her feet, her expression a mix of desperation and frustration. “That isn’t fair, Rio,” she said, her voice shaking. She was floundering, and she knew it, but she pressed on. “You know it’s my career that’s at stake if anything happens between us. Both of our careers. I’m scared, okay? But you said you’d wait. You- you said, ‘take your time.’ I thought you fucking meant that.”

Rio’s jaw clenched, and her eyes narrowed, her anger simmering just below the surface. Her tone, though quieter, was laced with frustration as she snapped, “I know that I said take your time, its just-”

“So why are you going on this date?” Agatha interjected, her voice rising. “I thought you’d let me work my feelings out.”

The words came out in a rush, sharp and wounded, but they seemed to strike a deeper nerve in Rio. Her face twisted into something furious and raw, and before Agatha could blink, Rio’s voice broke through like a crack of thunder.

“BECAUSE I CAN’T FUCKING TAKE IT ANYMORE, AGATHA!”

The shout rang out, loud and unrestrained, leaving both women stunned in its wake. Rio inhaled sharply, pressing her hand to her face as a tear slipped free. She exhaled slowly, visibly pulling herself together before speaking again, her voice softer but no less resolute.

“Look,” Rio said, her tone trembling now, “I’m sorry. I really am. I understand the position you’re in, and I know I said ‘take your time,’ but I just can’t fucking do it anymore.” She swallowed hard, her voice catching as her hands dropped limply to her sides.

“Rio-” Agatha started, but she was cut off again.

“No. Let me finish,” Rio said firmly. She looked at Agatha, her eyes bright with unshed tears and a kind of exhaustion that seemed bone-deep. “Look, anyone can fucking see that there’s something here. You’re not blind, Agatha. But you just keep going back to the same fucking denial bullshit over and over again. At first, I laughed at it. I thought it would be a fun challenge, see if I could break through your façade, but-”

She faltered, her voice cracking. Rio’s hands shook slightly as she gestured between them, and she laughed bitterly through her tears. “It’s breaking me, Agatha. I can’t take it anymore. Either you want to be with me, or you don’t. You don’t get to have me whenever you want and then pretend it didn’t happen the next morning.”

Agatha’s heart clenched, her throat tightening painfully as she struggled to find words, any words, that could stop the spiralling devastation before her.

Rio held up a hand, silencing her once more. “So here’s how it’s going to be,” she said, her voice hoarse but steady. “Either you’re just my supervisor, I go on this date tonight, and tomorrow we go back to working on research and nothing more, or…”

Her voice softened, trembling under the weight of her words. “Or you admit that none of this has been an accident. That this is something more. And you tell me that you want it to happen.”

Chapter Notes

small cw/ death of a child + grief + some very unhealthy views on grief/mourning

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Agatha had been at work when the call came.

The call that would change her life. A moment etched so deeply into her mind that even though it had been years, she still replayed it every time she closed her eyes. Even now, she could recall it as vividly as if it had happened yesterday. The memory itself was enough to leave her stomach clenching, as though someone had reached inside her and twisted her abdominal organs until she was hollow. And that was just the memory, living through it had been so much worse.

‘You’d better come up to the ward. It’s Nicky.’

That was what Nurse Sarah had said. Sarah was kind, compassionate, a steady presence throughout the six years since Nicky’s diagnosis. Tay-Sachs disease, the condition destroyed Nicky’s nervous system bit by bit, until his body could no longer sustain him. The doctors had initially given him a year to live and somehow Nicky had defied those odds, but Agatha always knew this day would come.

The bloody irony of it all was not lost on Agatha, the top neuroscientist in her field, forced to watch her son’s brain wither away in front of her, with nothing she could fucking do. It gnawed at her constantly, a bitter reminder that all her knowledge and research, everything she had worked for, could be rendered useless by fate.

She didn’t remember whether she had even hung up the phone, it had all been all a blur as she bolted from her office. The lab building stood just across the road from the university hospital where Nicky was being cared for, but the journey across the street had felt like miles. Her mind had been mess, she hadn’t been sure where she was or which way was up or down, or why her damn legs couldn’t carry her any fucking faster!

She had never been religious, not since she realised she didn’t have to conform to the senseless dogma her mother had preached throughout her childhood. By the time she left home, she wanted nothing to do with religion - or religious people, for that matter. Agatha understood not everyone was a homophobic, hateful zealot like the ones she had grown up around, but the mere mention of God was wrapped in layers of pain she couldn’t untangle. Besides, she doubted science and religion could truly coexist; to her, they seemed fundamentally at odds.

But as she sprinted across the road, dodging cars and ignoring the blaring horns of buses, she had prayed. For the first time since she was eleven years old in her room asking god to make her ‘normal’, Agatha Harkness prayed. Begged was a better word really. She begged, to God, to Jesus, to Allah, to Buddha, to any deity or force that might be listening - even Death itself. She begged, over and over:

Do not take him before I get there. Please, don’t let him go yet. Just please, let me see him. I need to see him. I need to see him… I need to see my son.

She had pushed through the hospital doors, her breath coming in gasps, her chest tight with fear. The hallways had blurred as she ran, her feet stumbling on the sterile tiles, her hands brushing the walls for balance. When she had finally reached the paediatric neurology ward, the nurses and doctors she had come to know over the years stood there, their faces etched with sorrow.

“Nicky, what’s- is he-” she had choked out, barely able to form the words.

“No, not yet.” Nurse Sarah said gently but firmly, placing a hand on Agatha’s shoulder. “No, he’s hanging on for now. He’s a strong boy, that one. But…” She hesitated, her voice softening. “I’m sorry, Agatha. I don’t think he has long. A few hours at most.”

She leaned heavily against the larger woman, clutching her for support as a choked sob had torn from her throat. She stayed there, rooted in place, for what felt like an eternity but was likely only a minute. The sobs came in relentless waves, one after another, they had seemed to surround her. Was Nurse Sarah crying too? Agatha couldn’t tell. She could barely register her own voice in that moment; it had felt as though she had left her body, hovering above and watching herself unravel.

At last, Nurse Sarah, her eyes shimmering, had met Agatha’s gaze with a look that was both compassionate and firm before she finally spoke

“This is the most horrific thing a mother can experience.” Sarah said finally, “I’m so sorry, Agatha. But you need to be strong for him. He can’t see you like this. Go in there and give him joy… love.”

And that was just what Agatha had done. She had sat beside him, taking his fragile hand in hers, and had read to him, letting him choose his favorite books. Hours passed as she filled the room with stories, her voice unwavering even as her heart broke. She wanted these moments to be filled with happiness.

Eventually, Nicky looked up at her, his voice weak but full of joy and innocence.

“Mmmm-mumma,” he had whispered, his speech slurred from the disease, but he pushed through. “I… I’m tir… tired.”

And in that moment, Agatha’s heart had swelled with such an overwhelming rush of love and adoration. In an instant, her sadness and panic seemed to dissolve, leaving only the fierce need to make her son feel as comfortable and loved as possible.

“That’s okay, my lovely,” she whispered back, gently ruffling his hair as she pulled his blankets snug. A single tear traced down her cheek as her voice wavered, breaking with emotion. “You go to sleep, my sweet boy. Just relax, and Mumma will be right here next to you. Where I always am, Nicky. My sweet, sweet Nicky.”

Nicky’s weak hand gripped hers feebly, and he managed to give her a small, fragile smile.

“I llo- I… I love you, Mmmm- Mumma,” he struggled out.

Agatha leaned down, hugging him as gently as she could manage. Her instinct was to hold him as tight as she could and never let go, but she didn’t want to hurt him. She tucked his hair behind his ears and a tear streamed down her face as she bent to press a gentle kiss to his forehead.

“I love you, Nicky. Mumma loves you so much. Now rest, my sweet boy.”

And with that, he was gone.

— — —

Agatha thought back to that memory more often than she cared to admit. She knew it wasn’t healthy, usually surfacing when something good was finally happening in her life. Her mind would dig up the deepest shame she had ever faced and pull her right back down. Not that she fought it much. She wasn’t exactly dragged kicking and screaming into misery. No, she had welcomed the sadness. Honestly, she thought she deserved it.

And that was the thought that echoed relentlessly in her mind as she now stood across from Rio, still reeling from the weight of the younger woman’s confession.

She was right. Trying to distance herself from Rio had to stop. Agatha realised, in that moment, how deeply she had been clinging to her misery, how she had closed herself off when Nicky died. She had withdrawn from Wanda and Vision, pretending their friendship didn’t exist. She scared off acquaintances at work, becoming the wicked witch of the lab , convinced it was better to be feared than pitied. After all, she didn’t feel like she deserved comfort. She hadn’t even tried at romance… well, not until Rio.

People had been interested, of course, but she pushed them away as much as possible. It sounded silly now, but to her it had felt… selfish. After experiencing such a profound loss, she had convinced herself that she shouldn’t be able to feel positive emotions anymore. Love, attraction, it all seemed too far out of reach. She had assumed that part of her had died with Nicky.

But Rio had been different. Being around her, letting herself grow closer, had felt like coming up for air after nearly drowning. It was like she was beginning to piece together the broken pieces of herself, parts she thought would remain shattered forever.

But that had scared Agatha. It felt wrong. Like she was erasing the grief, covering it with the happiness she wasn’t sure she deserved. She was scared that allowing herself to feel love again meant she was downplaying Nicky’s death in some way.

But now, standing there, on the brink of losing Rio, she knew she couldn’t keep doing this. Mourning for the rest of her life, stuck in memories, wasn’t honouring Nicky at all. Her sweet, sweet boy, so strong, never letting anyone tell him what he couldn’t do. Agatha would do the same. She wouldn’t let her mind tell her that she could never feel happy again. She wouldn’t let herself waste away, trapped in the past. She would let love in. Let Rio in.

Agatha took a decisive step forward, her breath catching in her throat as her heart pounded in her chest. Every beat felt like a thousand miles a minute, a whirlwind of emotions rushing through her. With a slow, deliberate movement, she pressed her lips to Rio’s.

At first, Rio froze, caught off guard by the sudden intimacy. She didn’t pull away, but neither did she react right away. Agatha pulled back slightly, her eyes meeting Rio’s dark ones, searching for something, anything.

“I’m sorry,” she began, her voice trembling slightly. She gazed into Rio’s eyes, hoping her sincerity could be conveyed through the look in her eyes. She knew sorry wasn’t enough, could never be enough, but she desperately needed Rio to understand how deeply she cared.

“I’ve not been fair to you,” she continued, her voice growing softer, almost reverent. “I want to make it up to you. Stop repressing my-”

Before she could finish, Rio leaned down again, her lips finding Agatha’s in a slow, tender kiss. The touch was soft, gentle. Unhurried but full of emotion. Agatha let herself sink into it, her eyes closing as her mind finally settled.

There were no words needed. The warmth of Rio’s lips against hers was enough. It was everything.

When they finally pulled away, their breaths mingling, Agatha couldn’t help but smile softly. She rested her forehead against Rio’s, a feeling of peace washing over her. In that moment, nothing else mattered. Just Rio, just them.

“So, you’ll admit it now?” Rio teased, her smirk growing wider. “Not an accident. Not a ‘lapse of judgment’ or any of that crap? These are real feelings?”

Agatha smiled softly, her fingers gently brushing a stray strand of Rio’s dark hair from her face. “Yes, the real thing, I promise,” she whispered. “I’ll stop denying that it's an actual relationship.”

Rio raised an eyebrow, that familiar smirk slowly spreading across her face. Agatha’s heart fluttered at the sight of it, a small laugh escaping her lips. She had missed that smirk more than she cared to admit in the last hour.

“Relationship?” Rio teased, her voice low and playful. “At least take me on a date first! I mean, after all I didn’t get to go on my date tonight, I feel like I deserve some kind of compensation.”

Agatha laughed softly, moving her hands to the back of Rio’s neck as her gaze deepened. She met Rio’s playful expression with a raised eyebrow, a smirk of her own slowly forming. “Hmm… tomorrow. Tomorrow we’ll go out. For tonight, I can think of a better kind of compensation.”

Before Rio could respond, Agatha closed the distance between them, capturing her lips in a slow, deliberate kiss. This time, Rio didn’t hold back. She met Agatha’s lips with equal fervor, her hands trailing lightly down Agatha’s arms, pulling her closer.

The kiss deepened, warmth and desire flooding the moment. Rio gently pushed Agatha back against the wall, her hands sliding down to rest against the curve of her waist. The intensity of their kiss returned, deeper and more fluid this time, as if they were lost in the rhythm of one another. Agatha wrapped her arms around Rio’s neck, holding her close as their bodies pressed together, the heat between them palpable.

The world seemed to shrink again, leaving just the two of them, a quiet sanctuary in the middle of everything. Rio’s hands moved slowly, exploring the soft fabric against Agatha’s skin, tracing delicate patterns with her fingertips. Agatha let out a soft sigh into the kiss, her breath mingling with Rio’s as they both surrendered to the moment.

They paused briefly, breathless and smiling, their foreheads resting against one another once again. Agatha’s voice was a soft whisper against Rio’s lips. “You sure know how to make up for lost time,” she murmured, her voice husky with emotion.

Rio smiled, her fingers trailing lightly along Agatha’s jawline. “I aim to please,” she whispered, her voice barely audible.

This time, their kiss deepened again, slower and more tender, as if savouring every second. The touch of Rio’s lips was soothing, grounding, a reminder that in this moment, everything was exactly as it should be.
